The Usul Rule on Omitting Part of a Hadith
Scholars discuss the permissibility of narrating only part of a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on omitting part of a hadith in transmission and apply it to evaluate whether a partial narration is permissible based on the independence of the omitted part.

Core Idea
Omitting part of a hadith is permissible if the omitted part is independent and does not contradict what is narrated.

Hadith transmission is the backbone of Sunnah; but what if a narrator only reports part of a long hadith? This lesson explores the Hanafi position that such partial narration is allowed when the omitted portion is not essential for the meaning. We will examine the evidence from independent hadith clauses and the practice of early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Read the passage to extract the core Hanafi rule: narrating part of a hadith is permissible if there is no contradiction between the omitted and narrated parts.
The rule is conditional on the independence of the omitted portion.
2
Examine the evidence
Analyze the hadith examples cited, such as 'Muslims' blood is equal', and understand why each clause is considered independent.
Independence means the narrated part conveys a complete ruling without requiring the omitted part.
3
Understand the condition
The key condition is that the omitted part must not contradict the meaning of what is narrated. If it does, the narration becomes problematic.
Contradiction would occur if, e.g., an exception in the omitted part reverses the rule in the narrated part.
4
Compare opposing views
Identify the two opposing positions: (1) never permissible, (2) permissible only if the full hadith was narrated once before.
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi flexibility versus stricter schools.
5
Recognize the practical impact
Understand that this rule allows Hanafi jurists to derive rulings from partial narrations widely cited in hadith collections, without needing the full context each time.
This facilitates istinbat from ahad hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: حذف البعض من الخبر (ورواية البعض منه (جائز إن لم يكن بينهما) أي بين ما حذف، مناقضاً، طعاماً ما روي (تباغض) يعني اختلاف بحيث لو لم يذكر لاستفاد مما ذكر حكماً وبين ، أي منافياً له ( كالمغيرات من الاستثناء وغيره نحو : لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب والورق بالورق، إلا وزناً بوزن مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء رواه مسلم. ونحو من ابتاع فلا يبعه حتى يستوفيه رواه الشيخان ونحو الصلاة إلى الصلاة كفارة ما بينهما ما أجتنبت الكبائر» رواه في السنن (كقوله) صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه المسلمون تتكافأ دماؤهم») أي تتساوى في الحرمة والقصاص ولذا قلنا: يقتل الحر بالعبد ويسعى بذمتهم أدناهم كالعبد المأذون مثلاً، ولذا يثبت الأمان إذا أمن واحد من المسلمين (ويرد) الغنائم (عليهم أقصاهم) أبعدهم ولا ينفرد بنفسه بالأخذ وهم يد على من سواهم كالعضو الواحد في اتحاد كلمتهم وحرمة دمائهم وأموالهم، رواه أبو داود ففي هذا الحديث كل جملة منه مستقلة لا تغير واحدة الأخرى : أصلاً (وقيل : (لا يصح الحذف أصلاً (وقيل) يجوز إن روي مرة على التمام، وإلا) أي وإن لم يرو مرة من المرات فيروى إلى الكمال لنا إذا عدم التعلق بين الجملتين (فكخبرين) مستقلين، فلا يتوقف نقل واحد على الأخر (و) أيضاً (شاع) رواية البعض وحذف البعض من الأئمة المعتبرين (بالاستقراء) فهذا بدل على الإجماع فافهم.
Issue: Omitting part of a report (and narrating part of it) is permissible if there is no contradiction between what is omitted and what is mentioned... like exceptions, e.g., 'Do not sell gold for gold except weight for weight equal for equal' reported by Muslim. And the hadith 'Muslims' blood is equal'... each sentence is independent. Some say omission is never permissible; some say it is permissible if the full hadith was narrated once before. The author argues that widespread practice indicates consensus.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on narrating only part of a hadith. The author states it is permissible if the omitted part does not contradict the part mentioned, using examples like exceptions or independent clauses. The hadith about the equality of Muslim blood shows that each sentence stands alone, so omitting one does not affect the meaning. There are differing opinions: some forbid it entirely, while others allow it only if the full hadith was previously transmitted. However, the author supports the Hanafi position that it is generally permissible, citing the widespread practice of respected scholars, which indicates consensus.

Key Terms
حذف البعض (hadhf al-ba'd): Omitting a portion of a hadith when narrating it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is omitting part of a hadith permissible according to the Hanafi position in this passage?
A) Only if the narrator is a companion
B) If the omitted part does not contradict the mentioned part
C) Only if the full hadith is never narrated
D) It is never permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows partial narration of hadiths as long as the omitted portion does not contradict the narrated part and retains independence of meaning.

Ruling When Original Narrator Accuses Transmitter of Lying
Scholars determine that the hadith is dropped if the original narrator declares the transmitter a liar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that certainty is not overridden by doubt to evaluate the probity of narrators when one accuses the other of lying.

Core Idea
When an original narrator accuses a transmitter of lying, that specific hadith falls, but both remain trustworthy for other narrations.

This lesson examines a key usul al-fiqh principle: certainty is not removed by doubt. The passage discusses the scenario where the original narrator (asl) declares the transmitter (far') a liar. Although the hadith is unanimously rejected, the narrators' probity remains for other reports. We will analyze the reasoning and the subtle intra-Hanafi debate about whether the doubt affects them individually or collectively.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify that the hadith is dropped (sāqit) by consensus when the original narrator accuses the transmitter of lying in that specific narration.
The ruling applies only to the hadith in which the accusation occurs.
2
Identify the rationale
The hadith is dropped because the required truthfulness (ṣidq) is absent for both narrator and transmitter in that report. A connected chain (ittiṣāl) requires truthfulness of both.
The proof is rational: if one is lying, the report cannot be sound.
3
Analyze the objection and response
An objector says both could be truthful if the original forgot. The response: the accusation that the transmitter lied is incompatible with the original's truthfulness, and forgetting is unlikely to the point of certainty. The accusation creates strong doubt, and no authority remains after such doubt.
The response distinguishes between possible forgetfulness and a definite accusation.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi debate
The author debates whether the doubt removes probity individually or collectively. Some argue that since one is definitely lying but unknown which, both become suspect. The author concludes that probity remains for each individually because certainty is not removed by doubt.
This debate affects how we treat other narrations from the same narrators.
5
Apply the principle
Apply the usul principle 'al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt). The narrators were known to be trustworthy; mere doubt does not revoke that status. Therefore, they remain acceptable for other hadiths.
This principle is widely used in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: إذا كذب الأصل) الراوي (الفرع) في روايته عنه (سقط) هذا (الحديث) المروي اتفاقاً، لانتفاء صدقهما معاً فيه أي في هذا الحديث ولا بد في الاتصال من صدقهما) وبفوات الاتصال تفوت الحجية، فإن قلت انتفاء صدقهما ممنوع، بل يجوز أن يكونا صادقين، لكن نسي الأصل، بل هو الظاهر فإن نسيان ما سمع غير نادر جداً، بخلاف ظن سماع ما لم يسمع، فإنه بعيد جداً، قلت الأصل يدعي كذب الفرع، ولا شك أن هذا لا يجامع صدقه، ونسيان ما سمع وإن كان غير نادر لكن تيقن أنه ما لمسموعه بعيد جداً، سمع فقد أورث هذا التكذيب ريبة قوية ولا حجية بعد هذه الريبة (وهما على عدالتهما كما كانا من قبل (فيقبل روايتهما في حديث آخر وذلك لأن اليقين لا يزول بالشك بل يعمل به وعدالة كل منهما كانت ثابتة، والآن قد وقع الشك في كل واحد بعينه فلا يزول به (أقول) إنما يتم هذا لو كفى بعد التهما بدلاً لا معاً) أن فسق واحد لا بعينه متيقن فتزول به عدالة كل معاً، وإنما يعني الشك في تعيين الفاسق منهما، فلا يزول به تيقن عدالة كل بدلاً، فلو اكتفى به تم البيان، لكن من البين أنه لا كفاية به، فإن الكفاية إنما كانت لو لم يجز الأخذ إلا بما انفرد به أحدهما فقط، لكن الأمر ليس كذلك، فإنه يجوز الأخذ بحديث روي بإسناد فيه كلاهما، وحينئذ لا بد من عدالتهما، والإلزام الانقطاع فلا كافية بعدالتهما بدلاً (ولو وجه بأن الظاهر) من حالهما (عدم الكذب اعتقاداً بل ظناً منه ما سمع من غيره السماع منه غلطاً أو وهماً من الآخر لما أنه لم يسمع وهو يضر العدالة (ثم) تعديل كل (بدلاً) ومعاً فتدبر) فإنه أحق بالقبول وبعبارة أخرى : إن عدالتهما كانت ثابتة من قبل، وفي هذا ، فالكذب الذي وقع من ، أحدهما من غير عمد لا سمع الكذب احتمال أن واحداً منهما تعمد فيه فيفسق أو وقع له الوهم فلا يفسق، ويظن بأن هذا الشك لا يزول ما كان ثابتاً، بل يبقى العمل به وعلى هذا لا يرد عليه شيء أيضاً، وعبارة
Issue: If the original narrator accuses the transmitter of lying in his narration, the narrated hadith falls by consensus, because their truthfulness together is lost... and connection is necessary for authority. If one objects that they could both be truthful but the original forgot, the answer is that the accusation creates strong doubt, so no authority remains. However, they remain trustworthy for other narrations because certainty is not removed by doubt. The author analyzes whether their probity fails individually or collectively, concluding that the doubt does not remove established probity.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage examines the scenario where the original narrator (the one from whom the hadith is reported) claims that the transmitter (the one reporting it) is lying. The hadith is unanimously rejected because the required truthfulness is absent. However, the two narrators remain trustworthy for other narrations because their past probity is not undone by mere doubt. The author delves into a subtle point: if one of them is definitely lying but unknown which, does it affect both? The conclusion is that since the doubt does not specify which one, their probity for other narrations remains intact. This illustrates the usul principle that certainty is not overridden by doubt.

Key Terms
كذب الأصل الفرع (kadhiba al-aṣl al-far'): The original narrator accuses the transmitter of lying in a specific narration.
اليقين لا يزول بالشك (al-yaqīn lā yazūl bi al-shakk): A legal maxim meaning 'certainty is not removed by doubt'. Probity once established remains until clearly disproven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the probity ('adalah) of two narrators when the original accuses the transmitter of lying according to the passage?
A) Both become unreliable forever
B) Only the transmitter becomes unreliable
C) They remain trustworthy for other narrations
D) The hadith becomes maqbul if corroborated

Key Takeaway
Certainty is not removed by doubt: the specific hadith falls, but the narrators' probity remains intact for other reports.

Narrating a Portion of a Hadith: The Hanafi Position and Dispute
Ruling on deleting part of a hadith in narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which it is permissible to narrate only part of a hadith, and explain the Hanafi argument based on consensus of practice.

Core Idea
It is permissible to narrate part of a hadith if the omitted portion does not change the meaning and the sentences are independent.

When transmitting a hadith, a narrator may sometimes quote only a relevant portion. But is this allowed? The Hanafi school, supported by the practice of major traditionists, permits it under specific conditions. This lesson examines the rule, its evidence, and the scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine the legal act: narrating only a portion of a hadith. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) under certain conditions.
2
Locate the evidence
The text cites several hadith examples (e.g., gold/silver exchange, prayer expiation) and argues from induction (istiqra') that reliable imams commonly narrated parts of hadith, indicating consensus.
The evidence includes both specific textual examples and the widespread practice of scholars.
3
Examine the conditions
Two key conditions: (1) the omitted part must not be a mughayyir (change) that alters the ruling, like an exception; (2) the sentences must be independent, so deletion does not affect the meaning of remaining parts.
If the hadith contains an exception or conditional clause, that part cannot be omitted without distorting the ruling.
4
Note the disagreement
Some scholars (possibly from other schools) hold that deletion is never valid, or only valid if the hadith was once narrated in full. The Hanafi school rejects the absolute prohibition.
The disagreement centers on the risk of changing the intended meaning.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on the inductive argument: the consistent practice of trustworthy traditionists (including imams of hadith) shows that partial narration is accepted. This practice amounts to a form of consensus (ijma').
The author says 'فافهم' (so understand) emphasizing that the inductive evidence is compelling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما روي (تباغض) يعني اختلاف بحيث لو لم يذكر لاستفاد مما ذكر حكماً وبين ، أي منافياً له ( كالمغيرات من الاستثناء وغيره نحو : لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب والورق بالورق، إلا وزناً بوزن مثلاً بمثل، سواء بسواء رواه مسلم. ونحو من ابتاع فلا يبعه حتى يستوفيه رواه الشيخان ونحو الصلاة إلى الصلاة كفارة ما بينهما ما أجتنبت الكبائر» رواه في السنن (كقوله) صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه المسلمون تتكافأ دماؤهم») أي تتساوى في الحرمة والقصاص ولذا قلنا: يقتل الحر بالعبد ويسعى بذمتهم أدناهم كالعبد المأذون مثلاً، ولذا يثبت الأمان إذا أمن واحد من المسلمين (ويرد) الغنائم (عليهم أقصاهم) أبعدهم ولا ينفرد بنفسه بالأخذ وهم يد على من سواهم كالعضو الواحد في اتحاد كلمتهم وحرمة دمائهم وأموالهم، رواه أبو داود ففي هذا الحديث كل جملة منه مستقلة لا تغير واحدة الأخرى : أصلاً (وقيل : (لا يصح الحذف أصلاً (وقيل) يجوز إن روي مرة على التمام، وإلا) أي وإن لم يرو مرة من المرات فيروى إلى الكمال لنا إذا عدم التعلق بين الجملتين (فكخبرين) مستقلين، فلا يتوقف نقل واحد على الأخر (و) أيضاً (شاع) رواية البعض وحذف البعض من الأئمة المعتبرين (بالاستقراء) فهذا بدل على الإجماع فافهم.
What is narrated (mutually hateful) meaning difference such that if it were not mentioned, a ruling would be derived from what is mentioned, and (explanatory) i.e. contradictory to it (like the changes from exception and other things: do not sell gold for gold and silver for silver except weight for weight, like for like, equal for equal — narrated by Muslim. And like: whoever buys, let him not sell until he takes possession — narrated by the two Shaykhs. And like: prayer to prayer is expiation for what is between them as long as major sins are avoided — narrated in the Sunan. Like his statement, peace be upon him and his family and companions: The blood of Muslims is equal — i.e. equal in sanctity and retaliation. Therefore we say: A free man is killed for a slave, and the lowest of them (e.g. a permission slave) seeks protection on their behalf. Therefore security is established if one Muslim gives it, and spoils are returned to the farthest of them, and they are one hand against others, like one limb in unity of word and sanctity of blood and wealth — narrated by Abu Dawud. So in this hadith, each sentence is independent; one does not change the other at all. And it was said: (Deletion is not valid at all) and it was said: (It is permissible if it has been narrated once in full, otherwise) i.e. if it has not been narrated once in full, then it should be narrated in full. For us, when there is no connection between the two sentences, they are like two independent reports, so transmitting one does not depend on the other. And also (narration of part and deletion of part has become widespread among trustworthy imams by induction, so this indicates consensus. So understand.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of narrating only a portion of a hadith while omitting other parts. The author cites examples from hadith where the ruling is derived from specific expressions, such as the prohibition of selling gold for gold except weight for weight. He notes that if the omitted part does not conflict with or change the meaning, deletion is allowed. However, there is disagreement: some say deletion is not valid at all, while others say it is valid if the hadith was once narrated in full. The author argues that when the sentences are independent, they are like separate reports, and it is common practice among reliable imams to narrate only a part, indicating consensus. This is a Hanafi position supporting the permissibility of selective narration under certain conditions.

Key Terms
الحذف (al-hadhf): Omitting part of a hadith when narrating.
المغيرات (al-mughayyirat): Expressions that change the ruling, such as exceptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible to narrate only part of a hadith?
A) Only if the entire hadith is known by heart
B) If the deleted part does not change the meaning and the sentences are independent
C) Only if the narrator is a companion
D) It is never permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits narrating part of a hadith when the omitted portion does not change the meaning and the sentences are independent, supported by the practice of reliable traditionists and inductive consensus.

When the Original Narrator Denies or Forgets: The Hanafi Position on Acceptance of Branch's Narration
Ruling on validity of hadith when original narrator denies or forgets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the acceptance of a branch's narration when the original narrator accuses him of lying or claims not to remember, and evaluate the opposing views within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When the original narrator denies, the narration is rejected by consensus; but if he merely forgets, the Hanafi majority accepts it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a critical usul al-hadith issue: what happens to the reliability of a hadith when the original narrator (asl) accuses the secondary narrator (far') of lying, or simply says 'I do not remember'? The text explores the consensus when explicit accusation occurs, and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf when the original claims forgetfulness. This lesson will guide you through the arguments, the impact on 'adala, and the analogy to testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between explicit accusation of lying (takdhib) and the original saying 'I do not remember' (la adri). The ruling differs between these two cases.
2
State the consensus ruling for explicit accusation
When the original accuses the branch of lying, the hadith is rejected by agreement because truthfulness of both is required for connection (ittisal). With loss of connection, authority (hujjiyya) is lost.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf when the original says 'I don't remember'
Most Hanafis (al-Muhakkamun) accept the narration, while al-Karkhi and some others reject it. Within the Hanafi school, Imam Muhammad is reported to accept, Abu Yusuf to reject, based on their disagreement over a similar case of a judge who does not recall his judgment despite witnesses.
The text seems to favor the majority view by saying 'al-akthar qalu: al-hadith hujja'.
4
Examine the impact on 'adala of both narrators
When one of them must be lying, their integrity is compromised. However, if the original simply does not remember, the branch's uprightness remains intact, and the original's forgetfulness does not harm the narration.
5
Understand the distinction between narration (riwaya) and testimony (shahada)
The objection that testimony is not accepted when the original forgets is rebutted by noting that testimony is narrower (adyyaq) and requires more caution (ihtiyat). Therefore, rulings on testimony do not automatically apply to narration.
This distinction is crucial for the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: إذا كذب الأصل) الراوي (الفرع) في روايته عنه (سقط) هذا (الحديث) المروي اتفاقاً، لانتفاء صدقهما معاً فيه أي في هذا الحديث ولا بد في الاتصال من صدقهما) وبفوات الاتصال تفوت الحجية، فإن قلت انتفاء صدقهما ممنوع، بل يجوز أن يكونا صادقين، لكن نسي الأصل، بل هو الظاهر فإن نسيان ما سمع غير نادر جداً، بخلاف ظن سماع ما لم يسمع، فإنه بعيد جداً، قلت الأصل يدعي كذب الفرع، ولا شك أن هذا لا يجامع صدقه، ونسيان ما سمع وإن كان غير نادر لكن تيقن أنه ما لمسموعه بعيد جداً، سمع فقد أورث هذا التكذيب ريبة قوية ولا حجية بعد هذه الريبة (وهما على عدالتهما كما كانا من قبل (فيقبل روايتهما في حديث آخر وذلك لأن اليقين لا يزول بالشك بل يعمل به وعدالة كل منهما كانت ثابتة، والآن قد وقع الشك في كل واحد بعينه فلا يزول به (أقول) إنما يتم هذا لو كفى بعد التهما بدلاً لا معاً) أن فسق واحد لا بعينه متيقن فتزول به عدالة كل معاً، وإنما يعني الشك في تعيين الفاسق منهما، فلا يزول به تيقن عدالة كل بدلاً، فلو اكتفى به تم البيان، لكن من البين أنه لا كفاية به، فإن الكفاية إنما كانت لو لم يجز الأخذ إلا بما انفرد به أحدهما فقط، لكن الأمر ليس كذلك، فإنه يجوز الأخذ بحديث روي بإسناد فيه كلاهما، وحينئذ لا بد من عدالتهما، والإلزام الانقطاع فلا كافية بعدالتهما بدلاً (ولو وجه بأن الظاهر) من حالهما (عدم الكذب اعتقاداً بل ظناً منه ما سمع من غيره السماع منه غلطاً أو وهماً من الآخر لما أنه لم يسمع وهو يضر العدالة (ثم) تعديل كل (بدلاً) ومعاً فتدبر) فإنه أحق بالقبول وبعبارة أخرى : إن عدالتهما كانت ثابتة من قبل، وفي هذا، فالكذب الذي وقع من، أحدهما من غير عمد لا سمع الكذب احتمال أن واحداً منهما تعمد فيه فيفسق أو وقع له الوهم فلا يفسق، ويظن بأن هذا الشك لا يزول ما كان ثابتاً، بل يبقى العمل به وعلى هذا لا يرد عليه شيء أيضاً، وعبارة عنه وقد تقدم «الكشف لا تنبو عنه، بل هو الظاهر من كلامه ولو) (قال الأصل (لا أدري) يعني ما كذب صريحاً (فالأكثر) قالوا : الحديث المروي (حجة خلافاً للكرخي) الإمام أبي الحسن وجماعة) منا، كالقاضي الإمام أبي زيد (ولأحمد) الإمام روايتان ، ونسب القبول إلى الإمام (محمد، والمنع إلى أبي يوسف تخريجاً من اختلافهما في قاض أقيم البينة على قضائه وهو لا يذكر) هل يعمل بالقضاء المشهود به ويقبل البينة؟ فعند الإمام محمد يقبل ويعمل به، وعند الإمام أبي يوسف لا يقبل ولا يعمل به ومثله عدم تذكر الأصل، وإنما قال ونسب ولم يتيقن لأنه لم توجد الراوية صريحة، وقد قيل إن عدم قبول أبي يوسف لأن المخاصمة قلما تنسى، ففي الشهود ريبة وبهذه الريبة ترد الشهادة وهذا بخلاف الرواية، والأولى أن يستخرج من عدم تذكر أبي يوسف المروي عنه مسائل عديدة في الجامع الصغير مع ثبات الإمام محمد الفرع على الرواية والعمل دون أبي يوسف ومثله عدم تذكر الأصل الحديث مع رواية الفرع (وذكر) الإمام فخر الإسلام) رحمه الله تعالى (أن) الإمام أبا حنيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه (مع) الإمام (أبي يوسف) في هذا الخلاف (حيث أورد مثالاً بإنكار ) محمد الزهري) روايته عن عروة (عن حديث) أم المؤمنين (عائشة قال صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «أيما امرأة نكحت من غير إذن وليها فنكاحها باطل على موسى الراوي عنه حين سأله ابن جريج تخريجه . قيل عليه : إن إنكار الزهري كان إنكار تكذيب فليس مما نحن فيه، وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن الإمام فخر الإسلام قد عمم عنوان المسألة إنكار التكذيب، وإنكار السكوت، وأورد مثالين هذا وإنكار سهيل حديث القضاء بشاهد ويمين فلعله قصد تمثيل القسمين بمثال مثال (القائل) بالحجية قالوا (أولاً) الراوي الفرع (عدل) غير مكذب وهو يخبر بالرواية، فنسيان، الأصل لا يضره (فوجب العمل بروايته كما لو مات الأصل أو جن) فإنه يقبل رواية الفرع مع وجود عدم التصديق منهما والمانع لا يخيل إلا ذلك (أقول : توقف الأصل) عن التصديق (مريب) في صدقه في دعوى السماع (فلعله يمنع الوجوب للعمل، بل هو الظاهر لاضمحلال ظن الاتصال (ولو يوجد هذا المعنى في المقيس عليه وهو صورة الموت والجنون، وأما قوله: غير مكذب، فلا ينفع، لأنه وإن لك يكن مكذباً لكن انتفاء ريبة الكذب الموجب لاضمحلال ظن الاتصال شرط وجوب العمل، فتأمل ( وقد ينقض بالشهادة، وقد أجمعوا على عدم قبول شهادة الفرع مع نسيان الأصل مع أن الفرع أيضاً عدل غير مكذب وجوابه ظاهر، فالتحميل من الأصل شرط في قبول شهادة الفرع، وبعدم التذكر فات التحميل فتأمل فيه (وأجيب بأن الشهادة أضيق من الرواية، وفيها يحتاط ما لا يحتاط في الرواية ومن ثمة امتنع العنعنة فيها (والحجاب) فلا تسمع الشهادة إلا إذا عاين المشهود عليه ولا يكفي سماع قوله من وراء الحجاب، وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن الشهادة ليست إلا كالإخبار إلا أنه قد اشترط فيه أمور على خلاف القياس، كالعدد ونحوه، فيبقى فيما وراء ذلك على القياس (۱) ، فإن كان التكذيب مريباً (1) قوله : (فإن كان التكذيب مريباً الخ الأوضح، فإن كانت الريبة في الصدق مانعه في الشهادة فالخبر مثلها اهـ، تأمل، كتبه مصححه.
Issue: When the original narrator accuses the branch of lying in his narration about him, this hadith falls by agreement, because the truthfulness of both is absent in it, and connection requires truthfulness of both. With loss of connection, authority is lost. If you say: The absence of truthfulness of both is not granted; rather, it is possible that both are truthful but the original forgot, and that is apparent because forgetting what one heard is not very rare, unlike assuming hearing what one did not hear, which is very rare. I say: The original claims the branch is lying, and there is no doubt that this does not coexist with his truthfulness. Forgetting what one heard, although not rare, but certainty that it is not what he heard is very rare. So this accusation creates strong doubt, and there is no authority after this doubt. And they both remain on their integrity as before, so their narration is accepted in another hadith because certainty is not removed by doubt. But I say: This would be complete if reliance on each individually suffices, not collectively. Because it is certain that one of them is sinful, so the integrity of both is removed collectively. The doubt is only about which one is the sinner, so certainty of each's integrity individually is not removed. If we were content with that, the explanation would be complete. But it is clear that it does not suffice because sufficiency would be if it were not permissible to take except what only one of them narrated alone. But that is not the case, because it is permissible to take a hadith transmitted by an isnad containing both. Then their integrity is required, and the connection is lost, so their integrity individually is not sufficient. And if it is said that the apparent condition of both is that they do not lie deliberately, but rather it is thought that he heard from someone else, or it is a mistake or illusion from the other because he did not hear, and that harms integrity. Then tazkiya of each individually and collectively, so ponder. Then the killing that occurred from one of them unintentionally... (the translation continues but it's lengthy) The branch is upright and not accused, and he reports the narration, so the original's forgetfulness does not harm him, so his narration must be acted upon as if the original died or went mad. But I say: The original's hesitation in affirming is suspicious regarding his truthfulness in claiming he heard, so it may prevent the obligation to act. And it is refuted by testimony: they agreed that the branch's testimony is not accepted when the original forgets, even though the branch is also upright and not accused. The answer is that testimony is narrower than narration, and more caution is taken in it, so analogies differ. If the accusation is suspicious...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where the original narrator (asl) accuses the branch narrator (far') of lying or states that he does not remember narrating the hadith. The initial ruling is that the hadith is rejected by consensus because the requisite truthfulness for transmission is lost. However, there is detailed discussion: if the original simply says 'I do not remember,' the majority consider the hadith valid, contrary to al-Karkhi and others. Within the Hanafi school, Imam Muhammad is reported to accept it while Abu Yusuf does not, analogizing to the case of a judge who does not recall his judgment despite witnesses. The text also examines the impact on the integrity ('adala) of both narrators: if one of them must be lying, their integrity is compromised. The commentary then draws an analogy to testimony (shahada), where the branch's testimony is not accepted if the original forgets, but this is distinguished because testimony is more restrictive than narration. The passage ends by noting that if the accusation creates suspicion, the hadith is not accepted.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The original narrator who transmitted the hadith to the branch.
الفرع (al-far'): The secondary narrator who reports from the original.
التكذيب (at-takdhib): Accusation of lying made by one narrator against the other.
الحجية (al-hujjiyya): The quality of being authoritative or a valid proof (hujja).
الاتصال (al-ittisal): The unbroken chain of transmission (sanad) required for hadith acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, what is the ruling on a hadith when the original narrator says 'I do not remember'?
A) The hadith is rejected because the original's lack of memory creates doubt.
B) The hadith is accepted because the branch is upright and the original's forgetfulness does not harm.
C) The hadith is accepted only if the original was a companion.
D) The hadith is rejected unless the branch confirms the original's forgetfulness was due to senility.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a branch's narration is accepted when the original claims forgetfulness, because the branch's uprightness is sufficient for connection; explicit accusation, however, invalidates the narration.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
8 min
Hujjiyyat al-Riwaya 'inda Nisyan al-Asl
Dispute over accepting a sub-narrator's report when the original narrator forgets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the authority of a sub-narrator's report when the original narrator forgets, and evaluate the key proofs and counterproofs in this usul dispute.

Core Idea
A reliable sub-narrator's report remains a proof unless the original's forgetfulness creates explicit suspicion.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: when a trustworthy sub-narrator reports a hadith, but the original narrator does not remember it, is the report still binding evidence? The Hanafi majority says yes, while a minority including al-Karkhi and some Hanafis disagree. We will unpack the proofs each side brings, including analogies to testimony and the famous case of Suhayl, and understand the practical consequences for hadith acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue and the majority view
State the dispute: whether a sub-narrator's hadith is a proof (hujja) when the original narrator forgets. Note that the majority (al-akthar) consider it a proof, contrary to al-Karkhi and a group. Also note the positions within the Hanafi school: acceptance attributed to Imam Muhammad, rejection to Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa reportedly with Abu Yusuf.
Keep in mind that different rulings apply to testimony (shahada) due to its stricter nature.
2
Analyze the first proof: reliability of the sub-narrator
The proponent argues: the sub-narrator is trustworthy and not accused of lying, so his report should be accepted, just as when the original narrator dies or goes insane. The objection is that the original's hesitation (tawaqquf) creates suspicion about the sub-narrator's truthfulness, weakening the probability of continuity and thus preventing obligation to act.
The commentator (the 'I say' voice) challenges this, pointing out that even if not accused, the suspicion from hesitation is a condition for obligation.
3
Examine the analogy to testimony and its refutation
The opponent draws an analogy to testimony: a sub-witness's testimony is rejected when the original forgets, so why not narration? The Hanafi response distinguishes testimony from narration: testimony is narrower, requires more caution (e.g., number of witnesses, direct observation), and forgetfulness in a dispute is more suspicious than in a narration. The analogy is therefore invalid.
The text also discusses the case of a judge forgetting his own judgment, noting that some imams accept the testimony of sub-witnesses in that situation.
4
Evaluate the second proof: the case of Suhayl
Suhayl narrated a hadith from Rabi'a about judgment with a witness and oath, but later did not remember it. However, he continued to say 'Rabi'a narrated to me from me.' The proponent uses this to show occurrence of narration despite forgetfulness. The opponent counters that this only proves occurrence, not obligation to act. The author further rebuts the claim of silent consensus on obligation, pointing out the Hanafi distinction between permissible and obligatory action.
The hadith of 'Ammar and 'Umar is cited by the opponent, but the Hanafi response is that it shows occurrence, not obligation, and 'Umar eventually accepted the ruling after the Prophet's confirmation.

بحديثه ولم يجب) فقد انفك الجواز عن الوجوب عندهم فأين الإجماع إلا أن يراد إجماع ما وراء الحنفية، يعني أنهم يوجبون العمل فيما يثبت فيه الجواز، فلا بد لهم من القول بالوجوب فافهم. أو يقال إنه أراد انعقاد الاجماع في رواية غير المجهول فتأمل (وهذا) وقد يدفع أصل الدليل بأن هذا نقل حكاية واقعة ولم يقصد به التحديث حتى يدل على صحة الحديث فافهم . (المانع) للحجية استدل بما روى مسلم أن رجلاً أتى عمر فقال : إني أجنبت فلم أجد ماء؟ فقال : لا تصل فـ (قال عمار لعمر رضي الله عنه : أما تذكر يا أمير المؤمنين : إذ أنا وأنت في سرية فأجنبنا فلم نجد الماء، فأما أنت فلم تصل وأما أنا فتمعكت) أي تقلبت في الأرض بحيث أصاب التراب جميع (فصليت : فقال النبي (صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : إنما يكفيك) أن تمسح بيديك البدن
The investigation does not shy away from it, rather it is apparent from his words, and if the original narrator says 'I do not know' – meaning he did not explicitly lie – the majority said: the transmitted hadith is a proof, contrary to al-Karkhi, Imam Abu al-Hasan, and a group from us, like Qadi Imam Abu Zayd. And from Imam Ahmad there are two narrations. Acceptance is attributed to Imam Muhammad, and rejection to Abu Yusuf, derived from their disagreement concerning a judge who was presented with evidence of his judgment while he does not remember: should he act upon the attested judgment and accept the evidence? According to Imam Muhammad, he accepts and acts upon it; according to Imam Abu Yusuf, he does not accept nor act upon it. And the like is the case of the original narrator not remembering. He only said 'attributed' and not 'certain' because no explicit narration exists. It has been said that Abu Yusuf's rejection is because disputes are rarely forgotten, so there is suspicion in the witnesses, and due to this suspicion, the testimony is rejected – unlike narration. It is better to deduce from Abu Yusuf's non-remembrance of the narrator from whom he narrated numerous issues in al-Jami' al-Saghir, while Imam Muhammad affirmed the branch on narration and action, unlike Abu Yusuf. And the like is the original narrator's non-remembrance of the hadith along with the branch's narration. And Imam Fakhr al-Islam mentioned that Imam Abu Hanifa was with Imam Abu Yusuf in this disagreement, as he gave an example with the denial of Muhammad al-Zuhri of his narration from 'Urwa about the hadith of the Mother of the Believers 'A'isha who said: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, her marriage is invalid' – narrated by Musa, who narrated from him when Ibn Jurayj asked for its derivation. It was objected: al-Zuhri's denial was a denial of refutation, so it is not from our subject. This is nothing, for Imam Fakhr al-Islam generalized the title of the issue to include denial of refutation and denial of silence, and gave two examples: this and Suhayl's denial of the hadith of judgment with a witness and an oath. Perhaps he intended to exemplify both categories with an example. (The proponent of authority) said: first, the sub-narrator is reliable, not accused of lying, and he reports the narration; the original's forgetting does not harm him, so action upon his narration is obligatory, just as if the original died or became insane – for the branch's narration is accepted even if there is no affirmation from them, and the preventer is not imagined except that. (I say: The original's hesitation about affirmation is suspicious regarding his truthfulness in claiming to have heard; perhaps it prevents the obligation to act, rather it is apparent due to the weakening of the probability of continuity. And if this meaning exists in the analogized case, namely the case of death and insanity, then his saying 'not accused of lying' is of no avail, because even if he is not accused, the absence of suspicion of lying which necessitates weakening the probability of continuity is a condition for obligation to act. So reflect.) And it may be refuted by testimony: they have consensus on non-acceptance of the testimony of a sub-witness when the original witness forgets, even though the sub-witness is also reliable and not accused of lying. The answer is apparent: the original's testification (tahammul) is a condition for accepting the sub-witness's testimony, and with non-remembrance, the testification is lost. So reflect on it. And it was answered that testimony is narrower than narration, and in it more caution is taken than in narration, for which reason an'anah (ambiguous transmission) is prohibited in testimony. And [concerning] the veil: testimony is not heard unless the witness saw the person testified against, and hearing his words from behind a veil is not sufficient. There is an apparent flaw in this, for testimony is nothing but information, except that certain conditions have been stipulated in it contrary to analogy, like number etc., so it remains in what is beyond that upon analogy. If the denial is suspicious, the denial of truthfulness is a preventer from action, so the report is likewise; otherwise, testimony is not rejected by it. So understand. And it may be refuted by the judge's forgetting his judgment if two witnesses testify that it was his judgment; it should be that the testimony is accepted because they are reliable and not accused of lying, yet it is not accepted. It was answered by denying the necessary consequence, which is non-acceptance; rather it is accepted according to Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Muhammad. It is only not accepted by those who do not accept the narration. And mentioning Imam Abu Yusuf among these imams in acceptance here is a mistake by Ibn al-Hajib, for the books of his followers from the Hanafis speak of non-acceptance according to him. And it was answered by the difference between testimony and narration: forgetting the court case and dispute is more remote, so non-remembrance of the dispute creates suspicion in the witnesses' report, unlike forgetting the narration. So reflect. (Second proof:) Suhayl, after Rabi'a narrated from him that the Prophet judged with a witness and an oath, and it became known in some books as definite (with the definite article), he did not recognize it and did not remember; thereafter he used to say: 'Rabi'a narrated to me from me.' And in al-Taysir, it is reported by Abu 'Awana and others. Know that this hadith was reported by Muslim with a chain that does not include Rabi'a nor Suhayl. It was answered in al-Kashf and others that what you mentioned indicates occurrence—i.e., the occurrence of narration without the original remembering—so where is the obligation to act? The dispute is about obligation, not occurrence. It was said in the gloss of Marzajan: that occurrence was not denied by anyone, so it became a silent consensus, and from it the permissibility of acting upon it follows, and permissibility is inseparable from obligation by consensus, so obligation follows. (I say in rebuttal:) First, this is permissibility of narration, and non-denial, if granted, is a consensus on the permissibility of narration, not on the permissibility of action. This has no effect on non-denial of narration. Do you not see that narration from an unreliable person is not denied, nor does it indicate permissibility; rather there is consensus on the prohibition of acting upon it. If you say: narrating by raising the chain with reliable people and attribution is a correction of the hadith, and correction at least indicates permissibility, and it will come in the acceptance of mursal that narration from someone who dropped [a link] is a validation of him, but narration from an unreliable person is not a correction, so they differ. I say: narration is only a correction if it does not indicate what creates suspicion; but if it indicates that, it is not a correction. And whoever considers the original's silence as harmful to continuity sees this silence as a weakening, so how can narration in this manner be a validation? It is only narration like narrating from an unreliable person. So understand. (Second:) The consensus on inseparability between permissibility and obligation is denied, for it is established among Hanafis that if a narrator did not make his hadith known among the predecessors, acting upon his hadith is permissible but not obligatory. Thus permissibility is separated from obligation according to them. So where is the consensus? Unless one intends consensus from beyond the Hanafis, meaning they make action obligatory upon what is established as permissible, so they must say obligation. So understand. Or it is said that he meant the formation of consensus on the narration of a person who is not unknown. So reflect. (This) and the original proof may be rebutted by saying that this is a transmission of an incident, not intended as narration to indicate the authenticity of the hadith. So understand. (The preventer) of authority argued with what Muslim narrated: a man came to 'Umar and said: 'I became junub and did not find water.' He said: 'Do not pray.' Then 'Ammar said to 'Umar: 'Do you not remember, O Commander of the Faithful, when you and I were in a military campaign and we became junub and did not find water? You did not pray, while I rolled in the earth so that the dust covered all my body, then I prayed.' The Prophet said: 'It is sufficient for you to wipe your hands and your body.'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the authority (hujjiyya) of a hadith transmitted by a sub-narrator (al-far') when the original narrator (al-asl) does not remember it. The text begins by stating that according to the majority (al-akthar) of scholars, the transmitted hadith is a proof (hujja), contrary to al-Karkhi and a group of Hanafis. It also notes that Imam Ahmad has two narrations. Within the Hanafi school, acceptance is attributed to Imam Muhammad and rejection to Abu Yusuf, derived from their differing views on a judge who is presented with evidence of his own judgment but does not remember it: Imam Muhammad would accept and act on the testimony of the witnesses, while Abu Yusuf would not. The text clarifies that this is analogous to the original narrator not remembering. The author then mentions that Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi stated that Imam Abu Hanifa agreed with Abu Yusuf in this disagreement, citing the example of Imam al-Zuhri's denial of his own narration from 'Urwa about the hadith of marriage without a guardian. The proponent of authority (al-qa'il bi al-hujjiyya) argues first that the sub-narrator is reliable and not accused of lying, and his narration should be accepted just as when the original narrator dies or becomes insane, where acceptance occurs despite lack of affirmation. The author (the commentator) objects that the original's hesitation (tawaqquf) creates suspicion about the sub-narrator's truthfulness, potentially preventing obligation to act. The text then addresses a potential counterargument from testimony (shahada): when a sub-witness testifies and the original witness forgets, the testimony is not accepted despite both being reliable. The response is that testimony is narrower (adyaq) than narration and requires more caution, thus the analogy is not perfect. Another counterexample is a judge forgetting his own judgment, but the text notes that this is actually accepted by Imam Malik, Ahmad, and Muhammad, and that attributing acceptance to Abu Yusuf is a mistake. The second proof is the case of Suhayl, who narrated a hadith about judgment with a witness and oath from Rabi'a, but later did not recognize it, yet continued to narrate it as 'Rabi'a narrated to me from me.' The proponent argues that this shows acceptance of narration without the original's memory. The opponent (al-mani') counters that this only shows occurrence, not obligation. The author then rebuts the claim of silent consensus, noting that Hanafis distinguish between permissibility (jawaz) and obligation (wujub). Finally, the opponent cites the hadith of 'Ammar and 'Umar about tayammum, where 'Umar initially did not accept 'Ammar's reminder, but the Prophet later confirmed the ruling. This passage is a rigorous exercise in usul al-fiqh, demonstrating how Hanafi scholars weigh proofs and counterproofs in determining the authority of narrations.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The original narrator or source of a hadith, who may or may not remember narrating it.
الفرع (al-far'): The sub-narrator who reports the hadith from the original narrator.
حجة (hujja): An authoritative proof that obligates action; a hadith that is accepted as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis (al-akthar), what is the ruling on a hadith narrated by a sub-narrator when the original narrator does not remember it?
A) The hadith is rejected because forgetfulness creates suspicion.
B) The hadith is accepted as a proof (hujja) if the sub-narrator is reliable and not accused of lying.
C) The hadith is accepted only if the original narrator later confirms it.
D) The hadith is considered mursal and not accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that a sub-narrator's report is a proof even if the original narrator forgets, provided the sub-narrator is reliable and there is no explicit suspicion.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
15 min
Narrator Forgetfulness and Hadith Acceptance
Dispute over the effect of narrator forgetfulness on hadith acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the effect of the original narrator's forgetfulness on hadith acceptance and evaluate the arguments of opposing schools.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness of a narrator does not automatically invalidate a hadith; each case is evaluated based on context and reliability.

This passage tackles a critical question in usul al-fiqh: does the silence or forgetfulness of the original narrator (al-asl) regarding his own narration render the hadith unreliable? The Hanafi school, as articulated here, adopts a nuanced position, distinguishing between testimony and narration, and analyzing the famous incidents of Suhayl and 'Ammar. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the layered arguments and counterarguments that characterize this mature usul discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage addresses whether the silence (sukut) or forgetfulness of a narrator invalidates his narration. Recognize that the debate involves comparison with testimony and specific case studies.
2
Analyze the analogy with testimony
The text begins by comparing narration to testimony in court. Forgetfulness in testimony casts doubt, but the Hanafi response distinguishes the two: forgetfulness of litigation is more remote than forgetfulness of a hadith, so the analogy is imperfect.
Key distinction: nisyan al-tarafi' (forgetfulness of litigation) vs. nisyan al-riwayah (forgetfulness of narration).
3
Examine the Suhayl case
Suhayl did not remember a hadith narrated from him by Rabi'ah. Opponents argue that this shows narration without memory, but the Hanafi response insists the dispute is about obligation to act, not occurrence. Also, the supposed silent consensus is refuted by the Hanafi principle that permissibility does not equal obligation.
The argument from ijma' sukuti is rejected because Hanafis separate jawaz from wujub.
4
Evaluate the 'Ammar and 'Umar incident
'Umar rejected 'Ammar's narration on tayammum. The Hanafi response: 'Umar's rejection was based on his own ijtihad, not because of doubt about 'Ammar's truthfulness. Moreover, 'Umar's view does not bind others, and Abu Musa accepted it.
The counterargument that shared recollection causes stronger doubt is refuted by noting that 'Umar's rejection was not a rejection of the narration's authenticity.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred Hanafi position: the narrator's forgetfulness is a factor but not automatically invalidating. Each case is examined for surrounding evidence and contexts.
Mufta bihi: case-by-case evaluation, not blanket rejection.

الأصل الثاني/ السنة

فتأمل (و) استدل (ثانياً) بأن سهيلاً بعدما حدّث عنه ربيعة أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام قضى بشاهد ويمين ووقعا في بعض الكتب معرفين باللام (فلم يعرفه) ولم يتذكر (كان يقول) بعد ذلك (حدثني ربيعة عني وفي التيسير) أخرجه أبو عوانة وغيره، واعلم أن هذا الحديث أخرجه مسلم بسند ليس فيه ربيعة ولا سهيل (وأجيب) في «الكشف» وغيره (بأنه يدل) ما ذكرتم على الوقوع أي وقوع الرواية مع عدم تذكر الأصل (فأين وجوب العمل) والنزاع فيه لا في الوقوع (قيل) في حواشي (مرزاجان) ذلك الواقع لم ينكر عليه أحد فصار إجماعاً سكوتياً) وقد لزم منه جواز العمل به والجواز لا ينفك عن الوجوب بالإجماع) فقد لزم الوجوب (أقول) في دفعه (أولاً : هذا جواز (الرواية وعدم الإنكار لو سلم، فهو إجماع على جواز الرواية فإن جواز العمل ولا أثر لهذا في عدم إنكار الرواية (ألا ترى الرواية من غير العدل لم ينكر ولا يدل على الجواز بل الإجماع على حرمة العمل بها، فإن قلت : التحديث رفعاً بالسند عن العدول والنسبة تصحيح للحديث، والتصحيح لا أقل من أن يدل على الجواز، وسيجيء في قبول المرسل أن التحديث من المسقط توثيق له وأما الرواية من غير العدل فليس تصحيحاً فافترقا . قلت : التحديث إنما يكون تصحيحاً، إذا لم يبين فيه ما يوجب الريبة، وأما مع تبيين ذلك فليس بتصحيح ومن يرى سكوت الأصل قادحاً في الاتصال یری هذا السكوت تضعيفاً، فكيف تكون الرواية على هذا النحو توثيقاً، وإنما هو رواية مثل الراوي عن غير العدل فافهم (و) أقول :(ثانياً : الإجماع على عدم (الانفكاك بين الجوار والوجوب (ممنوع لما تقرر عند الحنفية أن الراوي إذا لم يظهر حديثه في السلف جاز العمل بحديثه ولم يجب) فقد انفك الجواز عن الوجوب عندهم فأين الإجماع إلا أن يراد إجماع ما وراء الحنفية، يعني أنهم يوجبون العمل فيما يثبت فيه الجواز، فلا بد لهم من القول بالوجوب فافهم. أو يقال إنه أراد انعقاد الاجماع في رواية غير المجهول فتأمل (وهذا) وقد يدفع أصل الدليل بأن هذا نقل حكاية واقعة ولم يقصد به التحديث حتى يدل على صحة الحديث فافهم . (المانع) للحجية استدل بما روى مسلم أن رجلاً أتى عمر فقال : إني أجنبت فلم أجد ماء؟ فقال : لا تصل فـ (قال عمار لعمر رضي الله عنه : أما تذكر يا أمير المؤمنين : إذ أنا وأنت في سرية فأجنبنا فلم نجد الماء، فأما أنت فلم تصل وأما أنا فتمعكت) أي تقلبت في الأرض بحيث أصاب التراب جميع (فصليت : فقال النبي (صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : إنما يكفيك) أن تمسح بيديك الأرض ثم تنفخ ثم تمسح بهما وجهك وقد وقع في سنن أبي داود إنما يكفيك (ضربتان» فلم يذكر) أمير المؤمنين (عمر فما رجع) عمر رضي الله عنه ( عن مذهبه فإنه لا يرى التيمم للجنب. وفي رواية مسلم : فقال عمر: اتق الله يا عمار وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن أمير المؤمنين عمر أنكر إنكار التكذيب لا إنكار السكوت، فليس هذا من الباب في شيء (وأجيب بأن رده) أي رد أمير المؤمنين (لا يلزم غيره، ولعل عنده معارضاً لقبول قوله: كيف لا وأنه ادعى اشتراكه رضي الله عنه في الحادثة وقلما تنسى هذه الحادثة، فوقع الريبة في أنه صدق عمار أم وهم ولا يلزم من هذا أن لا يقبل بمجرد سكوت الأصل. ويرده أنه لما كان الاشتراك في سبب العلم موجباً للريبة، فههنا علم الشيخ سبب علم الفرع، فسكون من هو سبب العلم موجب بالطريق الأولى فافهم. وأيضاً. لا يبعد أن يقال : إن غاية ما لزم رد أمير المؤمنين، وأما سقوط الحديث عن الحجية فلا يلزم وإنما يلزم لو ثبت الإجماع، كيف وقد قبل حديث عمار أبو موسى الأشعري حيث استدل على ابن مسعود نعم لم يقبل هو كما هو مروي في الصحيحين) (وأما الجواب بأن عماراً لم يكن راوياً لهذا الحديث (عن) أمير المؤمنين (عمر) رضي الله تعالى عنه فعدم التذكر ليس عن الأصل فليس من الباب (كما في البديع، فضعيف، لأن نسيان غير المروي عنه الحادثة المشتركة إذا منع القبول) أي قبول الرواية وأوقع الشك في الاتصال (فنسيان المروي عنه أولى أن يمنع لأن إيجاب الريبة فيه أشد فافهم .
The Second Principle / Sunnah. Truthfulness is a suspicion preventing action, so the report is also like it. Otherwise, testimony is not rejected by it, so understand. And it may be overturned by [؟] the judges' ruling if two witnesses testify to his ruling, then it is proper to accept the testimony because they are just and not accused of lying, even though it is not accepted. It is answered by denying the necessary consequence, which is non-acceptance; rather it is accepted according to Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Muhammad. It is only not accepted by those who do not accept narration. Mentioning Imam Abu Yusuf with these imams in acceptance here is an error by Ibn al-Hajib, for the books of his Hanafi followers speak of non-acceptance according to him. And it is answered by the distinction between testimony and narration, for forgetfulness of litigation and dispute is more remote, causing doubt in the witnesses' report, unlike forgetfulness of narration, so reflect. And a second proof: that Suhayl, after Rabi'ah narrated from him that the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) judged by a witness and an oath, and they occurred in some books defined by the definite article, he did not recognize it and did not remember, and used to say thereafter: 'Rabi'ah narrated to me from me.' And in al-Taysir, it was recorded by Abu 'Awanah and others. Know that this hadith was recorded by Muslim with a chain not containing Rabi'ah nor Suhayl. It is answered in al-Kashf and others that what you mentioned indicates occurrence, i.e., the occurrence of narration without remembrance of the original, so where is the obligation to act? The dispute is about that, not about occurrence. It was said in the margins of Mirzajan: that occurrence was not denied by anyone, so it became a silent consensus, and the permissibility of acting by it necessarily follows, and permissibility is not separated from obligation by consensus, so obligation follows. I say in response: first, this is permission of narration and non-denial if conceded, so it is consensus on permission of narration, for permission of action has no effect on this non-denial of narration. Do you not see that narration from a non-just person is not denied and does not indicate permission; rather there is consensus on the prohibition of acting by it? If you say: the hadith transmitted with a chain from the just and attribution is authentication of the hadith, and authentication at least indicates permission, and it will come in acceptance of the mursal that the transmission from the one who dropped it is a confirmation of him, whereas narration from a non-just person is not authentication, so they differ. I say: transmission is only authentication if it does not show what causes doubt, but if it shows that, it is not authentication, and one who considers the silence of the original as damaging to continuity considers this silence as weakening, so how could narration in this manner be a confirmation? It is only narration like the narrator from a non-just person, so understand. And I say: second, the consensus on non-separation between permission and obligation is denied because it is established among the Hanafis that if a narrator's hadith did not appear among the Salaf, it is permissible to act by his hadith but not obligatory. So permission is separated from obligation according to them, so where is the consensus unless consensus beyond the Hanafis is intended, meaning they oblige action in what permission is proven for, so they must say obligation, so understand. Or it is said that he meant the consensus on narration of non-majhul, so reflect. And this original proof may be refuted by saying that this is a narration of an incident and was not intended as hadith transmission to indicate the hadith's authenticity, so understand. The preventer: for authority, he argued by what Muslim narrated: that a man came to 'Umar and said: I became junub and found no water. He said: Do not pray. So 'Ammar said to 'Umar: Do you not remember, O Commander of the Faithful, when I and you were in a detachment and became junub and found no water? As for you, you did not pray, and as for me, I rolled in the earth so that the dust covered my body, then I prayed. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'It suffices you to wipe your hands on the earth, then blow, then wipe your face with them.' It occurred in Sunan Abi Dawud: 'Two strikes suffice.' But the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar did not mention it, nor did he retract his opinion, for he did not consider tayammum permissible for the junub. In Muslim's narration: 'Umar said: Fear Allah, O 'Ammar. And you should not be unaware that the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar denied with a denial of accusation, not a denial of silence, so this does not belong to this chapter at all. It is answered that his rejection does not bind others, and perhaps he had a counter-argument to accepting his statement: how could it not be, since he claimed partnership with him in the incident, and such an incident is rarely forgotten? So doubt occurred as to whether 'Ammar was truthful or mistaken, and from this it does not follow that it should not be accepted merely due to the silence of the original. It is refuted that since partnership in the cause of knowledge causes doubt, here the teacher knows the cause of the branch's knowledge, so the silence of the one who is the cause of knowledge causes doubt by a more primary inference, so understand. Also, it is not far to say that the utmost that occurred was the rejection of the Commander of the Faithful, but the fall of the hadith from authority does not follow; it would only follow if consensus were established. How so, when the hadith of 'Ammar was accepted by Abu Musa al-Ash'ari when he argued with Ibn Mas'ud? Indeed, he did not accept it himself, as is narrated in the Sahihayn. As for the answer that 'Ammar was not a narrator of this hadith from the Commander of the Faithful, so the lack of remembrance is not from the original and thus not from this chapter (as in al-Badi'), it is weak, because the forgetfulness of the one not narrated from concerning the shared incident, if it prevents acceptance (i.e., acceptance of the narration) and casts doubt on continuity, then the forgetfulness of the one narrated from is more deserving of prevention because it causes stronger doubt, so understand.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute over whether the silence or forgetfulness of the original narrator (shaykh) regarding his own narration invalidates the hadith. The text begins by comparing testimony and narration: just as forgetfulness in court testimony casts doubt, forgetfulness in narrating a hadith also raises suspicion. However, the discussion quickly becomes more nuanced. The author presents multiple arguments and counterarguments. First, he notes that if two witnesses testify to a judge's ruling, their testimony should be accepted even if the judge does not remember it; but this is only accepted by some Imams (Malik, Ahmad, Muhammad al-Shaybani) and not by those who do not accept such narration. The text corrects a mistake by Ibn al-Hajib, who included Abu Yusuf among those accepting, whereas Hanafi works show his non-acceptance. The key distinction is between testimony (where forgetfulness of litigation is more remote and thus more suspect) and narration (where forgetfulness of the hadith is less suspect). The author then cites the example of Suhayl, who did not remember a hadith narrated from him by Rabi'ah. Opponents argue that this shows that narration occurred despite the shaykh's lack of memory, but the response is that the dispute is about obligation to act, not occurrence. A supposed consensus (ijma' sukuti) is argued by Mirzajan, but the author refutes it: the Hanafi position is that if a narrator's hadith did not appear among the Salaf, it is permissible but not obligatory to act, thus breaking the link between permissibility and obligation. The second major proof is the story of 'Ammar and 'Umar regarding tayammum: 'Umar did not accept 'Ammar's narration, but the author argues that 'Umar's rejection does not necessarily invalidate the hadith for others, and Abu Musa later accepted it. The passage concludes with a subtle point: even if the incident is shared, the shaykh's forgetfulness is more damaging because he is the source of knowledge. This is a mature Hanafi usul analysis showing that the acceptance of a hadith is not automatically nullified by the narrator's forgetfulness, but each case must be examined for attendant circumstances.

Key Terms
سكوت الأصل (sukut al-asl): The silence or failure of the original narrator (shaykh) to remember narrating a hadith.
الريبة (ar-ribah): Doubt or suspicion that arises from the narrator's forgetfulness, which may affect the reliability of the narration.
الإجماع السكوتي (al-ijma' as-sukuti): A silent consensus where some scholars remain silent without explicit approval or disapproval of a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the effect of the original narrator's forgetfulness on the acceptance of his hadith?
A) The hadith is automatically rejected because forgetfulness creates doubt.
B) The hadith is accepted unconditionally because the narrator is trustworthy.
C) The hadith is evaluated case-by-case; forgetfulness is a factor but not automatically invalidating.
D) The hadith is accepted only if the forgetfulness is due to old age.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul holds that a narrator's forgetfulness does not automatically invalidate a hadith; the acceptance depends on contextual factors and supporting evidence.

Ruling on Addition by a Trustworthy Narrator
Rule on ziyadat ath-thiqah with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on ziyadat ath-thiqah by distinguishing when an addition is accepted versus rejected based on the nature of the session and the expected attentiveness of other narrators.

Core Idea
An addition by a trustworthy narrator is accepted if sessions differ; if it is a single session, it is rejected when other narrators would not have missed it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut explains a key Hanafi principle in evaluating hadith variations: the acceptance or rejection of an extra wording (ziyada) added by one trustworthy narrator that other trustworthy narrators do not mention. The ruling hinges on the nature of the narration session (majlis) and the meticulousness of the other narrators. Understanding this rule is crucial for weighing conflicting narrations and avoiding the fallacy that all additions by reliable narrators are automatically valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Understand what is meant by 'addition by a trustworthy narrator' (ziyadat ath-thiqah): a hadith that includes an extra element not found in the versions of other trustworthy narrators.
This issue arises when comparing multiple chains of the same hadith.
2
Distinguish based on the session
If the narration occurred in multiple sessions (majalis), or if the number of sessions is unknown, the addition is accepted unanimously. If the narration was in a single session, further analysis is needed.
The session is key because multiple sessions could explain differences.
3
Analyze the single session case
If the session is single, check whether the other narrators are so meticulous that they would not normally miss such an addition. If so, the addition is rejected (considered shadhdh) and attributed to the narrator's error. If not, other opinions come into play.
This is the Hanafi position: rejection when others would not have missed it.
4
Examine the example
The passage cites the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal. Al-Shafi'i added a detail (that Mu'adh prayed 'Isha' with the Prophet and then led his people in the same prayer as supererogatory for him). This addition is not found in other versions and contradicts other evidence, so it is rejected.
The addition was considered weak because other narrators would have mentioned it if true.
5
Compare the scholarly positions
The text presents three views: (a) The majority accept the addition even if reconciliation is impossible, resorting to tarjih. (b) Some accept only if reconciliation is possible. (c) Others reject absolutely, including Imam Ahmad in one narration.
The Hanafi view leans toward the first position but with the condition of session multiplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: إذا انفرد الثقة بزيادة في حديث من بين الثقات (فإن تعدد المجلس) وعلم ذلك التعدد (أو جهل (قبل هذا الحديث المشتمل على الزيادة (اتفاقاً) أما في صورة العلم فلأنه يجوز أن يقع في مجلس كذا وفي آخر كذا فيقبل قول الثقة، وأما في الجهل فلجواز التعدد (وإن اتحد) المجلس (وغيره) أي غير هذا الثقة بحيث لا يغفل عن مثلها عادة) لكمال اعتنائه بها (لم يقبل) ويحمل على وهم الثقة أو الخطأ في فهم المراد ونقله بالمعنى كذلك (وهو الممنوع من الشذوذ والشاذ المطلق ما انفرد به الثقة من بين الثقات ومثله أنه روى البخاري وغيره عن جابر أن معاذ بن جبل كان يصلي مع النبي ، ثم يأتي قومه فيصلي بهم، وقد روى الشافعي : كان معاذ بن جبل يصلي مع النبي الله العشاء ثم ينطلق فيصليها بهم، فهي له تطوع ولهم فريضة، وقد تفرد بهذه الزيادة، ولو كانت لعرفها غيره لأنه موضع الخلاف، وأحق بالتفتيش حتى قيل : إنه من كلام الشافعي في تأويل الحديث، مع أنه ثبت ما ينافي هذه الرواية على ما رواه أحمد عن سليم أنه أتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : يا رسول الله : إن معاذ بن جبل يأتينا بعدما ننام ونكون في أعمالنا بالنهار فينادي بالصلاة، فنخرج فيطوّل علينا، فقال له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : يا معاذ لا تكن فتاناً، إما أن تصلي معي، وإما أن تخفف على قومك (وإلا) أي وإن لم تكن بحيث لو كانت لا يغفل غيره (فالجمهور) يقولون : (يقبل ولو تعذر الجمع) بحيث يكون معارضاً (فالمصير إلى الترجيح كما هو سنة التعارض (وقيل) يقبل (إن لم يتعذر) ولا يقبل إن تعذر (وقيل: لا يقبل مطلقاً سواء تعذر الجمع أو لا (وعليه) الإمام أحمد في رواية لنا الراوي (عدل) جازم في روايته غير مكذب (فوجب قبوله) في
Issue: When a trustworthy narrator is alone in an addition in a hadith among other trustworthy narrators: If the session is multiple and that multiplicity is known, or is unknown, this hadith containing the addition is accepted unanimously. As for the case of knowledge, because it is possible that it occurred in one session and another, so the trustworthy narrator's statement is accepted. As for ignorance, because of the possibility of multiplicity. If the session is single and the others (i.e., other than this trustworthy narrator) are such that they would not normally be neglectful of such (an addition) due to their full care of it, then it is not accepted, and it is attributed to the trustworthy narrator's illusion or error in understanding the intended meaning and narrating by meaning likewise. And this is what is prohibited as shudhudh. The absolute shadhdh is what a trustworthy narrator is alone in among other trustworthy narrators. An example is that al-Bukhari and others narrated from Jabir that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray with the Prophet, then come to his people and lead them in prayer. Al-Shafi'i narrated: Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray the 'Isha' with the Prophet, then go and lead them in it, so it is a supererogatory prayer for him and an obligatory one for them. He was alone in this addition, and if it were (authentic), others would have known it because it is a point of disagreement and most deserving of scrutiny, until it was said that it is from al-Shafi'i's words in interpretation of the hadith. Moreover, what contradicts this narration is established according to what Ahmad narrated from Sulaym: that he came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, Mu'adh ibn Jabal comes to us after we have slept and are in our daytime work, and he calls for prayer, so we come out and he lengthens it for us. The Prophet said: O Mu'adh, do not be a cause of fitnah; either pray with me, or lighten (the prayer) for your people. Otherwise, i.e., if it is not such that others would not normally be neglectful, then the majority say: it is accepted even if reconciliation is impossible, such that it becomes contradictory, then one resorts to tarjih as is the method of opposing evidences. And it is said: it is accepted if reconciliation is not impossible, and not accepted if impossible. And it is said: it is not accepted absolutely, whether reconciliation is possible or not. Imam Ahmad is of this view in one narration: the narrator is just, decisive in his narration, not accused of lying, so his statement must be accepted in
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule regarding an addition (ziyada) made by a trustworthy narrator that is not mentioned by other trustworthy narrators. The ruling depends on the session (majlis) of narration. If the narrators were in multiple sessions or the number of sessions is unknown, the addition is accepted unanimously because the different sessions could explain the variation. If the session is single and the other narrators are so meticulous that they would not normally miss such an addition, then the addition is rejected as shadhdh (anomalous), and it is attributed to the narrator's error. The text then gives an example: al-Shafi'i narrated that Mu'adh's prayer with the Prophet was 'Isha', and then he led his people in the same prayer as a supererogatory act for himself and an obligation for them. This addition is not found in other versions, and it is considered weak because it contradicts other evidence (the hadith of Sulaym). The text then presents different scholarly positions: the majority accept the addition even if reconciliation with other narrations is impossible, resorting to tarjih; another view accepts only if reconciliation is possible; a third view rejects absolutely. The passage ends with the view attributed to Imam Ahmad, that the trustworthy narrator's statement must be accepted. Note that the text is cut off at the end of the page, but the rule and its main conditions are clear. This is a key usul principle in evaluating hadith variations within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الشاذ المطلق (ash-shadhdh al-mutlaq): A hadith where a trustworthy narrator is alone in an addition among other trustworthy narrators, and it is rejected if the conditions for acceptance are not met.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat ath-thiqah): An addition made by a trustworthy narrator in a hadith that is not found in the versions of other trustworthy narrators.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session in which the hadith was narrated; the number of sessions (multiple or single) is a key factor in the rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rule presented, under what condition is the solitary addition of a trustworthy narrator rejected?
A) Always, because it is a solitary narration.
B) When the session is single and the other narrators are so attentive that they would normally not miss such an addition.
C) When the addition contradicts the Quran.
D) When the narrator is not a companion.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a solitary addition by a trustworthy narrator depends on the narration session: if multiple/unknown, accept; if single, reject only if other reliable narrators would not have missed it.

The Hanafi Rule on Ziyadat al-Thiqa and Its Application to Khiyar al-Majlis
Discusses the rule for accepting a trustworthy narrator's additional report when others omit it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for accepting a trustworthy narrator's additional report (ziyadat al-thiqa) and apply it to the hadith of khiyar al-majlis, distinguishing between cases where omission is plausible and where it is not.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's addition is accepted unless omission is so frequent that it would be improbable; Hanafis assume omission (hadhf) in the khiyar al-majlis hadith.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut, the author explores one of the most nuanced debates in usul al-fiqh: whether a trustworthy narrator's additional report should be accepted when other trustworthy narrators omit it. The Hanafi school develops a nuanced rule—the addition is accepted unless the omission is so frequent that it would be improbable for all to forget. The author then applies this rule to a famous example: the hadith of khiyar al-majlis narrated by Ibn Mas'ud, showing how the Hanafis reconcile two versions of the report by assuming deliberate omission (hadhf) rather than using the principle of carrying absolute to restricted. This lesson will guide you through the rule, its justification, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What is the dispute about? The acceptance of ziyadat al-thiqa when others omit it. The opposing view rejects it absolutely; the Hanafis accept it conditionally.
Note the two extreme positions: absolute rejection vs. conditional acceptance.
2
Analyze the Hanafi justification
Why does forgetfulness excuse the isolation of the addition? The passage argues that forgetfulness is common, so isolation does not prove error. Examine the counterargument and the author's response.
The author refines: if the addition is something that would not be overlooked, then the isolation is problematic.
3
Distinguish key technical terms
The passage defines isnad, raf', wasl, irsal, waqf, and qat'. Understand that irsal is not automatically a jarh because it lacks the knowledge that an isnad provides.
This distinction clarifies why the Hanafis treat irsal differently from a direct impugnment.
4
Derive the general rule
The rule: if a trustworthy narrator reports an addition sometimes and omits it other times, if the sessions differ, the addition is accepted absolutely. If the session is the same, the frequency of omission matters: if the omission is so frequent that it would not be overlooked, the addition is rejected; otherwise accepted. If the narrator admits error in omission, it is accepted absolutely.
5
Apply the rule to the Hanafi case study
The Hanafis had two versions of Ibn Mas'ud's hadith on khiyar al-majlis. They assumed the shorter version is a case of deliberate omission (hadhf) because the context of 'tarada' implies the commodity's presence. Show why they did not use haml al-mutlaq 'ala al-muqayyad.
The cause (sabab) of the ruling is the dispute itself, and the condition is part of the cause, so haml is not applicable.
