بعد حين لقاؤه أبا هريرة فيذكر قولهما فقال : إنهما أعلم مني وأنا لم أسمعه من النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وسمعته من الفضل بن عباس فرجع أبو هريرة عما كان يقوله : وفي هذا ليس رد أم المؤمنين على أبي هريرة ولا يعرف له إسناد والذي يفهم إنه لم يكن سمعه من غير واسطة، وقد تعارض عنده خبراً واحداً فرجح بأعلمية أمي المؤمنين، والحق ما قال الخطابي أنه منسوخ وما في الحاشية» إن أم المؤمنين إنما ردت لمخالفة الكتاب، فشجرة نبتت على الأصل الموهون. فإن الرد لم يثبت وإنما روت فعله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، والكتاب هو قوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَتُ إِلَى نِسابكم ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] وقد مر وروی) ابن عباس : لا ربا إلا في النسيئة وأحل به التفاضل في الصرف (ثم قال سمعته من بن زيد ورجع عما كان يفتي به بخبر أبي سعيد، ولو كان سمعه هو لما ساغ له الرجوع

بخبر الواحد المفيد للظن عند معارضة المقطوع بالسماع وما ورد في بعض الروايات عنه مرفوعاً فمعناه منسوباً إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وإن كان بالإرسال (وقال البراء بن عازب ما كل ما نحدثه سمعناه من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم ، وإنما حدثناه عنه لكنا لا نكذب في التحديث (وإرسال الأئمة من التابعين، كالحسن و سعيد بن المسيب و) عامر (الشعبي) وإبراهيم النخعي وغيرهم، وكان ذلك) أي التحديث على سبيل الإرسال ( معروفاً) بينهم (مستمراً) من قرن الصحابة إلى التابعين (بلا نكير) أحد من الأئمة ( فكان) ذلك ( إجماعاً) على قبول المراسيل ولا يذهب عليك السكوت عن إرسال الصحابة، فإن قبوله متفق عليه لا يصلح حجة في المتنازع فيه، ولعل مقصوده أن الإرسال صنع جرى من وقت الصحابة إلى القرون التي بعدها وقبل الكل ولم يتركوا المرسل (وأجيب بإنكار) محمد بن سیرین قدس سره، وهو من كبار التابعين فلا إجماع (قال : لا نأخذ بمراسيل الحسن وأبي العالية فإنهما لا يباليان عمن أخذا الحديث، وفيه) أي في الجواب (ما فيه) فإن غايته ما لزم من قول ابن سيرين عدم قبول مراسيل الحسن وأبي العالية خصوصاً بسبب مختص لا عدم قبول مطلق المراسيل، فلا يضر الإجماع أصلاً، ثم إنه لا يتم قوله أيضاً، فإن غاية ما قال عدم المبالاة في أخذ الحديث لا عدم المبالاة في روايته، وإيجاب العمل بها، وهما شارطان فيها العدالة وسائر الشرائط، فهما وإن لم يباليا في الأخذ فهما لا يرويان إلا عن العدل، ولا يرسلان إلا إذا كان مثل الشمس على نصف النهار كما تقدم قوله قدس سره فافهم (الأكثر) استدلوا (أولاً) بما استدل به للمختار (ولا يفيدهم) الاستدلال (تعميماً) حتى تقبل مرسلات غير الأئمة أيضاً، فلا يفيد مدعاهم واستدلالهم بهذه الاستدلالات يرشدك على أن مقصودهم قبول المرسل من الأئمة ذوي البصيرة (و) استدلوا (ثانياً بأن رواية الآحاد (توثيق له، والمرسل رواية العدل عن ثقة فيكون حجة ودفع بأن ذلك) أي كون رواية العدل توثيقاً له في الجاهل ممنوع ، لأن مطابقة جزمه) للواقع (غير ظاهر) بل احتمال الخطأ قائم، نعم رواية العدل توثيق في زعمه وهو لا يفيد وإنما يفيد، لو كان العدل الراوي ذا بصيرة وعلم وحينئذ لا نزاع، وقد عرفت أن مقصود الأكثر لا يتجاوز عنه .

المنكرون (قالوا: أوّلاً في المرسل جهل ذات الراوي و(جهل الذات مستلزم لجهل الصفات) فتكون صفاته من العدالة والضبط ،مجهولة ورواية المجهول غير مقبولة (قلنا) استلزام جهل الذات لجهل الصفات ممنوع ، فإن تحديث أئمة الشأن عنه (دليل العلم) بصفاته، فالذات وإن كانت مجهولة لكن كونه ثقة معلوم (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو قبل المرسل (لقبل في عصرنا أيضاً للاشتراك في علة القبول (قلنا بطلان اللازم ممنوع في (الأئمة الماهرين بشرائط القبول (على أن فساد الزمان) بفشو الكذب وكثرة) الوسائط المتعسر معرفة أحوالها (مريب) في مطابقة جزم المرسل، بخلاف تلك الأعصار لقلة الوسائط وصلاح الزمان فافترقا، فالملازمة ممنوعة فتأمل (و) قالوا :(ثالثاً : لو جاز قبول المرسل (لما أفاد الإسناد بل يكون تطويلاً من غير فائدة لتساوي الإرسال والإسناد والتالي باطل لاشتغال الأئمة الأعلام به قلنا : الملازمة ممنوعة فإنه يفيد تفاوت الرتب فإن رتبة المسند أعلى من رتبة المرسل فإن الإسناد عزيمة، والإرسال رخصة (و) يفيد (الاتفاق على قبوله للاختلاف في قبول المراسيل، وفي الإسناد تفصيل والتفصيل أقوى من الإجمال، ولهذا أي لأجل أن المسند أقوى لا يجوز النسخ) أي نسخ المسند (عندنا) معشر من يقبل المرسل (بالمراسيل لئلا يلزم إبطال الأقوى بالأدنى، فإن قلت : كيف يكون المسند أقوى وقد صح عن تاج المحدثين ما صح من قوّة المرسل، فلا بد من كونه أقوى من المسند لكونه متواتراً، وهو مقدم على المسند؟ قلت : هذا نادر جداً قلنا يوجد إن وجد فهو في إرسال هذا الخبر لا غير. ثم كونه متواتراً عند المرسل لا يفيد، فإن الكلام فيمن عنه مرسلاً فهو عنده من الآحاد بعد لكونه خبر الواحد المرسل لما مر أن شرط التواتر مساواة ،الطبقات، لكن على هذا يلزم تعارض المسند ،والمرسل، وعدم ثبوت القوة من جهة الإسناد والجواب هو الأول، ويلزم مساواة مرسل هذا الخبر للمسند ولا يضر فيه ومن ههنا ظهر لك جواب آخر هو أن الملازمة ممنوعة فإن فائدة الإسناد الإحالة من أسند عنه، وقلما يوجد الاطمئنان الشديد على الراوي بحيث ينسب الورع التقي خبره إلى الجناب المقدس صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه. قال الشافعي: إن لم يكن معه عاضد لم يحصل الظن لجهالة المروي عنه، فلا يكون حجة إلا بالعاضد (قلنا) عدم حصول الظن من عاضد (ممنوع) بل اعتماد الإمام الثقة مفيد للظن (أقول : على أن قول الصحابي عنده كقول المجتهد) وهو لا يكون عاضداً فكذا قول الصحابي (فالفرق بين الاعتضاد بقول الصحابي والاعتضاد بقول مجتهد آخر (تحكم وفيه ما فيه فإن لقول الصحابي مزية لاحتمال السماع، كذا في «الحاشية»، وهذا العذر غير صحيح، فإنه رحمه الله تعالى أهدر هذا الاحتمال، حتى قال : كيف أتمسك بقول من لو كنت في عصره لحاججته، فلا فرق مع أنه يرد عليه أن قول أكثر العلماء ليس حجة كقول واحد فلا اعتضاد به ولا يجري فيه هذا الجواب، إذ لا احتمال للسماع هناك اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن للجماعة مزية فقولهم يقوي المرسل ويفيد صحته (وقد أخذ عليه بأن ضم غير المسند إلى مثله (ضم غير مقبول إلى مثله) فلا اعتضاد للمرسل بإرسال آخر وهل هذا إلا كما ضم ضعيف بالفسق إلى آخر (وفي المسند العمل به) دون
After a while, he met Abu Hurayra and mentioned their statement, so he said: 'They are more knowledgeable than I, and I did not hear it from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) and heard it from al-Fadl ibn 'Abbas.' So Abu Hurayra retracted what he used to say. In this, there is no refutation of the Mother of the Believers against Abu Hurayra, nor is a chain known for it. What is understood is that he had not heard it without an intermediary. A single report contradicted in his view, so he gave preference based on the superior knowledge of the two Mothers of the Believers. The truth is what al-Khattabi said: that it is abrogated. And what is in the marginalia: 'The Mother of the Believers only rejected it because it contradicted the Book.' So a tree grew on a weak foundation. Indeed, the rejection was not established; rather, she narrated his action (peace be upon him and his family and companions). The Book is His statement: 'Permitted to you on the night of fasting is intimacy with your wives' [al-Baqarah 2:187], and it has passed. And Ibn 'Abbas narrated: 'There is no riba except in nasi'ah,' and he permitted excess in currency exchange. Then he said: 'I heard it from Ibn Zayd' and retracted what he used to give fatwa with based on the report of Abu Sa'id. If he had heard it himself, it would not have been permissible for him to retract, by a single report that yields probability when it contradicts what is definitively heard. And what is narrated in some reports from him as marfu' is meant as attributed to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) even if it is by irsal. And al-Bara' ibn 'Azib said: 'Not everything we narrate did we hear from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions); rather, we narrate it from him, but we do not lie in narration.' And the irsal of the imams among the tabi'un, like al-Hasan, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, 'Amir al-Sha'bi, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and others. And that (i.e., narrating by way of irsal) was well-known among them and continuous from the generation of the Companions to the tabi'un, without any denier among the imams. Thus it was a consensus on accepting the marasil. And do not be misled by the silence about the irsal of the Companions, for its acceptance is agreed upon and does not serve as proof in the disputed matter. Perhaps his intent is that irsal was a practice that occurred from the time of the Companions to the subsequent centuries, and everyone accepted it, and they did not abandon the mursal. And it was answered by the denial of Muhammad ibn Sirin (may God sanctify his secret), who was among the major tabi'un, so there is no consensus. He said: 'We do not accept the marasil of al-Hasan and Abu al-'Aliyah, for they do not care from whom they take hadith.' In this answer, there is something. For its utmost implication is that Ibn Sirin's statement entails non-acceptance of the marasil of al-Hasan and Abu al-'Aliyah specifically due to a particular reason, not absolute non-acceptance of all marasil. Thus it does not harm the consensus at all. Moreover, his statement is not complete, for the utmost he said is that they do not care in taking hadith, not that they do not care in narrating it and requiring action upon it. And both conditions require justice and other conditions. So even if they did not care in taking, they only narrate from a just person and only send (irsal) when it is like the sun at midday, as his statement (may God sanctify his secret) previously indicated. So understand. The majority argued: First, with what was argued for the chosen view, but that argument does not give them generality so that the marasil of non-imams are also accepted. Thus it does not support their claim. And their argument with these evidences indicates that their intent is acceptance of the mursal from the imams of insight. And second: That narrating a single report is a tawthiq (declaration of reliability) for him, and the mursal is a narration by a just person from a trustworthy person, so it is proof. It was refuted: That a just person's narration is a tawthiq for him — regarding the unknown person, it is denied because his certainty matching reality is not apparent; rather, the possibility of error exists. Yes, a just person's narration is a tawthiq in his opinion, and that does not benefit; it would only benefit if the just narrator had insight and knowledge. Then there is no dispute, and you have known that the intent of the majority does not exceed that. The deniers said: First: In the mursal, there is ignorance of the narrator's identity, and ignorance of identity necessarily implies ignorance of attributes, so his attributes of justice and precision are unknown, and the narration of an unknown person is not accepted. We said: The implication of ignorance of identity for ignorance of attributes is denied, for the fact that the imams of the field narrate from him is evidence of knowledge of his attributes. So even if the identity is unknown, his being trustworthy is known. And they said: Second: If the mursal were accepted, it would be accepted in our time as well due to the shared cause of acceptance. We said: The invalidity of the consequent is denied regarding the expert imams who fulfill the conditions of acceptance. Moreover, the corruption of the time (due to the prevalence of lies and the multitude of intermediaries whose conditions are difficult to ascertain) is suspicious regarding the certainty of the mursal reporter, unlike those eras due to the few intermediaries and the righteousness of the time. So they differ, thus the implication is denied. So reflect. And they said: Third: If acceptance of the mursal were permissible, then isnad would be useless, and it would be a prolongation without benefit, since irsal and isnad would be equal. The consequent is false because the eminent imams occupied themselves with it. We said: The implication is denied, for it yields a difference in rank: the rank of the musnad is higher than the rank of the mursal, for isnad is an 'azimah (determined obligation) and irsal is a rukhsa (concession). And it yields agreement on its acceptance due to the difference over accepting marasil, while in isnad there is detail, and detail is stronger than generalization. For this reason (that the musnad is stronger), it is not permissible to abrogate the musnad by marasil according to us — the group that accepts the mursal — lest it entail abrogating the stronger by the weaker. If you say: How can the musnad be stronger when it has been authentically reported from the Crown of the Hadith Scholars what is authentically reported about the strength of the mursal? So the mursal must be stronger than the musnad due to being mutawatir, and it is given precedence over the musnad. I say: This is very rare, and if it exists, it is in the irsal of this specific report only. Moreover, its being mutawatir according to the one who sends it (as mursal) does not benefit, for the discussion is about the one from whom he narrates as mursal; it remains, in his view, from the ahad after being a single mursal report, because the condition of tawatur is equality of the levels. But based on this, it would entail contradiction between the musnad and the mursal, and the lack of proven strength from the aspect of isnad. The answer is the first. And it entails equality of this mursal report with the musnad, and that does not harm. From here, another answer becomes apparent to you: that the implication is denied, for the benefit of isnad is to refer from the one who is cited, and rarely is there extreme confidence in a narrator such that the pious, God-fearing person attributes his report to the sacred presence (may the blessings and peace of God be upon him and his family and companions). Al-Shafi'i said: If there is no supporting evidence (with him), probability does not arise due to ignorance of the one narrated from, so it is not proof except with supporting evidence. We said: The lack of probability arising from supporting evidence is denied; rather, reliance on a trustworthy imam yields probability. I say: Moreover, the statement of a Companion according to him is like the statement of a mujtahid, and that does not serve as supporting evidence, so likewise the statement of a Companion. So the distinction between being supported by the statement of a Companion and being supported by the statement of another mujtahid is arbitrary. And there is something in it, for the statement of a Companion has the advantage of possibility of having heard (directly). This is from the marginalia. And this excuse is not correct, for he (may God have mercy on him) disregarded this possibility, even saying: 'How can I hold to the statement of someone with whom I would have argued had I been in his time?' So there is no distinction. Moreover, it is objected to him that the statement of most scholars is not proof like the statement of one, so there is no support by it, and this answer does not apply there since there is no possibility of hearing there. Unless it is said: The group has an advantage, so their statement strengthens the mursal and yields its authenticity. And it has been objected to him that joining a non-musnad to its like is joining an unacceptable to its like, so there is no support for the mursal by another mursal. Is this not like joining a person weak due to sin to another? And in the musnad, action is taken upon it, while not upon it.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute regarding the acceptance of mursal hadith (a hadith with a missing link in the chain of narrators). The author presents the arguments of the majority (al-akthar) who accept mursal from reliable imams, and the deniers (al-munkirun) who reject it. The passage begins with an example of Abu Hurayra retracting a ruling based on a report from two ladies, which illustrates the principle of preferring a stronger source. Then the discussion focuses on the practice of the tabi'un sending mursal reports, with the claim that this was a continuous practice from the Companions onward, implying consensus. However, Muhammad ibn Sirin's objection is raised, but the author shows that his objection is limited to specific individuals. The majority then argue that narrating a single report from a just person is a form of tawthiq (declaring reliability), making the mursal proof. The deniers counter with three arguments: 1) ignorance of the narrator's identity leads to ignorance of his attributes, so the narration is rejected; 2) if mursal were accepted in early times, it should be accepted in later times too, but the author refutes by distinguishing eras; 3) if mursal is accepted, isnad becomes useless, but the author explains that isnad has a higher rank and is an 'azimah, while irsal is a rukhsa, and there is a difference in strength. The passage also addresses the possibility of a mursal being mutawatir (mass transmitted) but notes this is rare. The author then discusses the need for supporting evidence ('idad) as per al-Shafi'i's view, but argues that reliance on a trustworthy imam suffices for probability. Finally, the author compares the statement of a Companion to that of a mujtahid, noting that a Companion's statement has the advantage of possible direct hearing, but this is debated. The Hanafi position, as presented by the author, is that mursal from reliable imams is accepted and is a valid proof, though not as strong as musnad.

Key Terms
جهل الذات (jahalat al-dhat): Ignorance of the narrator's specific identity (name, person)
العزيمة والرخصة (al-'azimah wa al-rukhsa): 'Azimah is the stronger, determined obligation; rukhsa is a concession. Here, isnad is 'azimah and irsal is rukhsa.
العاضد (al-'adid): Supporting evidence that strengthens a weak report. Al-Shafi'i requires a 'adid for mursal to be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why is the deniers' first objection (ignorance of narrator's identity) not a valid reason to reject a mursal?
A) Because identity is not important for hadith acceptance
B) Because the imams' practice of narrating from the person provides knowledge of his trustworthiness
C) Because the narrator's identity can always be discovered later
D) Because the deniers are mistaken about the definition of mursal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school successfully rebuts the three main objections to mursal by employing principles of tawthiq, historical context, and rank differentiation.

Debate on Acceptance of Mursal Hadith
Dispute on whether mursal hadith is acceptable as proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi justification for accepting mursal hadith from a trustworthy source and evaluate the Shafi'i requirement of supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept mursal if the sender is reliable; Shafi'is require external corroboration.

This lesson dives into a classic usul dispute: can a hadith with a missing link (mursal) still be used as proof? The Hanafi school says yes, under certain conditions, while the Shafi'i school demands extra evidence. As you read the source, watch how each side builds its argument from principles of narration and trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether a mursal hadith (where a Successor omits the Companion) is a valid proof (hujja).
2
Examine the three objections
The Shafi'i camp raises three arguments: ignorance of the narrator, inconsistency across eras, and redundancy of isnad. List each.
These objections are stated and then answered.
3
Follow the Hanafi responses
For each objection, see how the Hanafi side refutes it—especially the claim that imams' narration proves trustworthiness, and the contextual difference between early and later times.
4
Analyze the debate on supporting evidence
Al-Shafi'i insists on a ‘supporting evidence’ (عاضد). The Hanafi says reliance on a trustworthy imam itself produces probability. Examine the exchange about the Companion's saying and the role of multiple mursal chains.
5
Note the subsidiary ruling
The text ends with a distinction: saying ‘a man’ without identification is not accepted, while ‘a trustworthy man’ or ‘a Companion’ is accepted.
This clarifies the boundary of the Hanafi position.

المنكرون (قالوا: أوّلاً في المرسل جهل ذات الراوي و(جهل الذات مستلزم لجهل الصفات) فتكون صفاته من العدالة والضبط ،مجهولة ورواية المجهول غير مقبولة (قلنا) استلزام جهل الذات لجهل الصفات ممنوع ، فإن تحديث النسخ) أي نسخ المسند (عندنا) معشر من يقبل المرسل (بالمراسيل لئلا يلزم إبطال الأقوى بالأدنى، فإن قلت : كيف يكون المسند أقوى وقد صح عن تاج المحدثين ما صح من قوّة المرسل، فلا بد من كونه أقوى من المسند لكونه متواتراً، وهو مقدم على المسند؟ قلت : هذا نادر جداً قلنا يوجد إن وجد فهو في إرسال هذا الخبر لا غير. ثم كونه متواتراً عند المرسل لا يفيد، فإن الكلام فيمن عنه مرسلاً فهو عنده من الآحاد بعد لكونه خبر الواحد المرسل لما مر أن شرط التواتر مساواة ،الطبقات، لكن على هذا يلزم تعارض المسند ،والمرسل، وعدم ثبوت القوة من جهة الإسناد والجواب هو الأول، ويلزم مساواة مرسل هذا الخبر للمسند ولا يضر فيه ومن ههنا ظهر لك جواب آخر هو أن الملازمة ممنوعة فإن فائدة الإسناد الإحالة من أسند عنه، وقلما يوجد الاطمئنان الشديد على الراوي بحيث ينسب الورع التقي خبره إلى الجناب المقدس صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه. قال الشافعي: إن لم يكن معه عاضد لم يحصل الظن لجهالة المروي عنه، فلا يكون حجة إلا بالعاضد (قلنا) عدم حصول الظن من عاضد (ممنوع) بل اعتماد الإمام الثقة مفيد للظن (أقول : على أن قول الصحابي عنده كقول المجتهد) وهو لا يكون عاضداً فكذا قول الصحابي (فالفرق بين الاعتضاد بقول الصحابي والاعتضاد بقول مجتهد آخر (تحكم وفيه ما فيه فإن لقول الصحابي مزية لاحتمال السماع، كذا في «الحاشية»، وهذا العذر غير صحيح، فإنه رحمه الله تعالى أهدر هذا الاحتمال، حتى قال : كيف أتمسك بقول من لو كنت في عصره لحاججته، فلا فرق مع أنه يرد عليه أن قول أكثر العلماء ليس حجة كقول واحد فلا اعتضاد به ولا يجري فيه هذا الجواب، إذ لا احتمال للسماع هناك اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن للجماعة مزية فقولهم يقوي المرسل ويفيد صحته (وقد أخذ عليه بأن ضم غير المسند إلى مثله (ضم غير مقبول إلى مثله) فلا اعتضاد للمرسل بإرسال آخر وهل هذا إلا كما ضم ضعيف بالفسق إلى آخر (وفي المسند العمل به) دون المرسل فيلغو المرسل من البين، ويبقى المسند معمولاً به فلا يعتضد بالمسند أيضاً (ودفع الأول بأن الظن قد يحصل بالانضمام ألا ترى كثرة طرق الضعيف تخرجه عن الضعف ويتقوّى ظن الصدق فكذا هذا، والحق أن هذا الدفع مجادلة فإن المرسل إنما لا يقبله لجهالة المروي وبانضمام المرسل الآخر لا ترتفع هذه الجهالة، بل لا تزيد على رواية المجهولين في العدالة والحفظ ومن البين أنه لا تصير رواية المجهول العدالة بانضمام مثله حجة فكذا هذا (والثاني، قال ابن الحاجب وارد لا دفع له وأجيب بأنه يعمل به وإن لم تثبت عدالة رواة المسند فلا يلغو المرسل، بل العمل به لكون المسند غير قابل للعمل، وهذا في غاية السقوط، فإن ضم ما فيه ريبة بالجهالة إلى ما فيه قطعاً، فلا يزيل هذا المجهول تلك الريبة، يصير واجب العمل على أن صيرورتهما دليلين تفيد في المعارضة) فإنه يقع الترجيح عنده بكثرة الأدلة فافهم .
(فرع): قال رجل : لا يقبل في المذهب (الصحيح) وليس هذا كالارسال كما نقل عن شمس الأئمة، لأن هذا رواية عن مجهول والإرسال جزم بنسبة المتن : إلى الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهذا لا يكون إلا بالتوثيق فافترقا (بخلاف) قال (ثقة) أو رجل من الصحابة، لأن هذا رواية عن ثقة لأن الصحابة كلهم عدول (ولو) اصطلح على معين معلوم العدالة على التعيين برجل (فلا إشكال في القبول .
The deniers said: First, in the mursal, there is ignorance of the identity of the narrator, and ignorance of identity necessitates ignorance of attributes. Thus his attributes of integrity and precision are unknown, and the narration of an unknown person is not accepted. We said: The claim that ignorance of identity necessitates ignorance of attributes is not conceded, for the fact that leading imams narrate from him is evidence of knowledge of his attributes. So even if his identity is unknown, his being trustworthy is known. They said: Secondly, if the mursal were accepted, it would be accepted in our time as well due to the shared cause of acceptance. We said: The falsity of the consequent is not conceded concerning the imams skilled in the conditions of acceptance. Moreover, the corruption of the times through widespread lying and the multitude of intermediaries whose states are difficult to ascertain makes the correspondence of the mursal's certainty suspect, unlike those earlier ages due to the few intermediaries and the righteousness of the times, so they differ. Thus the implication is not conceded, so reflect. They said: Thirdly, if accepting the mursal were permissible, then isnad would be useless and would be a lengthy procedure without benefit, since sending and chaining would be equal. The consequent is false because the eminent imams occupied themselves with it. We said: The implication is not conceded, for it yields a difference in ranks: the rank of the musnad is higher than the rank of the mursal, because isnad is a determined duty while irsal is a concession. It also yields agreement on its acceptance due to disagreement on accepting mursals, while in isnad there is detail, and detail is stronger than generality. For this reason, i.e., because the musnad is stronger, abrogation of the musnad by mursals is not permissible according to us who accept the mursal, lest it lead to replacing the stronger with the weaker. If you say: How can the musnad be stronger when it is authentically reported from the Crown of Traditionists what is authentically reported of the strength of the mursal, so it must be stronger than the musnad because it is mutawatir, and it is given precedence over the musnad? I say: This is extremely rare. If it exists, it is solely in the sending of this report. Then its being mutawatir according to the one who sends it is not beneficial, for the discussion concerns the one from whom it is sent as a mursal; to him it is still ahad because it is a khabar wahid mursal, since the condition for tawatur is equality of levels. But on this, contradiction between the musnad and the mursal would arise, and lack of proof of strength from the aspect of isnad. The answer is the first. And the equality of this mursal report with the musnad is required, and it does not harm. From here another answer appears to you: the implication is not conceded, for the benefit of isnad is to refer to the one from whom it is chained, and rarely is there complete reliance on a narrator such that the pious, God-fearing person attributes his report to the sacred presence (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions). Al-Shafi'i said: If there is no supporting evidence with it, it does not produce probability due to ignorance of the one reported from, so it is not a proof except with supporting evidence. We said: The lack of probability from supporting evidence is not conceded; rather, reliance on a trustworthy imam is beneficial for probability. I say: According to him, the saying of a Companion is like the saying of a mujtahid, and it is not supporting evidence, so likewise the saying of a Companion. The distinction between seeking support from the saying of a Companion and seeking support from the saying of another mujtahid is arbitrary, and there is something in it. For the saying of a Companion has an advantage due to the possibility of hearing, as in the gloss. This excuse is not sound, for he (al-Shafi'i) dismissed this possibility, even saying: How can I hold on to the saying of one whom, if I were in his time, I would argue with? So there is no difference. Moreover, it is objected to him that the saying of the majority of scholars is not a proof like the saying of a single one, so there is no support in it, and this answer does not apply there, since there is no possibility of hearing there. However, it could be said: The group has an advantage, so their saying strengthens the mursal and gives it correctness. It was objected to him that joining a non-musnad to its like is joining something unacceptable to its like, so there is no support for the mursal by another mursal. Is this not like joining a weak person due to sin to another? The musnad is acted upon without the mursal, so the mursal becomes void and the musnad remains acted upon, so it is not supported by the musnad either. The first objection is repelled by saying that probability may occur through joining; do you not see that many chains of a weak report remove its weakness and strengthen the probability of truth? So likewise here. The truth is that this response is merely polemical, for the mursal is rejected only due to ignorance of the one reported from, and by joining another mursal this ignorance is not removed; it is no more than the narration of two unknown persons in integrity and memory, and it is clear that the narration of a person unknown in integrity does not become a proof by joining its like, so likewise this. The second objection was stated by Ibn al-Hajib as irrefutable. It was answered that it is acted upon even if the integrity of the narrators of the musnad is not established, so the mursal does not become void; rather, it is acted upon because the musnad is not fit to be acted upon. This answer is extremely weak, for joining something suspicious due to ignorance to something certain does not remove that suspicion; it becomes obligatory to act upon it? However, their being two proofs is beneficial in opposition, for preference occurs by multiplicity of proofs, so understand. (Subsidiary issue): A man said: It is not accepted in the (correct) school, and this is not like mursal, as transmitted from Shams al-A'imma, because this is a narration from an unknown person, while mursal is a definitive attribution of the text to the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and Companions), and this is only with documentation, so they differ. Unlike saying: ‘a trustworthy person’ or ‘a man from the Companions’ because this is a narration from a trustworthy person, for all Companions are upright. If they agree on a specific person known for uprightness by naming him as ‘a man’ there is no issue in acceptance.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute concerning the acceptance of mursal hadith (a hadith where a Successor directly attributes a statement to the Prophet, omitting the Companion). The opponents (likely Shafi'is and others) raise three objections: (1) The narrator of the mursal is unknown, so his reliability is unknown, hence the hadith is unacceptable; (2) If mursal were accepted in the past, it should be accepted today too, but today it is not accepted due to corruption of the times; (3) If mursal were acceptable, then isnad would be pointless. The Hanafi responder answers each: (1) The very fact that leading imams narrate from him shows they knew him to be trustworthy; ignorance of his name does not equal ignorance of his trustworthiness. (2) The times are different: earlier ages had fewer intermediaries and more righteousness, so mursal from that period is reliable; today's corruption makes it unreliable. (3) Isnad has value because it gives a higher rank to the musnad chain; mursal is a concession, not equal. The Hanafi school holds that mursal from a trustworthy Successor is acceptable, but it is weaker than musnad. The discussion also covers al-Shafi'i's requirement of a 'supporting evidence' (عاضد) for mursal to be considered a proof. The commentator refutes this by stating that reliance on a trustworthy imam itself produces probability. The subsidiary issue distinguishes between saying 'a man' without identification (which is not accepted) and saying 'a trustworthy man' or 'a Companion' (which is accepted because all Companions are upright). This shows the Hanafi position that mursal is accepted when the sender is reliable, but absolute anonymity is not acceptable.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where a Successor narrates directly from the Prophet without mentioning the Companion.
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a continuous chain of narration back to the Prophet.
تواتر (tawatur): A transmission by a large number of narrators at each level, making knowledge certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the mursal from earlier ages acceptable even though the narrator's identity may be unknown?
A) Because the Successor is always a Companion.
B) Because the leading imams' narration from him indicates his trustworthiness.
C) Because all mursal hadith are mutawatir.
D) Because the opponents have no valid objection.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts mursal hadith from a trustworthy Successor because the imams' acceptance proves reliability, and the musnad's higher rank is preserved by not allowing abrogation by mursal.

Conflict Between Hadith and Qiyas: Precedence of Khabar
Stating the majority view that hadith is preferred over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the conflict between khabar and qiyas, identify the conditions for hadith to be preferred, and evaluate the differing views of other scholars.

Core Idea
A clear hadith is preferred over qiyas because it is direct revelation.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational rule of Hanafi usul: when a single-narrator hadith (khabar wahid) and analogical reasoning (qiyas) conflict and cannot be reconciled, which takes precedence? The majority of scholars, including the three great Imams, hold that the hadith is absolutely preferred. However, there are nuances regarding the clarity of the hadith and the reliability of the narrator. This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' lays out the consensus and the differing opinions, and it is essential for understanding the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict scenario
Understand when a khabar and qiyas conflict such that reconciliation (jam') is impossible. The text mentions cases where both are specific (khass) with no indication of figurativeness, or both are general ('amm) and equal, etc.
If reconciliation is possible, tarjih is not needed.
2
State the majority view
The majority (including Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the hadith is preferred absolutely. However, note the qualifier: the hadith must be clear in indication (مُتَّضِحُ الدَّلَالَةِ), not problematic (mushkil) or ambiguous (mujmal).
This is the Hanafi position.
3
Explore the dissenting views
Some scholars, like Imam Malik (attributed), hold that qiyas is always preferred. Others, like Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili, distinguish based on certainty of the 'illa. Isa ibn Aban adds a condition regarding narrator precision.
These are minority views.
4
Understand the Hanafi qualifiers
The Hanafi view is not absolute; the hadith must be from a reliable narrator. If the narrator is careless (mutasahil), then the status of the hadith is examined; if still authentic, hadith is preferred, otherwise qiyas. Also, if the narrator is a mujtahid Companion, hadith is even stronger.
This explains the intended meaning of the three Imams.
5
Apply the rule
In practice, when a clear, authentic hadith exists on a matter, it overrides analogical reasoning. For example, the hadith 'The prayer of one who passes by a person praying is not valid' would override qiyas that says the person passing does not invalidate the prayer.
This is a common application in Hanafi fiqh.

مسألة: إذا تعارض الخبر والقياس وتعذر الجمع بين خبر الواحد والقياس) كأن يكونا خاصين ولا قرينة على التجوز أو عامين مساويين ونحوهما (فالإجماع على تقديم أرجح الظنين الحاصلين منهما (لكن) الخلاف في أن أي الظنين أرجح فقال (الأكثر) من أهل الأصول (ومنهم الأئمة (الثلاثة الإمام الهمام أبو حنيفة والإمام الشافعي والإمام أحمد رضوان الله تعالى عليهم والصاحبان أبو يوسف ومحمد بل جل أصحاب الإمام الأعظم رحمهم (أن ذلك الرجحان (في الخبر مطلقاً لعل المراد بالخبر ما كان متضح الدلالة لا مثل المشكل والمجمل كما لا يخفى (وقيل) الترجيح (في القياس مطلقاً ونسب إلى الإمام مالك و) قال (أبو الحسين المعتزلي : القياس مقدم إن كان ثبوت العلة بقاطع فإن لم يقطع إلا بالأصل) دون ثبوت العلة ووجوده في الفرع فالاجتهاد في الترجيح يعني ليس ترجيح أحدهما حتماً، بل قد يكون الخبر مرجحاً، وقد يكون القياس مرجحاً ويعلم هذا بالاجتهاد فيوكل إليه (وإلا) أي وإن لم يقطع بثبوت العلة ولا بالأصل فالخبر ) راجح (و) قال (عيسى بن أبان) منا (إن كان الراوي ضابطاً غير متساهل فالخبر راجح وإلا فموضع الاجتهاد والحاصل أن الخبر راجح البتة، إلا إذا وجد في الراوي نوع من التساهل فننظر إن كان هذا التساهل لا يضر في صحة الخبر أو حسنه، فالخبر وإلا فالقياس، وهذا في الحقيقة تبيين مراد ما عن الأئمة الثلاثة لا مذهب آخر (و) قال الإمام فخر الإسلام إن كان الراوي من المجتهدين كالأربعة) الخلفاء الراشدين ( والعبادلة) في «الحاشية) : العبادلة : ابن عباس وابن عمر وابن الزبير وابن عمرو بن العاص، وليس منهم ابن مسعود وقد غلط الجوهري كذا في القاموس»، أقول: هذا عند
Issue: If a hadith and qiyas conflict, and it is impossible to reconcile between a khabar wahid and qiyas, such as when both are specific and there is no indication of figurative interpretation, or both are general and equal, and the like, then there is consensus on giving precedence to the more probable of the two probabilities obtained from them. However, the disagreement is over which of the two probabilities is more weighty. The majority of usul scholars, including the three imams: the great Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad (may Allah be pleased with them), and the two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), indeed most of the followers of the Grand Imam (may Allah have mercy on them), said that the preference lies in the hadith absolutely. Perhaps what is meant by hadith is that which is clear in indication, not like the problematic and the ambiguous, as is not hidden. It was also said that preference lies in qiyas absolutely, attributed to Imam Malik. Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili said: Qiyas is preferred if the proof of the 'illa is decisive; if only the asl is certain but not the 'illa and its existence in the far', then ijtihad in preference is left to the mujtahid, meaning neither is necessarily preferred; sometimes hadith is preferred, sometimes qiyas, known by ijtihad. If neither the proof of the 'illa nor the asl is certain, then hadith is preferred. Isa ibn Aban (from us) said: If the narrator is precise and not careless, then hadith is preferred; otherwise it is a matter of ijtihad. The gist is that hadith is absolutely preferred, unless there is some carelessness in the narrator; then we look: if this carelessness does not harm the authenticity or good status of the hadith, then hadith (is preferred); otherwise qiyas. This is in reality an explanation of the intended meaning from the three imams, not a separate school. Imam Fakhr al-Islam said: If the narrator is from the mujtahids like the four Rightly Guided Caliphs and the 'Abadilah (in the gloss: the 'Abadilah are Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn al-Zubayr, and Ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As; Ibn Mas'ud is not among them, and al-Jawhari made an error, as in al-Qamus). I say: This is at...
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul rule when a khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) conflicts with qiyas (analogical reasoning) and reconciliation is impossible. All scholars agree that the more probable of the two should be given precedence, but they differ on which is inherently more weighty. The majority—including Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and most Hanafis—hold that the hadith is preferred absolutely, provided it is clear in indication (zahir or nass). Imam Malik is reported to hold that qiyas is preferred absolutely. Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili distinguishes: if the 'illa is established by a decisive proof, qiyas is preferred; if only the asl is certain but not the 'illa, then ijtihad determines preference; if neither is certain, hadith is preferred. Isa ibn Aban (a Hanafi) adds a condition regarding the narrator: if the narrator is precise (ضابط) and not careless, hadith is preferred; otherwise it is subject to ijtihad. The commentator notes that this is essentially the same as the majority view, just making explicit the condition of narrator reliability. Imam Fakhr al-Islam adds that if the narrator is from the mujtahid Companions (like the four caliphs and 'Abadilah), the hadith is obviously preferred due to their high level of reliability. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating continued discussion on the next page (not provided). Overall, the Hanafi position is that khabar, when clear, takes precedence over qiyas, as it is a direct revelation.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report from the Prophet through a single chain (khabar wahid) that is clear in indication.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning to derive a ruling for a new case from an original case due to shared 'illa.
ترجيح (tarjih): Giving precedence to one evidence over another due to greater weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of usul scholars (including Abu Hanifa, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad), which is preferred when a clear hadith conflicts with qiyas?
A) Qiyas is always preferred.
B) Hadith is preferred absolutely.
C) It depends on the strength of the 'illa.
D) Neither is preferred; both are equally valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a clear and authentic hadith takes precedence over analogical reasoning because it is a direct source of revelation.

Al-Sunnah as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Principle: Khabar is Preferred over Qiyas
Establishing the rule and its Companions' evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for preferring khabar over qiyas and identify the exception of 'insidad bab al-ra'y'.

Core Idea
Khabar takes precedence over qiyas, except when no reasonable ijtihad remains—a near-absolute rule.

This lesson examines the foundational Hanafi usul principle that a transmitted report (khabar) is given priority over analogical reasoning (qiyas) when they conflict. We will explore the evidence from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab and the claimed consensus of the Salaf, as well as the nuanced exception for when 'the door of opinion is closed.' Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly weighing sources in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy being established
Recognize that the Hanafi school gives primacy to khabar over qiyas, even if the narrator lacks juristic expertise (fiqaha), except when 'the door of opinion is closed' (insidad bab al-ra'y).
The exception is extremely rare in practice.
2
Understand the condition of the narrator
Note that the narrator's reliability ('adala) is sufficient; fiqaha is not required for the khabar to be preferred, though a non-faqih narrator may raise suspicion when the ruling is clear.
Abu Hurayra is cited as an example; the text clarifies he was actually a faqih.
3
Analyze the exception – insidad bab al-ra'y
When the qiyas is so clear that no valid ijtihad remains, the khabar may be set aside due to suspicion that the narrator misinterpreted. This is based on Imam Fakhr al-Islam's view.
The hadith of musarra (fraudulent sale) is given as an example.
4
Examine the evidence from Umar's practice
Umar abandoned qiyas in three cases (fetus, diya of fingers, wife's inheritance) based on specific hadiths. His statement 'If I had not heard this, I would have judged with our own opinion' directly shows the priority of khabar.
These cases became widely accepted as precedents.
5
Evaluate the claim of consensus
The widespread acceptance of Umar's practice by the Salaf and Khalaf is presented as ijma' on the principle. The objection that this only proves permissibility is rebutted by pointing to the Companions' silence in disputes.
The passage argues that silence implies obligation.

The conclusion of his view is that the khabar is absolutely preferred except that when the door of opinion is closed, suspicion arises in conformity when the narrator is non-faqih, so it is not accepted due to this suspicion. So this also is in reality agreeing with what is from the three Imams. And al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani al-Shafi'i paused. (And the chosen) among some later scholars (if the establishment of the cause is preponderant over the khabar and its existence in the branch is not weak) but remains at the measure it was in the root or is preponderant in it, (then qiyas) is preferred. (And if they are equal) i.e., the establishment of the cause in the root and branch, and the establishment of the khabar, then pause, and neither is given preference over the other. (And otherwise) i.e., if there is neither preponderance nor equality, (then the khabar) is preferred. (For us) according to the chosen of the later scholars: preferment of the preponderant is determined and obligatory, so qiyas is preferred when the establishment of the cause is preponderant, and the khabar is preferred when it is preponderant. (And) preferment (in equality is arbitrary) so one pauses at equality necessarily. Know that this is very clear, and the three Imams do not deny it. How? For preferment of the preponderant is necessary and agreed upon. Rather, the place of dispute is whether such a qiyas exists or not. Their point of view is that it does not exist. So whoever claims the preponderance of qiyas, even in one case, must prove it, and that is extremely difficult. And for the majority, firstly: The Commander of the Faithful (Umar), may Allah be pleased with him, abandoned qiyas regarding the fetus, which is the non-obligation of the ghurra (blood money) like other doubtful matters. Its summary: analogy of destroying the fetus to destroying other matters doubtful in life and existence, (because of the khabar of Hamal ibn Malik that he (peace be upon him and his family and companions) obligated the ghurra in it as previously mentioned, and he said: 'Were it not for this, I would have judged in it with our own opinion.' It was narrated by Abu Dawud, and its wording: 'Allahu Akbar, if I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise,' and in another narration: 'It is a lie that we judge in this with our own opinion.') (And) the Commander of the Faithful Umar abandoned (qiyas regarding the diya of fingers. His opinion was regarding the little finger: six, regarding the ring finger: nine, regarding the middle finger: ten, regarding the index finger: twelve, and in al-Tahrir: ten, and regarding the thumb: fifteen) camels, all of that in al-Taysir. The commentator said: thus mentioned by more than one, but what is in the narration of al-Bayhaqi is that he regarded the index finger as twelve and the middle finger as thirteen. Al-Shafi'i narrated his decree regarding the thumb likewise based on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: for every finger ten camels in the book. (And) the Commander of the Faithful Umar abandoned (qiyas regarding the inheritance of the wife from the blood money of her husband, which indicates non-inheritance, since the husband did not own it so that she would inherit, and the marriage relationship did not remain after death so that it would be established initially through kinship, etc., besides many widespread incidents. And none of the Salaf or Khalaf denied it, so it was a consensus on the preference of khabar. This is very clear for one who studies incidents and histories. I say: If it is said: The necessary implication of what you mentioned is permissibility, i.e., permissibility of acting on khabar, not the obligation of preferring the khabar. We say: Their silence in disputes is evidence of obligation, so understand. And it may be said: Perhaps the school of the Commander of the Faithful was choice when there is conflict, so silence in choosing one of the options does not necessitate obligation. This is nothing, because the context of the story indicates otherwise, and his statement: 'If I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise' is explicit that the preventer from acting on qiyas was the existence of the khabar. Moreover, such cases are many, and what is mentioned are specific examples learned through experience, repetition, and complete induction. So the objection that this only indicates the preference of some khabars over some qiyases, and perhaps the khabar here has strength unlike other khabars, is baseless and not listened to. (And it was objected by the abandonment of Ibn Abbas to the khabar of Abu Hurayra: 'Perform wudu from what is touched by fire.' He said: 'Should we not perform wudu with hot water?' as an addition of the described to the attribute: 'How can we perform wudu with what we perform wudu from?' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, its wording: He said to him: 'O Abu Hurayra, do I perform wudu from oil? Do I perform wudu from hot water?' So Abu Hurayra said: 'O son of my brother, if you hear a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ, do not strike an example for it.') (And) by his abandonment of his khabar: 'Whoever carries a funeral let him perform wudu.' And in another narration: 'Let him perform ghusl.' By this khabar, Imam Ahmad obligated ghusl in one narration. He said: 'Wudu is not required for carrying dry sticks.' (And) by his abandonment of (his khabar about the one who wakes up from his sleep: 'When one of you wakes from his sleep, let him wash his hand before inserting it into the vessel, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' Narrated by the two Shaykhs and others. (And likewise) the Mother of the Believers (Aisha) al-Siddiqa. They said: 'How do we deal with the mihras, which is a huge carved stone that no one can move; water is taken from it by hand or a small vessel and one performs wudu by inserting the hand?' The summary of the response: If this were the case, wudu with the mihras would not be valid. He said in al-Taysir: This is not established from them, rather it is established from a man called Qayn al-Ashja'i, and there is disagreement about his Companionship. And it was answered that their denial was due to the apparentness of the conflict, i.e., the apparentness of its conflict, not for abandoning qiyas. Thus I found the copy, and perhaps it is a scribal error. (And the more apparent: not for abandoning the khabar by qiyas, although it is forced, and it is said that the addition of the source to the subject is of the type 'inbat al-rabi' (spring growth), and the object is understood, and the meaning is that qiyas is not a cause for abandoning the khabar, meaning it is a cause for abandonment such that it would be a proof for you. I say in it an admission of non-preference of khabar when the qiyas is clearer than the khabar, because the apparentness of the opposition is only the apparentness of a clear qiyas understood with minimal reflection. So understand. This is extremely weak, because the summary of the answer is that the denial is because its opposite is clear from the Sharia. For performing wudu with hot water was necessarily known in the religion, and carrying a funeral is a common occurrence from the time of the lawgiver (peace be upon him and his family and companions). So if it necessitated wudu, it would have become widespread, but it is only a matter of dry sticks, and it is necessarily known from the Sharia that it is not an impure event. Similarly, the use of the mihras was well known, so if what was mentioned were true, the mihras would not have been used. So their abandonment of this hadith was due to it falling into a matter of general affliction, and it does not contain an admission of the precedence of qiyas, even if clear, over khabar. So understand. And it is not far-fetched to say: They did not reject the hadith itself, but rather they rejected Abu Hurayra's interpretation of obligating wudu from what is touched by fire and carrying a funeral and the impurity of water by inserting the hand into the vessel, deeming it contrary to the legal principles. Rather, the meaning of 'wudu' in the two hadiths is cleaning, like washing the hand and rinsing the mouth after eating what is touched by fire, and washing the hand and foot from carrying a funeral, and the prohibition of inserting the hand into the vessel is a prohibition of dispraise when possible. (And) for the majority: (Secondly: his, peace be upon him and his family, confirmation).
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul argument for preferring khabar over qiyas when they conflict. It begins by addressing the status of narrators: according to the Hanafi school, even if a narrator is known for reliability ('adala) but not for juristic expertise (fiqaha), like Abu Hurayra (though the text notes that Abu Hurayra actually was a mujtahid), the khabar is still given precedence over qiyas, except when 'the door of opinion is closed'—meaning when the issue is so clear that no reasonable ijtihad remains. This exception is illustrated by the hadith of musarra (a sale with fraud), where qiyas might suggest otherwise but the hadith takes priority.

The author then presents the position of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and later scholars: if the establishment of the legal cause ('illa) is preponderant over the khabar, qiyas is preferred; if equal, pause; if neither, khabar prevails. The Hanafi response is that this is self-evident and the real issue is whether such preponderant qiyas ever exists—they argue it does not.

Evidence is then marshalled from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who abandoned qiyas in three cases: (1) the fetus—he obligated the ghurra based on a hadith despite qiyas suggesting no obligation; (2) diya for fingers—he fixed varying amounts for each finger based on a hadith rather than the qiyas of equal value; (3) inheritance of a wife from her husband's blood money—he gave inheritance based on a hadith despite qiyas suggesting none. The widespread acceptance of these rulings by the Salaf and Khalaf is claimed as ijma' (consensus) on the principle of preferring khabar.

The passage then addresses objections: some argued that these examples only show permissibility, not obligation. The response is that the Companions' silence in these disputes indicates obligation. Others argued that Umar might have been exercising choice, but his explicit statement 'If I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise' shows the khabar was the preventer.

Finally, counterexamples are discussed: Ibn Abbas and Aisha seeming to ignore certain ahādīth. The Hanafi commentator refutes that these were not rejections of the khabar itself but of interpretations that conflicted with clearer principles of the Sharia. The actual rulings from those Companions were based on other considerations, not on preferring qiyas over khabar. Thus the Hanafi position that khabar is always preferred (with the limited exception) remains intact.

Key Terms
الخبر (al-khabar): A report from the Prophet (hadith), whether mutawatir or ahad, used as a source of law.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause ('illa).
الفقاهة (al-fiqaha): Jurisprudential expertise; the ability to deduce rulings independently.
انسداد باب الرأي (insidad bab al-ra'y): The closing of the door of opinion, meaning the situation where the ruling is so clear that no valid ijtihad remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is qiyas theoretically given preference over khabar?
A) When the narrator of the khabar is known for reliability but not for fiqaha.
B) When the establishment of the 'illa is preponderant over the khabar and its existence in the branch is not weak, and the door of opinion is not closed.
C) Never; the khabar is always preferred unconditionally.
D) When the khabar is ahad and the qiyas is jali.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes transmitted reports over analogical reasoning, reserving an exception only for cases where no reasonable ijtihad remains—a scenario that never actually occurs.

Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
10 min
Defending the Preference: Refuting Counterexamples from Ibn Abbas and Aisha
Refuting counterexamples to preserve the rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi response to the apparent contradictions from Ibn Abbas and Aisha and distinguish between rejection of a khabar and rejection of an interpretation.

Core Idea
Apparent conflicts between Companions' actions and narrations are not rejections of the khabar itself but rejections of flawed interpretations.

This lesson continues the defense of the Hanafi principle by addressing specific counterexamples where Companions like Ibn Abbas and Aisha seemed to ignore certain ahādīth. We will see that the Hanafi commentators argue these were not rejections of the narrations but rather rejections of the interpretations that conflicted with clearer principles of the Sharia. This clarifies that the rule of preferring khabar over qiyas remains intact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the counterexamples
Ibn Abbas and Aisha are reported to have acted contrary to specific hadiths: Ibn Abbas regarding wudu from what is touched by fire and carrying a funeral, and Aisha regarding washing hands from a vessel after sleep.
These are presented as objections by opponents of the Hanafi rule.
2
Understand the objection
The opponents argue that these Companions' actions show that qiyas can override khabar, since they apparently ignored the hadiths in favor of other reasoning.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: rejection of interpretation, not the khabar
The Hanafi response is that Ibn Abbas and Aisha did not reject the hadiths themselves; they rejected the interpretation that those hadiths required wudu in those specific situations. They understood the hadiths to refer to cleanliness (tanzih) rather than ritual purity.
The text cites that Abu Hurayra himself told Ibn Abbas not to strike examples for hadiths.
4
Examine the alternative explanations
The passage provides specific reasons: wudu from fire was known to be not obligatory by necessity; carrying a funeral is not an impurity; the prohibition of inserting the hand into a vessel was a recommendation (nadb) not a strict obligation.
The hadith about washing hands after sleep is interpreted as a recommendation for cleanliness.
5
Conclude that the rule remains intact
These examples do not prove that qiyas can override khabar; they only show that the Companions exercised ijtihad in understanding the scope of the hadith, not in rejecting its authority.
Thus, the Hanafi principle of preferring khabar over qiyas is upheld.

(And others) like the Mother of the Believers Aisha al-Siddiqa, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Abu al-Darda', and others, may Allah be pleased with them all. (Khabar is given precedence even if the narrator) is known for reliability without jurisprudence (fiqh), like Abu Hurayra, and it has preceded that Abu Hurayra is a jurist mujtahid undoubtedly (and Anas) ibn Malik (so the khabar is not abandoned due to opposition of qiyas except when the door of opinion is closed) and qiyas (like the hadith of musarra). The speech of Imam Fakhr al-Islam has passed as elaboration and confirmation. The conclusion of his view is that the khabar is absolutely preferred except that when the door of opinion is closed, suspicion arises in conformity when the narrator is non-faqih, so it is not accepted due to this suspicion. So this also is in reality agreeing with what is from the three Imams. And al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani al-Shafi'i paused. (And the chosen) among some later scholars (if the establishment of the cause is preponderant over the khabar and its existence in the branch is not weak) but remains at the measure it was in the root or is preponderant in it, (then qiyas) is preferred. (And if they are equal) i.e., the establishment of the cause in the root and branch, and the establishment of the khabar, then pause, and neither is given preference over the other. (And otherwise) i.e., if there is neither preponderance nor equality, (then the khabar) is preferred. (For us) according to the chosen of the later scholars: preferment of the preponderant is determined and obligatory, so qiyas is preferred when the establishment of the cause is preponderant, and the khabar is preferred when it is preponderant. (And) preferment (in equality is arbitrary) so one pauses at equality necessarily. Know that this is very clear, and the three Imams do not deny it. How? For preferment of the preponderant is necessary and agreed upon. Rather, the place of dispute is whether such a qiyas exists or not. Their point of view is that it does not exist. So whoever claims the preponderance of qiyas, even in one case, must prove it, and that is extremely difficult. And for the majority, firstly: The Commander of the Faithful (Umar), may Allah be pleased with him, abandoned qiyas regarding the fetus, which is the non-obligation of the ghurra (blood money) like other doubtful matters. Its summary: analogy of destroying the fetus to destroying other matters doubtful in life and existence, (because of the khabar of Hamal ibn Malik that he (peace be upon him and his family and companions) obligated the ghurra in it as previously mentioned, and he said: 'Were it not for this, I would have judged in it with our own opinion.' It was narrated by Abu Dawud, and its wording: 'Allahu Akbar, if I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise,' and in another narration: 'It is a lie that we judge in this with our own opinion.') (And) the Commander of the Faithful Umar abandoned (qiyas regarding the diya of fingers. His opinion was regarding the little finger: six, regarding the ring finger: nine, regarding the middle finger: ten, regarding the index finger: twelve, and in al-Tahrir: ten, and regarding the thumb: fifteen) camels, all of that in al-Taysir. The commentator said: thus mentioned by more than one, but what is in the narration of al-Bayhaqi is that he regarded the index finger as twelve and the middle finger as thirteen. Al-Shafi'i narrated his decree regarding the thumb likewise based on the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: for every finger ten camels in the book. (And) the Commander of the Faithful Umar abandoned (qiyas regarding the inheritance of the wife from the blood money of her husband, which indicates non-inheritance, since the husband did not own it so that she would inherit, and the marriage relationship did not remain after death so that it would be established initially through kinship, etc., besides many widespread incidents. And none of the Salaf or Khalaf denied it, so it was a consensus on the preference of khabar. This is very clear for one who studies incidents and histories. I say: If it is said: The necessary implication of what you mentioned is permissibility, i.e., permissibility of acting on khabar, not the obligation of preferring the khabar. We say: Their silence in disputes is evidence of obligation, so understand. And it may be said: Perhaps the school of the Commander of the Faithful was choice when there is conflict, so silence in choosing one of the options does not necessitate obligation. This is nothing, because the context of the story indicates otherwise, and his statement: 'If I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise' is explicit that the preventer from acting on qiyas was the existence of the khabar. Moreover, such cases are many, and what is mentioned are specific examples learned through experience, repetition, and complete induction. So the objection that this only indicates the preference of some khabars over some qiyases, and perhaps the khabar here has strength unlike other khabars, is baseless and not listened to. (And it was objected by the abandonment of Ibn Abbas to the khabar of Abu Hurayra: 'Perform wudu from what is touched by fire.' He said: 'Should we not perform wudu with hot water?' as an addition of the described to the attribute: 'How can we perform wudu with what we perform wudu from?' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, its wording: He said to him: 'O Abu Hurayra, do I perform wudu from oil? Do I perform wudu from hot water?' So Abu Hurayra said: 'O son of my brother, if you hear a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ, do not strike an example for it.') (And) by his abandonment of his khabar: 'Whoever carries a funeral let him perform wudu.' And in another narration: 'Let him perform ghusl.' By this khabar, Imam Ahmad obligated ghusl in one narration. He said: 'Wudu is not required for carrying dry sticks.' (And) by his abandonment of (his khabar about the one who wakes up from his sleep: 'When one of you wakes from his sleep, let him wash his hand before inserting it into the vessel, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' Narrated by the two Shaykhs and others. (And likewise) the Mother of the Believers (Aisha) al-Siddiqa. They said: 'How do we deal with the mihras, which is a huge carved stone that no one can move; water is taken from it by hand or a small vessel and one performs wudu by inserting the hand?' The summary of the response: If this were the case, wudu with the mihras would not be valid. He said in al-Taysir: This is not established from them, rather it is established from a man called Qayn al-Ashja'i, and there is disagreement about his Companionship. And it was answered that their denial was due to the apparentness of the conflict, i.e., the apparentness of its conflict, not for abandoning qiyas. Thus I found the copy, and perhaps it is a scribal error. (And the more apparent: not for abandoning the khabar by qiyas, although it is forced, and it is said that the addition of the source to the subject is of the type 'inbat al-rabi' (spring growth), and the object is understood, and the meaning is that qiyas is not a cause for abandoning the khabar, meaning it is a cause for abandonment such that it would be a proof for you. I say in it an admission of non-preference of khabar when the qiyas is clearer than the khabar, because the apparentness of the opposition is only the apparentness of a clear qiyas understood with minimal reflection. So understand. This is extremely weak, because the summary of the answer is that the denial is because its opposite is clear from the Sharia. For performing wudu with hot water was necessarily known in the religion, and carrying a funeral is a common occurrence from the time of the lawgiver (peace be upon him and his family and companions). So if it necessitated wudu, it would have become widespread, but it is only a matter of dry sticks, and it is necessarily known from the Sharia that it is not an impure event. Similarly, the use of the mihras was well known, so if what was mentioned were true, the mihras would not have been used. So their abandonment of this hadith was due to it falling into a matter of general affliction, and it does not contain an admission of the precedence of qiyas, even if clear, over khabar. So understand. And it is not far-fetched to say: They did not reject the hadith itself, but rather they rejected Abu Hurayra's interpretation of obligating wudu from what is touched by fire and carrying a funeral and the impurity of water by inserting the hand into the vessel, deeming it contrary to the legal principles. Rather, the meaning of 'wudu' in the two hadiths is cleaning, like washing the hand and rinsing the mouth after eating what is touched by fire, and washing the hand and foot from carrying a funeral, and the prohibition of inserting the hand into the vessel is a prohibition of dispraise when possible. (And) for the majority: (Secondly: his, peace be upon him and his family, confirmation).
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul argument for preferring khabar over qiyas when they conflict. It begins by addressing the status of narrators: according to the Hanafi school, even if a narrator is known for reliability ('adala) but not for juristic expertise (fiqaha), like Abu Hurayra (though the text notes that Abu Hurayra actually was a mujtahid), the khabar is still given precedence over qiyas, except when 'the door of opinion is closed'—meaning when the issue is so clear that no reasonable ijtihad remains. This exception is illustrated by the hadith of musarra (a sale with fraud), where qiyas might suggest otherwise but the hadith takes priority.

The author then presents the position of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and later scholars: if the establishment of the legal cause ('illa) is preponderant over the khabar, qiyas is preferred; if equal, pause; if neither, khabar prevails. The Hanafi response is that this is self-evident and the real issue is whether such preponderant qiyas ever exists—they argue it does not.

Evidence is then marshalled from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who abandoned qiyas in three cases: (1) the fetus—he obligated the ghurra based on a hadith despite qiyas suggesting no obligation; (2) diya for fingers—he fixed varying amounts for each finger based on a hadith rather than the qiyas of equal value; (3) inheritance of a wife from her husband's blood money—he gave inheritance based on a hadith despite qiyas suggesting none. The widespread acceptance of these rulings by the Salaf and Khalaf is claimed as ijma' (consensus) on the principle of preferring khabar.

The passage then addresses objections: some argued that these examples only show permissibility, not obligation. The response is that the Companions' silence in these disputes indicates obligation. Others argued that Umar might have been exercising choice, but his explicit statement 'If I had not heard this, I would have judged otherwise' shows the khabar was the preventer.

Finally, counterexamples are discussed: Ibn Abbas and Aisha seeming to ignore certain ahādīth. The Hanafi commentator refutes that these were not rejections of the khabar itself but of interpretations that conflicted with clearer principles of the Sharia. The actual rulings from those Companions were based on other considerations, not on preferring qiyas over khabar. Thus the Hanafi position that khabar is always preferred (with the limited exception) remains intact.

Key Terms
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A concept meaning 'general affliction' or common occurrence; if a ruling were obligatory, it would be widely known and practiced.
التنزيه (al-tanzih): Recommendation; an action that is not required but is encouraged for spiritual cleanliness.
المهراس (al-mihras): A large carved stone vessel used for water, shaped so that one must insert a hand to take water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the passage, why did Ibn Abbas say 'Wudu is not required for carrying dry sticks' despite the hadith 'Whoever carries a funeral let him perform wudu'?
A) He rejected the hadith as weak.
B) He used qiyas to override the hadith.
C) He understood the hadith to apply only when the corpse is present and impure, not to dry sticks.
D) He forgot the hadith.

Key Takeaway
Valid counterexamples to the rule of preferring khabar over qiyas are actually instances of rejecting interpretations, not the narrations themselves.

Responding to Companion Practice: Hadith vs Qiyas
Hanafi response to objections from Companion practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi response to the objection that Companions abandoned hadith for qiyas, and apply the principle of zuhur al-khilaf (clear opposition) to defend the precedence of hadith.

Core Idea
Companions did not abandon hadith for qiyas; they rejected interpretations that contradicted necessary religious knowledge.

In disputes over the hierarchy of legal sources, opponents of the Hanafi school sometimes cite examples where Companions like Ibn Abbas and Aisha appear to have set aside clear hadith in favor of qiyas. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut presents the Hanafi defense, arguing that these instances are either misinterpreted, based on weak reports, or stem from the principle that a hadith must not contradict a ruling known with certainty (zuhur al-khilaf). Understanding this response is crucial for grasping how the Hanafi school maintains the primacy of hadith while accounting for apparent counterexamples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
List the three instances where Companions are claimed to have abandoned hadith: Ibn Abbas on wudu from cooked food, Ibn Abbas on carrying a funeral, and Aisha on the mihras. Understand the apparent conflict.
These are the classic objections against the Hanafi principle.
2
Examine the Hanafi response to each
For each case, note the Hanafi explanation: either the hadith is interpreted metaphorically (cleaning), the report is weak, or the Companion’s action is due to zuhur al-khilaf (the hadith’s apparent meaning contradicts a well-known ruling).
The key is to see that the Companions did not reject the hadith itself.
3
Analyze the principle of zuhur al-khilaf
Understand that zuhur al-khilaf means the hadith’s apparent meaning conflicts with a ruling known by necessity from the religion (e.g., water does not become impure by contact). In such cases, the hadith is reinterpreted to align with that definite knowledge.
This principle preserves hadith’s authority while avoiding contradictions with definitive rulings.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Note the fiqhi outcomes: Hanafis do not require wudu from cooked food, ghusl from carrying a funeral, or washing hands before inserting into a well. Other schools (e.g., some reports from Ahmad) may differ.
The dispute is not merely theoretical; it has real impact on daily practice.
5
Evaluate the epistemological weight
Recognize that the Hanafi response relies on the principle that necessary knowledge (daruri) overrides zanni (speculative) hadith. This is a key usul al-fiqh concept that distinguishes between levels of certainty.
This approach is consistent with the Hanafi commitment to epistemic consistency.

Source Text

أتوضأ من الحميم؟ فقال أبو هريرة: يا ابن أخي، إذا سمعت حديثاً عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فلا تضرب له مثلاً. و بترك ابن عباس خبره من حمل جنازة فليتوضأ. وفي رواية: فليغتسل، وبهذا الخبر أوجب الإمام أحمد الوضوء بالمهراس. قال في «التيسير»: لم يثبت هذا منهما، وإنما يثبت من رجل يقال له قين الأشجعي وفي صحبته خلاف. وأجيب بأن إنكارهما لظهور الخلاف يعني لظهور خلافه لا لترك القياس هكذا وجدت النسخة، ولعلها من خطأ الناسخ، والأظهر لا لترك الخبر بالقياس وإن كانت فيتكلف، ويقال فيها إضافة المصدر إلى الفاعل من قبيل إنبات الربيع، والمفعول مقدر والمعنى لا يكون القياس تاركاً للخبر، بمعنى كونه سبباً للترك حتى يكون حجة لكم. أقول فيه اعتراف بعدم تقديم الخبر إذا كان القياس واضحاً من الخبر وذلك لأن ظهور المخالفة إنما هو ظهور قياس جليّ يفهم بأدنى تأمل. فافهم. وهذا في غاية السقوط، فإن حاصل الجواب أن الإنكار لأن خلافه العيدان والمعلوم من الشرع ضرورة أنه ليس حدثاً، وكذا اتخاذ المهراس كان معروفاً، فلو ما ذكر لم يتخذ المهراس، فتركهما هذا الحديث لوقوعه فيما يعم البلوى به، وليس فيه اعتراف بتقدم القياس ولو واضحاً على الخبر فافهم. ولا يبعد أن يقال: لم يردوا نفس الحديث، بل ردّوا تأويل أبي هريرة من إيجاب التوضئ مما مسته النار وحمل الجنازة وتنجس الماء بالإدخال في الإناء بأنه مخالف للقواعد الشرعية بل المراد من التوضئ
