Al-Sunnah as Source
advanced
15 min
Taqlid of a Companion in Hanafi Usul
Argument for and against taqlid of a Companion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position on taqlid of a Companion by distinguishing between transmitted matters (ma la yudraku bil-ra'y) and opinion-based matters, and evaluate the arguments for and against obligatory taqlid.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a Companion is binding only in matters beyond human reasoning, not in matters of opinion.

The issue of taqlid of the Companions is a key usul dispute. Some scholars argue that any Companion's saying is binding; others restrict it to the first two caliphs. The Hanafi school takes a nuanced position: while a Companion's saying is a proof, it only becomes obligatory to follow in purely transmitted matters, such as the duration of menstruation. This lesson examines the proofs and responses, focusing on why taqlid is not required in matters open to ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the dispute
Determine what exactly is being contested: is taqlid of a Companion obligatory in all matters, only for certain Companions, or under specific conditions?
The disputants are the proponents (المثبت) and the Hanafi scholars.
2
Examine the arguments for general taqlid
The proponent cites hadiths 'My Companions are like stars' and 'Follow the two after me' to argue for obligatory following.
These hadiths are interpreted literally by the proponents.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to these arguments
The Hanafis respond that the hadiths address the Companions themselves, not later generations. Also, the shura incident is about political following, not legal taqlid.
A key point: the addressees of the hadiths were already Companions, so they cannot be a general obligation.
4
Understand the Hanafi rule for transmitted matters
In matters not based on opinion (ma la yudraku bil-ra'y), a Companion's saying is treated as a proof (dalil al-dalil) and obligatory to follow, because it must be based on hearing from the Prophet.
Example: the minimum duration of menstruation is a transmitted matter.
5
Distinguish between the Companion and the Tabi'i
A Companion's direct hearing and contextual knowledge make his transmission reliable; a Tabi'i lacks that, so his saying does not carry the same weight.
The Hanafis justify this by the textual proof of Companions' justice and their firsthand experience.

شريت وبئسما اشتريت أبلغي زيد بن أرقم أنه قد أبطل جهاده مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم إن لم يتب منه قالت فما نصنع؟ قال : قالت عائشة : فَمَن جَاءَهُ مَوْعِظَةٌ مِّن رَّبِّهِ فَانتَهَى ، : فَلَهُ مَا سَلَفَ وَأَمْرُهُ إِلَى الله ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٧٥] ومن عاد فينتقم الله منه والحكم ببطلان الجهاد لا يكون بالرأي، فلا بد من السماع (۱) ، فإن قلت : يجوز أن يكون الوعيد لما أنه بايع إلى أجل مجهول وهو العطاء، أو لاشتراطها عليه اشتراء نفسها، والشرط الفاسد يفسد البيع، وكذا الأجل المجهول، قلت: لو سلم أن يوم العطاء كان مجهولاً وأن الشرط المذكور أدخلها في العقد أنها قالت : بئسما شريت واشتريت أبلغي الخ ... فقد رتبت الوعيد على شرائها منه، وإن كان بيعها أيضاً فاسداً، فقد ظهر أن شراء ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن لا يجوز، وجوب التقليد وكون مذهبه في حكم المرفوع لأنه لا بد من حجة نقلية) لأن الفتوى والعمل من غير حجة شرعية حرام والصحابة بريئون عنه بعد التهم، فالحجة عقلية أو نقلية، والأول منتف بالفرض ، فتعين الثاني فله حكم الرفع فمذهبه دليل الدليل كالإجماع (ونقض بالصحابي) فإنه ينبغي أن يجب باستقراء الحال فتدبر) وقد يجاب عن الثاني بأن اتخاذ الصحابي مذهباً فيما لا مجال للرأي فيه دل دلالة قاطعة أو مظنونة ظناً قوياً أنه فيه شيئاً، فهو سمع قطعي، عنده ثبوتاً، ثم هو مشاهد للقرائن فلا يخطىء في فهم المراد، فمذهب الصحابي دليل الدليل، وأما التابعي فليس هو سامعاً، فالمسموع ليس مقطوع الثبوت، وهو غير مشاهد للقرائن المفهمة، فجاز عليه الخطأ في فهم المراد، وظن ما ليس دليلاً دليلاً، العدالة غير منصوصة فاضمحل فيه ظن الدلالة على الدليل فافهم.
The Second Principle/Sunnah of the Mujtahid? Otherwise it is invalid by agreement. Answer: If his school is a proof, then he takes the ruling from its source, so it is not taqlid because taking the ruling from the evidence is not taqlid, so understand. The proponent said regarding taqlid of a Companion generally, whether one of the two shaykhs or others, the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'My Companions are like stars, by whichever of them you follow you will be guided.' Its takhrij has preceded with its pros and cons. And the proponent said specifically taqlid of only the two shaykhs: first, his saying (peace be upon him): 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and Umar.' And it is answered that the addressees in both hadiths are the followers, which is very apparent in the first, because oral address requires an existing addressee, and they too are Companions. The answer to the second is that its utmost implication is obligation of following them, not negation of following others, so understand. And the proponent said specifically, secondly: Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf (may Allah be pleased with him) appointed Ali (may Allah honor his face) to the caliphate with the condition of following the two shaykhs when the Commander of the Faithful Umar made it a shura among six: Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) departed while pleased with them. So Abd al-Rahman undertook selection. Ali (may Allah honor his face) did not accept, and Uthman accepted the caliphate with that condition, so he accepted and was given allegiance, and no Companion objected, so it became consensus. That is weak. How so? If it were correct, it would necessitate taqlid of a mujtahid Companion by a mujtahid Companion, and that is invalid by agreement. Rather, the intent is following in conduct and politics. Ali did not accept because he was cautious in the pledge, and everything is facilitated for what it is created. Uthman accepted because he trusted himself. And taqlid of a Companion in matters not based on opinion is obligatory according to our companions by agreement, such as estimating the minimum of menstruation by the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, Anas, Umar, Ali, Uthman, and Ibn Abi al-As—as cited in al-Taysir to Jami' al-Asrar. Indeed, estimations are not reached by opinion. If you say: al-Daraqutni narrated from him (peace be upon him) raised: 'The minimum of menstruation is three days and its maximum ten days.' So here action is based on that, not on the Companion's saying. And this hadith, even if its chain is weak, became hasan and worthy of proof due to multiple chains as explained by Shaykh Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir. I say: That is fine; the ultimate matter is that two proofs came for one desired ruling. Another example: Razin narrated from Umm Anas that she said: Umm Walad of Zayd ibn Arqam came to Aisha and said: I sold a slave-girl to Zayd for eight hundred dirhams until the stipend, then I bought her back before the term for six hundred, and I had stipulated upon him that if he sells her, I will buy her from him. Aisha said to her: How bad is what you sold and bought! Inform Zayd ibn Arqam that his jihad with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is invalidated if he does not repent. She said: So what should we do? Aisha said: 'But whoever receives an admonition from his Lord and desists, then what has passed is for him, and his affair rests with Allah' [al-Baqarah 2:275], and whoever returns, Allah will take vengeance on him. And the ruling of invalidation of jihad is not based on opinion, so there must be hearing. If you say: It is possible that the threat was due to his selling for an unknown term—the stipend—or due to her stipulation upon him to buy herself, and the invalid condition invalidates the sale, and likewise the unknown term. I say: Even if it is granted that the day of stipend was unknown and that the mentioned condition entered the contract, she said: 'How bad is what you sold and bought! Inform...' So she placed the threat on her buying from him, even if her own sale was also invalid. So it appears that buying back what one sold at a lower price before payment of the price is not permissible. The obligation of taqlid and that his school has the ruling of being raised (marfu') because a transmitted proof is necessary. Because issuing fatwa and acting without a legal proof is forbidden, and the Companions are innocent of that after suspicion. So the proof is either rational or transmitted; the first is excluded by assumption, so the second is determined. Thus his school has the ruling of being raised, so his school is evidence of the evidence, like consensus. And it is rebutted by the Companion: It would also be obligatory upon him to follow taqlid because the raised (marfu') is binding on him as well. And it is rebutted by taqlid of the tabi'i in matters not based on opinion, because a transmitted proof is also necessary. I say: The lack (meaning the lack of the claim) is prevented. Rather, it is obligatory upon the Companion to follow his saying, and upon us to follow the tabi'i's saying in it, not absolutely, but when there is no suspicion of adopting a school without evidence. Hence Zayd ibn Arqam acted on the saying of the Mother of the Believers. But the Companions may suspect each other, so they do not act on each other's sayings. As for us, we speak nothing but good and do not suspect them at all because the proof of their justice is established like the sun at midday, so it is not permissible for us to abandon taqlid. As for the tabi'i, we may suspect him as well because there is no textual evidence for the justice of the tabi'is, only probability from induction of the situation, so reflect. And it may be answered regarding the second that adopting a Companion's school in matters with no room for opinion indicates with conclusive or strong probable indication that he heard something; it is hearing that is certain in his view in terms of thubut, and he witnessed the contextual clues so he does not err in understanding the intended meaning. Hence the Companion's school is evidence of the evidence. As for the tabi'i, he is not a listener, so the heard thing is not certain in thubut, and he did not witness the contextual clues that convey meaning, so he may err in understanding the intended meaning and assume something not evidence to be evidence. Justice is not textually established, so the probability of indication to the evidence disappears, so understand.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute on the issue of taqlid of a Companion. The author first clarifies that taking a ruling from a proof is not taqlid. Then he presents the proponent's arguments: the hadith 'My Companions are like stars' for general taqlid, and specifically the hadith 'Follow the two after me' for taqlid of Abu Bakr and Umar. The Hanafi response is that these hadiths address the Companions themselves, not later generations. The story of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf's condition is rejected as weak because it would require a mujtahid to follow another mujtahid, which is invalid. The Hanafi position is that taqlid of a Companion is obligatory only in matters not based on opinion, like estimating minimum menstruation, because these are purely transmitted. The hadith from al-Daraqutni about minimum menstruation is used to show that the ruling comes from the Prophet, not just the Companion's saying. The example of Aisha and the slave-girl illustrates that the ruling on invalidating jihad is based on hearing, not opinion. The author then argues that a Companion's saying in such matters has the force of a marfu' hadith because a transmitted proof is necessary. He addresses objections about why a Companion himself does not have to follow another Companion (because they may suspect each other) and why a tabi'i's saying is different (because his justice is not textually proven and he lacks direct hearing of the Prophet). Finally, he explains that the Companion's direct hearing and acquaintance with context make his understanding reliable, whereas the tabi'i is prone to error. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that taqlid of a Companion is binding only in transmitted matters, not in matters of opinion.

Key Terms
تقليد الصحابي (taqlid al-sahabi): Following the legal opinion of a Companion in matters where the Companion's saying is taken as a proof.
ما لا يدرك بالرأي (ma la yudraku bil-ra'y): Matters that cannot be determined by human reasoning, such as estimations of time periods and unseen matters; they require transmitted knowledge.
دليل الدليل (dalil al-dalil): The Companion's saying serves as evidence pointing to the actual proof (e.g., the Prophet's statement), thus it is like a marfu' hadith indirectly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of matters do the Hanafis consider taqlid of a Companion obligatory?
A) Matters of opinion, like analogy
B) Matters not based on opinion, like estimating minimum menstruation
C) All legal matters without exception
D) Only the sayings of Abu Bakr and Umar

Key Takeaway
Taqlid of a Companion is binding only in purely transmitted matters where human reasoning has no access.

Hanafi Taqlid of Sahabi Opinions: Principle and Application
Explains Hanafi taqlid of Sahaba with two examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi principle regarding taqlid of Sahabi opinions and apply it to distinguish between following and departing from a Sahabi ruling based on conflicting evidence.

Core Idea
Hanafi imams follow Sahabi opinions unless a stronger evidence (other Sahabi view or marfu' hadith) conflicts.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut addresses a crucial aspect of Hanafi usul: the authority of the sayings of the Companions (Sahabah). Some may think the Hanafi school disregards Sahabi opinions when they contradict, but the text clarifies that the imams always respected them. Departures from a Sahabi's view are not arbitrary but result from conflicting evidence such as another Sahabi's opinion or a marfu' hadith. By examining two concrete examples, we will see how this principle operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases presented
The passage gives two examples where the Hanafi imams either followed or departed from a Sahabi opinion. Locate them: the salam contract (following Ibn 'Umar) and the liability of the jointly-employed worker (following 'Ali partially). Note the contrasting outcome.
In salam, they did not require informing about visible capital; in liability, they held the worker liable for theft but not fire.
2
Analyze the reasoning for departing from a Sahabi opinion
In the liability case, Abu Hanifah did not fully adopt 'Ali's ruling (general liability) because he considered the worker a trustee (amin), and because there might be a conflicting marfu' hadith. Explain the usul principle that Sahabi opinion is a proof but can be overridden by stronger evidence.
The text mentions 'Ali's retraction or a marfu' hadith as possible conflicting evidence.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's quoted statement
Read the quote from Ibn al-Mubarak: 'Whatever has come from the Prophet and his Companions, we accept... whatever from Companions, I do not abandon it.' This confirms his commitment to Sahabi opinions.
This quote shows that taqlid of Sahaba is the default position.
4
Synthesize the Hanafi principle
The principle: Sahabi opinions are binding unless a conflicting evidence (another Sahabi or marfu' hadith) is available. This explains the apparent inconsistency between the general statement and specific departures.
The principle is not arbitrary rejection but careful weighing of evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(تنبيه : لا رواية في المسألة المذكورة (عن) الإمام أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، بل اختلف عملهم فتارة يقلدون وتارة لا فلم يشترطا إعلام قدر رأس المال المشاهد في السلم (لأن الإشارة كالتسمية في المعرفة والتعيين يرتفع بها الجهالة وشرطه بقول ابن عمر) وقد عزى إلى أمير المؤمنين عمر أيضاً فلم يقلد أو قلد هو (وضمناً الأجير المشترك فيما يمكن الاحتراز عنه كالسرقة لا كالحرق الغالب (بقول) أمير المؤمنين (علي) كرّم الله وجهه، رواه ابن أبي شيبة، وروى الشافعي عنه أنه كان يضمن الصباغ والصائغ ويقول : لا يصلح الناس إلا ذلك (ونفاه) أي التضمين (هو بناء على أنه أمين فلا يضمن (كالمودع) إلا إذا وجد التعدي، فلم يقلد وقلدا، هذا، لكن قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي في فتح المنان في تأييد مذهب النعمان»، قال ابن المبارك : قال أبو حنيفة : ما جاء عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فبالرأس والعين وما جاء عن أصحابه فلا أتركه فهذا نص صريح منه على أنه يقلد الصحابة، وأما عمله في بعض المسائل على خلاف قول الصحابي فلعله ثبت عند معارضة قول آخر كما قيل في مسألة التضمين، إن أمير المؤمنين علياً رجع عنه، بل نقل فيه حديثاً مرفوعاً فافهم.
(Note: There is no transmitted report in the mentioned matter from Imam Abu Hanifah and his two companions, rather their practice differed: sometimes they engaged in taqlid and sometimes not. Thus they did not require informing about the amount of visible capital in salam (because pointing is like naming in knowledge and specification, so ignorance is removed by it; and they stipulated it by the saying of Ibn 'Umar). And it was attributed to Amir al-Mu'minin 'Umar as well, so sometimes he did not follow and sometimes he followed. And they held the jointly-employed worker liable for what can be avoided, like theft, not like overwhelming fire, by the saying of Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali, may Allah honor his face, reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah. Al-Shafi'i reported from him that he used to hold the dyer and the goldsmith liable and said, 'People are only set right by that.' And he (Abu Hanifah) negated liability, i.e., he built it on the basis that the worker is a trustee, so he does not guarantee like the depositary, unless there is transgression. Thus sometimes he did not follow and sometimes they followed. But Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi said in Fath al-Mannan in support of the madhhab of al-Nu'man: Ibn al-Mubarak said: Abu Hanifah said: 'Whatever has come from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family, and his Companions, we accept with head and eye; and whatever has come from his Companions, I do not abandon it.' So this is an explicit text that he does taqlid of the Companions. As for his practice in some matters contrary to a Sahabi's saying, perhaps it is established that there is a conflicting saying, as was said in the issue of liability: that Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali retracted it, rather he transmitted a marfu' hadith regarding it. Understand.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This note (tanbih) addresses the observation that Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) do not have a single reported position on every issue; sometimes they followed a Sahabi's opinion and sometimes they did not. The author gives two examples: first, in the salam contract, they did not require the buyer to inform the seller of the exact amount of capital that is already visible, because pointing suffices, and they based this on the practice of Ibn 'Umar, even though another narration from 'Umar might suggest otherwise. Second, regarding the liability of a jointly-employed worker (ajir mushtarak), they followed the opinion of 'Ali that he is liable for theft but not for fire, even though 'Ali also reportedly held him liable for all losses. Abu Hanifah did not follow 'Ali's opinion in the general liability case because he considered the worker an amin (trustee). The author then quotes Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi, who cites Ibn al-Mubarak quoting Abu Hanifa's own statement that he accepts everything from the Prophet and the Companions. When he seems to contradict a Sahabi, it is likely because another Sahabi's opinion or a stronger evidence, such as a marfu' hadith, existed. This shows that the Hanafi madhhab does not abandon the Sahabah's opinions lightly, but weighs them against other evidence.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): Following the opinion of a qualified mujtahid without knowing the specific evidence; in this passage, it refers to the practice of the Hanafi imams of adhering to the opinion of a Sahabi when they found no conflicting evidence.
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A jointly-employed worker who works for multiple employers (e.g., a dyer, tailor). According to Hanafi fiqh, he is a trustee (amin) and is not liable for loss unless he is negligent or commits transgression, except for certain cases like theft where he can avoid it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifah not follow the general ruling of 'Ali regarding the liability of the jointly-employed worker?
A) Because he considered the worker as a trustee (amin) and not liable unless there is transgression.
B) Because he preferred the opinion of 'Umar over 'Ali.
C) Because there was no reliable narration from 'Ali on that issue.
D) Because he believed all workers are absolutely liable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Sahabi opinions as authoritative but not infallible; they may be set aside when a stronger evidence is present.

The Hujjiyah of the Tabi'i: Not Equal to the Sahabi
Argues that the opinion of a Tabi'i lacks the authority of a Sahabi's opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate why the Hanafi school does not treat a Tabi'i's opinion as an independent legal proof (hujjah) and identify the key distinction from a Sahabi's statement.

Core Idea
A Tabi'i's opinion lacks the authority of a Sahabi's because he did not directly hear from the Prophet or witness the revelatory context.

In this passage, the Hanafi Usul tradition firmly distinguishes the legal authority of a Companion's statement from that of a Successor (Tabi'i). While a Sahabi's opinion can function as a proof (hujjah) and is often treated as marfu' (traceable to the Prophet), a Tabi'i's opinion is merely ijtihad and does not bind. The author examines two counterexamples—Shuraih and Masruq—to refute the claim that a Tabi'i's opinion can be an independent hujjah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
Recognise that some scholars argue a Tabi'i's opinion, especially if he was a judge appointed by the Sahaba (like Shuraih), is a hujjah.
The opposing evidence is presented in parentheses in the text.
2
State the Hanafi rule regarding the Tabi'i's authority
The Hanafi position is clear: a Tabi'i's statement is not like a marfu' hadith because he lacks sam' (direct hearing) and mushahadat al-qara'in (witnessing contextual clues).
The narration from the Imam (if Sahaba agree we submit, if Tabi'in come we oppose) illustrates this.
3
Examine the opponent's evidence
The opponent cites Shuraih's appointment and his ruling on testimony, and Masruq's correction of Ibn 'Abbas on a vow matter, as proof that Tabi'un opinions are authoritative.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author shows that Shuraih's ruling actually agreed with a marfu' hadith and 'Umar's opinion, so it is not an independent proof. Masruq's disagreement does not make his opinion a hujjah; it was a valid ijtihad that may have caused retraction due to reasoning.
Thus, the examples do not support the opponent's claim; they align with the Hanafi view.
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis do not consider the Tabi'i's opinion as a binding source; it may be considered but not obligatory. Other schools may give it weight as a precedent.
This distinction preserves the hierarchical authority of the early generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(تذييل : التابعي ولو زاحم بفتواه رأي الصحابة في عصرهم فليس مثلاً لهم) فلا يكون قوله كالمرفوع لعدم وجود المناط، وهو السماع ومشاهدة القرائن ولا فضل الصحابة. روي عن الإمام إذا اجتمعت الصحابة سلمناهم، وإذا جاء التابعون زاحمناهم، وفي رواية : لا أقلدهم، هم رجال اجتهدوا ونحن رجال نجتهد، كذا في التقرير ، كذا في «الحاشية». وإن هذا فيرشدك إلى أن اجتماع الصحابة يوجب العمل ولا عبرة بالتابعين عند حضرتهم (فاستدلال البعض على صحة تقليده برد شريح وهو تابعي جليل القدر قلده القضاة أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه، الله عنه، فبقي فبقي قاضياً إلى زمان أمير المؤمنين علي كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام ،وبعده ثم ترك القضاء زمن فتنة عبد الله بن الزبير واستعفى الحجاج الظالم من القضاء فأعفاه لما رأى من عدم تمكنه من الحكم بالحق ومات هو رضي الله عنه سنة وثمانين (شهادة الإمام الحسن رضي الله عنه (لعلي وهو) أي أمير المؤمنين علي كرّم الله يقبل الابن في الشهادة للأب حين جاء أمير المؤمنين علي بيهودي شريحاً فادعى عليه أن الدرع الذي في يده درعه وأنكره هو، فطلب شريح البينة منه، فجاء بالإمام الحسن وقنبر فقال : أقبل شهادة مولاك ولا أقبل شهادة ابنك، فامتنع أمير المؤمنين عن أخذ الدرع فأسلم اليهودي، وكان معه إلى أن استشهد بصفين ومخالفة مسروق) وهو أيضاً من كبار التابعين (ابن عباس في إيجاب مائة من الإبل في النذر بذبح الولد إلى الشاة وقال : ليس ولده خيراً من إسماعيل (فرجع) ابن عباس عن قوله (لا يفيد) خبر لقوله : فاستدلال البعض، فإن غاية ما لزم منه أن مخالفة التابعي الصحابي قد وقع وأما أنها حجة فمن أين :نعم : يدل على عدم تقليد التابعي للصحابي) وهذا أيضاً غير تام عند من رأى الحجية فإن شريحاً وإن خالف أمير المؤمنين علياً لكنه وافق أمير المؤمنين عمر ، ويوافق أيضاً الحديث المرفوع المروي في «الهداية» الذي خرجه في فتح القدير بسند متصل برواية الشيخ أبي بكر الرازي عن أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها : لا يجوز شهادة الوالد لولده ولا الولد لوالده، ولا المرأة لزوجها ولا الزوج لامرأته، ولا العبد لسيده ولا السيد لعبده، ولا الشريك لشريكه ولا الأجير لمن استأجره» ومخالفة مسروق كحكم سليمان مخالفاً لحكم داود في الحرث والولد كما روي في «الصحيحين» .
(Appendix: The Tabi'i, even if he opposes by his fatwa the opinion of the Companions in their time, is not like them.) So his saying is not like the marfu' due to the absence of the effective basis, which is hearing and witnessing the contextual clues, nor does he have the virtue of the Companions. It is narrated from the Imam: 'When the Companions agree, we submit to them; when the Tabi'in come, we oppose them.' And in another narration: 'I do not do taqlid of them; they are men who exercised ijtihad, and we are men who exercise ijtihad.' Thus in al-Taqrir and in al-Hashiyah. And this indicates to you that the agreement of the Companions necessitates action, and the Tabi'in are not considered in their presence. (Thus the argument of some on the validity of his taqlid by the rejection of Shuraih, who is a great Tabi'i, appointed as judge by Amir al-Mu'minin 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, so he remained judge until the time of Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali, may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, and after him he left the judiciary during the fitnah of 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr and asked al-Hajjaj the oppressor to relieve him, so he relieved him when he saw that he was not able to judge with truth, and he died, may Allah be pleased with him, in the year eighty. (The testimony of Imam al-Hasan, may Allah be pleased with him, for 'Ali, meaning Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali, may Allah honor his face, did he accept the testimony of a son for his father? When Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali came with a Jew to Shuraih and claimed that the armor in his hand was his armor and he denied it, Shuraih asked him for evidence, so he brought Imam al-Hasan and Qanbar and said, 'I accept the testimony of your freed servant but I do not accept the testimony of your son.' So Amir al-Mu'minin refrained from taking the armor, so the Jew became Muslim, and he (the Jew) remained with him until he was martyred at Siffin? And the opposition of Masruq, who is also among the great Tabi'in, to Ibn 'Abbas regarding the obligation of one hundred camels in a vow to slaughter a son? He said, 'Your son is not better than Ishmael.' So Ibn 'Abbas retracted his saying. (It does not benefit) predicate of 'so the argument of some'? For the most that follows from it is that opposition of the Tabi'i to the Sahabi occurred; but how is it a proof? Yes, it indicates the non-taqlid of the Tabi'i to the Sahabi. And this is also not perfect according to those who hold its hujjiyah, for Shuraih, although he opposed Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali, he agreed with Amir al-Mu'minin 'Umar, and also agrees with the marfu' hadith reported in al-Hidayah, which al-Kamal ibn al-Humam cited in Fath al-Qadir with a continuous chain of transmission via Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Razi from the Mother of the Believers 'A'isha al-Siddiqah, may Allah be pleased with her: 'It is not permissible for a father to testify for his son, nor a son for his father, nor a wife for her husband, nor a husband for his wife, nor a slave for his master, nor a master for his slave, nor a partner for his partner, nor an employee for his employer.' And the opposition of Masruq is like the judgment of Solomon opposing the judgment of David regarding the crop and the son, as narrated in the two Sahihs.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This appendix (tadhyil) reinforces the distinction between a Sahabi and a Tabi'i in terms of legal authority. The Tabi'i, even if he is a great scholar like Shuraih or Masruq, does not have the same weight as a Sahabi because he did not personally hear from the Prophet nor witness the revelatory context. The text reports that the early Hanafi imams would accept the consensus of the Sahaba but would contest the opinions of the Tabi'in, treating them as peers in ijtihad. To counter an argument that the practice of Shuraih (a Tabi'i) being appointed as judge by 'Umar and his decisions being followed proves the hujjiyah of a Tabi'i's opinion, the author responds that Shuraih's specific ruling on testimony (refusing to accept a son's testimony for his father) actually agreed with 'Umar's position and with a marfu' hadith from 'A'isha, so it is not an independent proof. Similarly, Masruq's disagreement with Ibn 'Abbas on a vow matter shows disagreement but does not prove that the Tabi'i's opinion is binding. The author concludes that such examples do not establish the Tabi'i's opinion as a hujjah; rather, they show that when a Tabi'i contradicts a Sahabi, he may be in line with another Sahabi or a hadith. Thus, the Tabi'i's opinion does not carry the authority of the Sahabi's.

Key Terms
التابعي (al-tabi'i): A follower (successor) who met the Companions but did not meet the Prophet; in usul, his opinion does not carry the same authority as a Sahabi's because he did not hear from the Prophet directly.
شريح (Shuraih): A prominent Tabi'i judge appointed by 'Umar; his example is used to argue against the hujjiyah of the Tabi'i because his rulings actually align with other Sahaba or hadith.
السماع (al-sam'): Direct hearing from the Prophet; a key attribute that makes a Sahabi's statement authoritative.
القرائن (al-qara'in): Contextual clues that accompany revelation, witnessed by the Sahaba but not the Tabi'in.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the example of Shuraih not prove that the Tabi'i's opinion is a hujjah?
A) Because Shuraih was not a reliable narrator.
B) Because Shuraih's ruling on the testimony agreed with 'Umar's opinion and a marfu' hadith.
C) Because Shuraih's opinion was rejected by 'Ali.
D) Because Shuraih was not a judge in the time of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
A Tabi'i's opinion is not a hujjah because it lacks direct hearing from the Prophet and witnessing of revelatory context, distinguishing it from a Sahabi's statement.

Resolving Apparent Contradictions Between Quran and Sunnah
Explains the divine nature of Sunnah and the method to resolve apparent contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for resolving apparent contradictions between Quran and Sunnah by dropping both conflicting strong proofs and acting upon the weaker evidence that remains.

Core Idea
Quran and Sunnah are both divine revelation; apparent contradictions are resolved by discarding both and using weaker evidence.

This lesson presents a key principle in Hanafi usul: the Sunnah is revelation like the Quran, so they cannot truly contradict. When faced with an apparent irresolvable contradiction, the Hanafi school applies a unique method—abandoning both strong conflicting proofs and relying on the weaker evidence that is left. This approach, based on consensus, simplifies the matter and ensures action is based on proof.

Guided Path
1
Establish the premise
Recognize that both Quran and Sunnah are divine revelation from Allah, who does not err or forget. Therefore, any apparent contradiction is only apparent.
The text emphasizes ‘لا حكم إلا لله’ (there is no ruling except from Allah).
2
Exhaust tarjih options
Determine that weighing (tarjih) between the conflicting proofs is impossible; no preference can be given.
The passage mentions ‘تعذر الترجيح’ (impossibility of weighing).
3
Identify the available approaches
Understand the various invalid approaches: acting arbitrarily, choosing one without basis, or acting on the original without proof.
The text dismisses these as fallacious (e.g., ‘تخيير بين ما هو حرام وواجب’).
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
Drop both conflicting strong proofs (as if they were never revealed) because they cancel each other. Then the weaker proof (the next strongest evidence) remains without opposition and can be acted upon.
The text says: ‘فكأنهما لم ينزلا من الأصل’ (as if they had not been revealed originally).
5
Confirm the consensus
Note that this method is supported by consensus of the scholars and makes the matter practical.
The author cites Matali' al-Asrar: ‘الإجماع قد انعقد على إهدار القويين والعمل بالأدنى’ (consensus on dropping the two strong and acting on the lower).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني/ السنة ولا يفقهه هذا العبد حق الفقه لأن السنة ليست إلا بالوحي، إذ لا حكم إلا لله، فالسنة والكتاب كلاهما كاشفان عن حكم الهي، والتعارض إنما وقع بين الحكمين، وهو كلام الله تعالى الأزلي وهو كلام متكلم واحد وأيضاً : الكلامان الصادران عن متكلم واحد صادق فيهما لا يضل ولا ينسى قطعاً، سواء في المطابقة، وإذا صدر عن متكلم آخر صادق قطعاً ليس له فضل على ذينك الكلامين المتناقضين والقياس على الشاهد باطل، لأنهما غير مقطوعي الصدق، فإذا صدر عنه كلام متناقض أوجب الريبة في الحفظ أو العدالة، فوقع الريبة في الصدق، فلا يقبل وههنا لا مساغ للريبة أصلاً ، بل متكلم السنة صادق قطعاً، كمتكلم الكتاب، فلا بد من مطابقتهما وهو التعارض وأما الفرعان فثمرة شجرة فاسدة ونقص ما هو الحق فيه، وغاية ما يقال في هذا المقام أنه إذا وقع التعارض وتعذر الترجيح فإما أن يتقاعد كل من الآية والخبر الموافق له والقياس الموافق له بمعارضة الآية الأخرى، إياه فيتعذر العمل في الحادثة، وذا لا يمكن ولا يمكن أن يقال : يعمل بالأصل، لأن الأصل إما دليل فهو أيضاً معارض فيتقاعد عن الحجية، وإما ليس دليلاً فيلزم العمل من غير دليل وإما أن يعمل بواحد منهما على سبيل التخيير، وذلك تخيير بين ما هو حرام العمل وواجب العمل، لأن أحدهما منسوخ قطعاً، وهو حرام العمل، وإما أن يعمل بإحدى الآيتين دون الأخرى، وهو ترجيح من غير مرجح، وإما أن يعتبرا دليلين متعارضين أو لا، ولا يعتبر ما هو أدون منهما. إذ الضعيف يضمحل عند مقابلة القوى ولا يستطيع معارضته ثم يتساقطان للمعارضة، فكأنهما لم ينزلا من الأصل، وإذا ارتفعا من البين بقي الدليل الأدنى من غير معارض، فيعمل به، فهذا هو الباقي فتأمل فيه، وقال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره: قد رأيت في بعض كتب الأصول أن القياس أن تهدر الحجج كلها ، لكن الإجماع قد انعقد على إهدار القويين والعمل بالأدنى، وإذا ثبت هذا يسهل الأمر جداً فافهم.
The second principle: Sunnah. And this servant does not fully comprehend it because Sunnah is only through revelation, since there is no ruling except from Allah. So the Sunnah and the Book are both revealers of a divine ruling. Contradiction only occurs between two rulings, and they are the speech of Allah, the Eternal, and it is the speech of a single speaker. Also: two statements issuing from a single truthful speaker who does not err or forget definitely, they are equal in correspondence. If they issued from another truthful speaker, he has no superiority over those two contradictory statements, and analogy upon the witnessed is invalid because they are not definitely truthful. So if contradictory speech issues from him, it causes suspicion in memory or justice, so suspicion falls upon truthfulness, so it is not accepted. But here there is no room for suspicion at all; rather, the speaker of the Sunnah is definitely truthful, like the speaker of the Book, so they must correspond—that is the contradiction. As for the two secondary matters, they are the fruit of a corrupt tree and a deficiency of what is truth in it. The utmost that can be said in this regard: when contradiction occurs and weighing is impossible, then either each of the verse and the report that agrees with it and the analogy that agrees with it are incapacitated by the other verse opposing it, so action becomes impossible in the incident—and that is not possible. And it cannot be said: act upon the original, because the original is either a proof, so it is also opposed and becomes incapacitated for authority, or it is not a proof, so action without proof is incumbent. Or act upon one of them by way of choice—and that is a choice between what is forbidden to act upon and what is obligatory to act upon, because one of them is definitely abrogated, and it is forbidden to act upon it. Or act upon one of the two verses without the other—and that is weighing without a weight. Or consider them as two conflicting proofs or not, and do not consider the lower of them. For the weak one disappears when faced with the strong and cannot oppose it, then they both fall due to opposition, as if they had not been revealed originally. And when they are removed from consideration, the weaker proof remains without opposition, so it is acted upon. This is the remaining one, so ponder upon it. And the author of Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya, may his secret be sanctified, said: I have seen in some books of usul that the analogical conclusion is that all proofs are dropped, but consensus has been reached on dropping the two strong ones and acting upon the lower. If this is established, the matter becomes very easy, so understand.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage opens with the second principle, which is the position of the Sunnah in Hanafi usul. The author emphasizes that the Sunnah, like the Quran, is divine revelation (wahy). Therefore, any apparent contradiction between the Quran and the Sunnah cannot be real, because both originate from the same divine source, Allah, who is one and does not contradict Himself. The text then explores what to do if an apparent contradiction seems irresolvable: it dismisses various fallacious approaches (such as acting arbitrarily, choosing one without weighting, or disregarding both). The correct approach, as supported by a cited authority, is to drop the two strong conflicting evidences and act upon the weaker evidence that remains. This principle is foundational for dealing with ta'arud in Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The sayings, actions, and approvals of the Prophet Muhammad, which are revelation.
الوحي (al-wahy): Divine revelation sent down to the Prophet.
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two evidences that cannot be reconciled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are both transmitted by the same people.
B) Because both are from Allah, who is One and does not contradict Himself.
C) Because the Sunnah is always inferior to the Quran.
D) Because contradictions are only apparent and can be resolved by qiyas.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, apparent contradictions between Quran and Sunnah are resolved by dropping both conflicting proofs and acting upon the weaker evidence that remains.

Resolving Conflicting Reports: The Prophet's Marriage to Maimuna
Applies affirmation/negation rule to reports about Prophet's state in Maimuna marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi tarjīḥ principles (preference of affirmation over negation, action over general statement) to conflicting ḥadīth and derive the ruling on marriage by a muhrim.

Core Idea
A witnessed specific action overrides a general prohibition when the narrator is more reliable.

This passage from Fawātiḥ al-Raḥamūt demonstrates how Hanafī uṣūl al-fiqh resolves apparent contradictions between reports of the Prophet’s action (fi‘l) and general statements (qawl). The specific case—whether the Prophet married Maimuna while in ihrām or while ḥalāl—becomes a test for the tarjīḥ rule that affirmation (ithbāt) is preferred over negation (nafy) when the negation is based on the original state. The analysis then extends to the broader inter-madhhab dispute on whether a muhrim may contract marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
The first report (Ibn ‘Abbās) states the Prophet married Maimuna while in ihrām (affirmation of a specific state). The second set of reports (Zayd ibn al-Aṣamm, Abū Rāfi‘, etc.) state he married while ḥalāl (negation of ihrām). Also a report from Sulaymān ibn Yasār suggests the marriage occurred before he left Madīnah.
2
Apply the Hanafī tarjīḥ rule for affirmation vs. negation
According to Hanafī uṣūl, when a report affirms a specific state contrary to the original state (negation), the affirmation is given preference because it is based on direct observation, while the negation is based on the assumption of the original state (no ihrām unless proven). Ibn ‘Abbās’s report is an ithbāt, so it outweighs the nafy reports.
This principle is rooted in the idea that the original state is the absence of ihrām, but direct observation overrides the default.
3
Analyze narrator reliability and chain strength
Ibn ‘Abbās is considered stronger in ḍabṭ (precision), fiqh (jurisprudence), ‘adāla (justice), and wara‘ (piety) compared to Zayd ibn al-Aṣamm and Abū Rāfi‘. Al-Zuhrī’s remark diminishes the credibility of Ibn al-Aṣamm. The chains of negation reports are also disconnected (munqaṭi‘), as Sulaymān ibn Yasār was born after the event.
The text notes that even if the chains were equal, qiyās would support the Hanafī position.
4
Extend to the broader Shāfi‘ī-Hanafī dispute
The Shāfi‘ī school relies on the general hadith “lā yankihu al-muḥrim” (the muhrim should not marry) from Muslim and Sunan. The Hanafī response: (1) Ibn ‘Abbās’s witnessed action is preferred over the general statement; (2) marriage is analogous to purchase (qiyās), which is not prohibited; (3) the prohibition can be interpreted as referring to intercourse, not the contract.
Also, Caliph ‘Umar annulled a muhrim’s marriage, but Hanafīs argue this is a single opinion counterbalanced by stronger evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf (practical consequence)
Shāfi‘īs rule that a marriage contract by a muhrim is invalid (bāṭil). Hanafīs rule it is valid (ṣaḥīḥ) and only the ḥajj may be affected if consummated. This difference has real implications for the validity of marriages contracted during ḥajj or ‘umra.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنقول (وفي تزوج ميمونة) كما روى الستة عن ابن عباس : تزوج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ميمونة وهو محرم كما في التيسير» (نفي للحل اللاحق) المنقول (على الأشهر كما يدل عليه هيئة محرم . محسوسة) إحرامية فعارض (رواية مسلم وابن ماجه عن زيد بن الأصم : حدثتني ميمونة : (تزوجها وهو حلال) وفي رواية أبي يعلى بعد أن رجعنا إلى المدينة وفي رواية الترمذي وابن خزيمة وابن حبان عن أبي رافع أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم تزوّج ميمونة وهو حلال، وبنى بها وهو حلال، وكنت الرسول بينهما، كذا في التيسير» (ورجح أن ابن عباس يزيد على يزيد بن الأصم وأبي رافع ضبطاً وإتقاناً قال الزهري : ما ندري ابن الأصم أعرابي بوال على ساقه أنجعله مثل ابن عباس وأن سند النفي أقوى فإن رواته كلهم أئمة فقهاء كما قال الطحاوي) وقوله على الأشهر إشارة إلى ما روى مالك في الموطأ) عن سليمان بن يسار قال : بعث النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أبا رافع مولاه ورجلاً من الأنصار فزوجا ميمونة بنت الحارث ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالمدينة قبل أن يخرج، ففيه نفي للإحرام، وعلى هذا قال الشيخ ابن الهمام إن هذا الإخبار بالأصل، فترجح عليه رواية ابن عباس لكونه عن الدليل، ولا يذهب عليك أن هذا الإخبار أيضاً بالدليل لأنه لا إحرام قبل الخروج، وأيضاً أنه منقطع فإنه على ما نقل في التقرير عن ابن عبد البر أن سليمان ولد سنة أربع وثلاثين، وأبو رافع مات قبل شهادة أمير المؤمنين عثمان بسنتين، فلا يعارض المسند، ( المصدر الثاني / السنة وإنما التعارض في الخبرين المذكورين سابقاً فافهم واعلم أن الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لم يجوّز نكاح المحرم ،والمحرمة وجوّزه أئمتنا، وتمسك بقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : «لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح رواه أصحاب السنن ومسلم وأجاب الشيخ ابن الهمام بأنه عارض رواية ابن عباس نكاح أم المؤمنين ميمونة وهو محرم وابن عباس أقوى ضبطاً وفقهاً وعدالة وورعاً، فالترجيح له، ولو سلم التساوي تساقطاً ووجب الرجوع إلى القياس، وهو مؤيد لنا لأن النكاح كالشراء للتسري وهو غير ممنوع بالإحرام، ثم إنه لو امتنع بالإحرام فلا يزيد على حقيقة الوطء المحرم وهو إنما يوجب فساد الحج، فكذا النكاح لو امتنع أفسد الحج، ولا وجه لفساد لفساد النكاح أصلاً، ولو صير إلى الجمع فهو أيضاً معناً، فيحمل النكاح على الوطء، والخطابة الواقعة في هذا الحديث في رواية مسلم وأبي داود: ولا يخطب» على التمكين للوطء . ولا تحتمل رواية ابن عباس هذا التوجيه وقد يؤاخذ عليه بأن القول يترجح إذا عارض الفعل، لأن الفعل يحتمل الاختصاص دون القول، لا سيما إذا وقعت روايات الفعل متعارضة. وأيضاً : روى الإمام مالك أن أبا غطفان أخبره أن أباه طريفاً تزوج امرأة وهو محرم، فرد عمر بن الخطاب نكاحه وقول الصحابي مرجح في صورة التعارض، وترجيح القياس بعده، لا سيما قول مثل أمير المؤمنين الذي لا يخفى عليه مثل هذا الحكم، ففعله دليل بقاء الحكم، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن الأولى في المؤاخذة أن يقال : إن القول عام فالتعارض إنما هو في حقه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام لا في حقنا لأنه لم يدل دليل وعلى التأسي، وأما ترجيح القول في هذه الصورة فمحل تأمل
The transmitted report (concerning the marriage of Maimuna) as narrated by the six [Imams] from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah married Maimuna while he was in ihrām.' This is in al-Taysīr. (It is a negation of the later permissibility) transmitted (according to the most famous [view] as indicated by a clearly visible state of ihrām). It was contradicted by the narration of Muslim and Ibn Mājah from Zayd ibn al-Asamm: 'Maimuna told me: He married her while he was halāl.' And in the narration of Abū Ya'lā: 'After we returned to Madīnah.' And in the narration of al-Tirmidhī, Ibn Khuzayma, and Ibn Hibbān from Abū Rāfi': 'The Prophet married Maimuna while he was halāl, and consummated with her while halāl, and I was the messenger between them.' (It is preferred that Ibn 'Abbas exceeds Zayd ibn al-Asamm and Abū Rāfi' in precision and mastery. Al-Zuhrī said: 'We don't know if Ibn al-Asamm is a Bedouin who urinates on his own leg that we should make him like Ibn 'Abbas.' And the chain of negation is stronger because its narrators are all imams and jurists, as al-Tahāwī said.) His statement 'on the most famous' refers to what Mālik narrated in al-Muwatta' from Sulaymān ibn Yasār: 'The Prophet sent Abū Rāfi' and a man from the Anṣār to marry Maimuna bint al-Ḥārith while the Messenger was in Madīnah before he left [for the 'umra].' This contains a negation of ihrām. On this, al-Sheikh Ibn al-Humām said: 'This report is based on the original state, so the narration of Ibn 'Abbas prevails because it is based on evidence.' But do not be unaware that this report is also by evidence because there is no ihrām before departure. Also, it is disconnected: according to Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, Sulaymān was born in the year 34 [AH], and Abū Rāfi' died two years before the martyrdom of 'Uthmān, so it does not contradict the musnad. The second source: The Sunnah. And the conflict is only in the two reports mentioned previously. Understand and know that al-Shāfi'ī (may Allah have mercy on him) did not permit the marriage of a muhrim (male or female), while our imams permitted it. He adhered to his statement: 'A muhrim should not marry nor be married.' This was narrated by the authors of Sunan and Muslim. Al-Sheikh Ibn al-Humām replied that it is contradicted by Ibn 'Abbas's narration of the marriage of Maimuna while he was in ihrām, and Ibn 'Abbas is stronger in precision, jurisprudence, justice, and piety, so preference is given to him. Even if equality is assumed, they fall and qiyās must be resorted to, which supports us, because marriage is like purchase for concubinage, which is not prohibited by ihrām. Then, if it were prohibited by ihrām, it is no more than actual prohibited intercourse, which only invalidates the Ḥajj. So also marriage, if prohibited, would invalidate the Ḥajj, and there is no ground for invalidating the marriage itself. If one attempts to harmonize, it also agrees with us: interpret 'nikāḥ' as 'intercourse,' and 'khuṭba' (engagement) in the ḥadīth of Muslim and Abū Dāwūd ('nor propose') as 'enabling intercourse.' Ibn 'Abbas's narration cannot be interpreted in this way. It may be objected that speech (qaul) is given preference when it contradicts action (fi'l), because action may be specific while speech is general. Especially since the action narrations conflict. Also, Mālik narrated that Abū Ghuṭafān told him that his father Ṭarīf married a woman while in ihrām, and 'Umar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb annulled his marriage. The statement of a Companion is preferred in a case of conflict, and qiyās after it, especially the statement of the Commander of the Faithful, to whom such a ruling is not hidden. So his action is evidence of the continuance of the ruling. And it should not be hidden from you that the first criticism is to say: the speech is general, so the conflict is only concerning him (the Prophet) and not concerning us, because there is no evidence of following (ta'siya). As for preferring the speech in this case, it is a matter of reflection.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage applies the usul rule of affirmation vs negation to a specific historical dispute: the state of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during his marriage to Maimuna. The conflict is between two groups of reports: one from Ibn 'Abbas stating the Prophet was in ihrām (affirmation of a specific state), and another from Zayd ibn al-Asamm, Abū Rāfi', and others stating he was halāl (negation of ihrām). The Hanafi response, following the principle that affirmation is preferred when negation is based on original state, argues that Ibn 'Abbas's report carries more weight due to his superior reliability. Additionally, the Hanafis consider the negation reports as based on original state (no ihrām unless proven). The passage then moves to the broader Shāfi'ī-Hanafī dispute on whether a muhrim may marry. The Shāfi'īs rely on the general hadith 'The muhrim should not marry,' while Hanafis defend their position by: (1) preferring Ibn 'Abbas's witnessed action over the general statement; (2) argument by qiyās that marriage is like purchase of a slave-girl, which is not prohibited; (3) explaining that the hadith of prohibition can be interpreted as prohibiting intercourse, not the contract. The passage also mentions the action of Caliph 'Umar who annulled a marriage contracted in ihrām, but Hanafis consider this a single opinion not overriding the stronger evidence. The overall thrust is to show how usul principles are applied to resolve conflicting reports and school disputes.

Key Terms
المحرم (al-muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihrām for Hajj or 'Umrah, during which certain acts are prohibited.
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): The process of giving preference to one evidence over another due to stronger reliability or other factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the primary reason the Hanafīs prefer Ibn ‘Abbās's report over the negation reports?
A) Ibn ‘Abbās was a relative of the Prophet
B) The negation reports are all from the same chain
C) Ibn ‘Abbās's report is an affirmation of a specific state and he is more reliable than other narrators
D) The negation reports were narrated by women only

Key Takeaway
When conflicting reports arise, Hanafī uṣūl prioritises affirmation over negation and the reliability of the narrator, leading to the preferred ruling that a muhrim's marriage is valid.

Resolving Ta'āruḍ: Marriage of a Muhrim
Response to Shafi'i position on marriage in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of tarjih (preference) between contradictory hadiths and evaluate the role of qiyas when textual evidence conflicts.

Core Idea
When a prophetic action contradicts a saying, the saying is preferred unless the action is proven to be general.

This lesson examines the classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding marriage while in the state of ihram. The Shafi'i school relies on the explicit prohibition in the hadith 'لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح', while the Hanafis counter with a narration of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet himself married Maymunah while in ihram. Through this case, we explore how Hanafi usul al-fiqh resolves ta'āruḍ (contradiction) by applying tarjīḥ (preference) based on the narrator's qualifications, and when necessary, resorting to qiyas. The passage also addresses the objection from Caliph Umar's action and highlights the nuance of whether the contradiction lies in the Prophet's own actions or in the ruling for the ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contradictory evidences
First, locate the two primary textual proofs: (1) the prophetic saying 'لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح' prohibiting marriage for a Muhrim, and (2) the narration of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet married Maymunah while in ihram (an action).
One is a saying (qaul), the other an action (fi'l).
2
Apply Hanafi tarjih criteria
Compare the narrators of the two reports. The Hanafi scholar Ibn al-Humam states that Ibn Abbas is stronger in memory (ḍabṭ), jurisprudence (fiqh), justice (ʿadāla), and piety (waraʿ), so his narration is preferred over the prohibitory hadith.
Tarjih is based on the qualities of the narrator, not merely the number of chains.
3
Fallback to qiyas if equality assumed
Even if the two reports were considered equal and dropped (tasāqutā), the Hanafis resort to qiyas: marriage is analogous to purchase for concubinage (shirāʾ li-l-tasarrī), which is permitted during ihram. Thus, qiyas supports permissibility.
The ʿilla (effective cause) is the acquisition of the right to intercourse.
4
Address objection from Caliph Umar's action
Consider the report that Caliph Umar invalidated a marriage in ihram. The Hanafi response notes that the prophetic saying is general and the contradiction is only regarding the Prophet himself, not binding on the ummah because no evidence indicates that his actions are to be followed (taʾassī) in every case.
This distinguishes between obligations from sayings vs. actions.
5
Evaluate the overall tarjih
After weighing the evidences, the Hanafi position (permissibility) is preferred because of the stronger narration and supporting qiyas. The Shafi'i position, based on the explicit prohibition, is acknowledged but outweighed.
This case illustrates how multiple usul tools (tarjih, qiyas, and the rule regarding actions) work together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني / السنة وإنما التعارض في الخبرين المذكورين سابقاً فافهم واعلم أن الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لم يجوّز نكاح المحرم ،والمحرمة وجوّزه أئمتنا، وتمسك بقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : «لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح رواه أصحاب السنن ومسلم وأجاب الشيخ ابن الهمام بأنه عارض رواية ابن عباس نكاح أم المؤمنين ميمونة وهو محرم وابن عباس أقوى ضبطاً وفقهاً وعدالة وورعاً، فالترجيح له، ولو سلم التساوي تساقطاً ووجب الرجوع إلى القياس، وهو مؤيد لنا لأن النكاح كالشراء للتسري وهو غير ممنوع بالإحرام، ثم إنه لو امتنع بالإحرام فلا يزيد على حقيقة الوطء المحرم وهو إنما يوجب فساد الحج، فكذا النكاح لو امتنع أفسد الحج، ولا وجه لفساد لفساد النكاح أصلاً، ولو صير إلى الجمع فهو أيضاً معناً، فيحمل النكاح على الوطء، والخطابة الواقعة في هذا الحديث في رواية مسلم وأبي داود: ولا يخطب» على التمكين للوطء . ولا تحتمل رواية ابن عباس هذا التوجيه وقد يؤاخذ عليه بأن القول يترجح إذا عارض الفعل، لأن الفعل يحتمل الاختصاص دون القول، لا سيما إذا وقعت روايات الفعل متعارضة. وأيضاً : روى الإمام مالك أن أبا غطفان أخبره أن أباه طريفاً تزوج امرأة وهو محرم، فرد عمر بن الخطاب نكاحه وقول الصحابي مرجح في صورة التعارض، وترجيح القياس بعده، لا سيما قول مثل أمير المؤمنين الذي لا يخفى عليه مثل هذا الحكم، ففعله دليل بقاء الحكم، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن الأولى في المؤاخذة أن يقال : إن القول عام فالتعارض إنما هو في حقه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام لا في حقنا لأنه لم يدل دليل وعلى التأسي، وأما ترجيح القول في هذه الصورة فمحل تأمل
The second principle: the Sunnah. The contradiction is only in the two reports mentioned previously, so understand. Know that al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, did not permit marriage for a Muhrim man or woman, whereas our imams permitted it. He (al-Shafi'i) adhered to his saying, peace and blessings upon him and his family: 'The Muhrim shall not marry nor be married,' narrated by the authors of the Sunan and Muslim. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam replied that it is contradicted by the narration of Ibn Abbas that he married Umm al-Mu'minin Maymunah while he was in ihram, and Ibn Abbas is stronger in memory, jurisprudence, justice, and piety, so preference is given to him. Even if equality is assumed, they both drop and one must resort to qiyas, which supports us because marriage is like purchase for concubinage, which is not prohibited by ihram. Then, if it were prohibited by ihram, it is not more than the reality of prohibited intercourse, which only causes the invalidation of Hajj. Similarly, if marriage is prohibited, it would invalidate Hajj, but there is no basis for the invalidation of the marriage itself. If one resorts to reconciliation, that also is with us: the marriage is interpreted as intercourse, and 'nor propose' occurring in this hadith in the narration of Muslim and Abu Dawud is interpreted as enabling intercourse. The narration of Ibn Abbas cannot bear this interpretation. He may be objected that the saying is preponderant when it contradicts an action, because the action may be specific whereas the saying is not, especially when the narrations of the action are contradictory. Also, Imam Malik narrated that Abu Ghutfan informed him that his father Tarif married a woman while in ihram, and Umar ibn al-Khattab invalidated his marriage. The saying of a Companion is preponderant in case of contradiction, and qiyas afterwards is also preponderant, especially the saying of the Commander of the Faithful, to whom such a ruling is not hidden. So his action is evidence of the continuation of the ruling. It is not hidden from you that the proper way to object is to say: The saying is general, so the contradiction is only regarding him, peace and blessings upon him and his family, not regarding us, because there is no evidence for following [his actions]. As for preferring the saying in this situation, it is subject to reflection.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute regarding the permissibility of marriage for a person in the state of ihram. The Shafi'i school prohibits it based on the hadith 'The Muhrim shall not marry nor be married.' The Hanafi school responds by noting a stronger narration from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet himself married Maymunah while in ihram. Since Ibn Abbas is more reliable, his narration takes precedence. Additionally, even if the two reports were equal, the Hanafi school relies on qiyas (analogy) to purchase for concubinage, which is permitted in ihram. The text also addresses the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab invalidating such a marriage, but the Hanafi response is that the contradiction is only in the Prophet's own actions, not binding on the ummah. The commentary by Shaykh Ibn al-Humam provides these arguments, and the passage closes by noting that the preferred view is subject to reflection.

Key Terms
مُحْرِم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah.
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): Contradiction between two authoritative proofs that cannot both be applied.
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Preferring one evidence over another due to strength (e.g., narrator reliability, chain).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the marriage of a Muhrim permitted despite the hadith 'لا ينكح المحرم ولا ينكح'?
A) The hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
B) The narration of Ibn Abbas (that the Prophet married Maymunah in ihram) is stronger and takes precedence.
C) The hadith is abrogated by a later revelation.
D) The Hanafi school allows it by analogy to sale, which is also permitted in ihram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage in ihram by preferring the stronger narration of Ibn Abbas and supporting it with qiyas to purchase for concubinage.

Definition and Ruling of Tarjih (Preponderance) in Usul al-Fiqh
Definition and ruling of tarjih with example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Shafi'i definition of tarjih, identify its ruling as wajib to act by the preponderant, and apply the concept by analyzing a conflict of evidences to determine the preponderant factor.

Core Idea
Tarjih compares conflicting evidences to determine the stronger probabilistically; acting by the preponderant is obligatory by consensus.

This passage introduces tarjih, a key tool when faced with conflicting evidences of equal authority but differing probability. While the definition is from the Shafi'i school, the principle of preferring the stronger evidence is universal. The passage also demonstrates tarjih through a famous example: preferring Aisha's narration over the Ansar's on the nullification of wudu.

Guided Path
1
1. Extract the definition of tarjih
Find the Shafi'i definition: 'the accompaniment of evidence with that by which it outweighs its opposite in providing probability.' Note the scope: only in zann (probable) matters, not qat' (certain).
The definition restricts tarjih to the realm of probability, excluding certainties.
2
2. Identify the ruling of tarjih
The passage states that tarjih 'necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the outweighed.' This is supported by ijma' (consensus) of the Companions and a rational proof: considering the outweighed in the presence of the preponderant is contrary to reason.
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) for the mujtahid once tarjih is performed.
3
3. Examine the example of tarjih
Two hadiths conflict: one from Aisha and one from the Ansar on the issue of wudu after ghusl. The Companions preferred Aisha's version because she was more knowledgeable in such matters, illustrating tarjih by the narrator's expertise.
This shows that qualitative factors (knowledge, specialization) can outweigh quantitative factors (number of narrators).
4
4. Understand the Shafi'i position on takhsis
The commentator notes that the Shafi'is allow particularizing a general text (takhsis) with something inferior in probability, which conflicts with the strict application of tarjih. This highlights a methodological difference.
The Hanafi position tends to be more restrictive in allowing takhsis when tarjih would indicate preponderance.
5
5. Analyze the objection against the example
An objection is raised: the testimony of four (witnesses) contradicts the testimony of two. Though incomplete, this suggests that the claim of Aisha's superiority was challenged by a rule from another field (shahada). Consider how tarjih must be consistent across fields.
The objection may be that quantitative testimony rules conflict with qualitative narrator preference, requiring further resolution.

Chapter on Tarjih. (It is in the terminology of the Shafi'is: the accompaniment of evidence with that by which it outweighs its opposite in providing probability, since there is no conflict for them in certainties. And they also permitted tarjih by abundance of evidences.) (And it) i.e. tarjih, (necessitates acting by the preponderant and dropping the outweighed) according to the majority of usul scholars, due to certainty from the Companions and those after them, so it is a matter of consensus. Also: considering the outweighed in the presence of the preponderant is contrary to reason. But then it invalidates what the Shafi'is claimed, that in the particularizer there must be participation in the source of probability but not in degree, so they permitted particularizing the general with what is inferior in probability. (And from it) i.e. from tarjih, (is their preferring) in practice (the narration of) the Mother of the Believers (Aisha) al-Siddiqah (over the saying) of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) which the Ansar narrated: ('Water is only from water') because the purified wives were more knowledgeable of this matter. Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of tarjih (preponderance) in usul al-fiqh. It gives the Shafi'i definition as 'the accompaniment of evidence with that by which it outweighs its opposite in providing probability,' noting that for Shafi'is, tarjih applies only in matters of probability (zann) not certainty. The commentator then explains that tarjih requires acting by the preponderant and discarding the outweighed, a principle established by consensus (ijma) of the Companions. A rational proof is also given: it is irrational to consider the outweighed evidence when a stronger one exists. However, this principle challenges the Shafi'i doctrine that a particularizer (takhsis) must share the same source of probability (asl al-zann) but not necessarily the same degree, allowing them to particularize a general text with something weaker in probability—this is inconsistent with the strict application of tarjih. An example of tarjih is given: the Companions preferred the hadith of Aisha ('Water is only from water') over the hadith of the Ansar on the same matter because Aisha had more knowledge of such matters. The last line mentions an objection based on testimony rules (shahada), but the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The accompaniment of evidence with that by which it outweighs its opposite in providing probability.
الراجح (al-rajih): The evidence that outweighs its opposite.
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The evidence that is outweighed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tarjih is a fundamental usul tool that resolves conflicts between equally authentic but probabilistically differing evidences, and it is wajib to act by the preponderant.

Tarjih of Denial Over Affirmation When Fame Lacking
Explaining tarjih of denial over affirmation when fame expected but absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih between denial (nafy) and affirmation (ithbat) in matters where widespread transmission is expected but absent.

Core Idea
Denial is preferred when fame is expected but the affirming report is unknown.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, when dealing with reports that contradict each other, preference (tarjih) is given based on certain criteria. This passage presents a key rule: in matters that are normally widely known (like basic rulings of wudu), a report that denies a ruling is preferred over a report that affirms it, if the affirming report lacks fame. This principle protects established norms from being undermined by obscure or weak affirming reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of report
Determine whether the report is negative (nafy) — stating that something is not a ruling or not established — or positive (ithbat) — stating that something is a ruling or established.
The passage focuses on reports about matters that are expected to be widely known (shuhra).
2
Assess the fame of the affirmative report
Check if the affirmative report is well-known (mashhur) or widely transmitted. If the matter is one in which fame is expected (e.g., basic obligations), an affirmative report that is not famous is considered weak.
Fame is the norm: al-ghalib fih al-shuhra.
3
Apply the tarjih rule
If the affirmative report lacks fame in a matter where fame is normal, the negative report is given preponderance over it. The negative report is considered stronger because it aligns with the expected widespread knowledge.
Example: hadith on wudu nullification by touching private parts — the negative report (no nullification) is preferred over the less famous affirmative report.
4
Understand the exception for denial by accusation
Distinguish between 'denial by silence' (inkar sukun) and 'denial by accusation of lying' (takdhib). Only if denial is by accusation of lying does the report become completely invalid by consensus. Otherwise, the negative report remains a valid proof and can be given preference.
The passage specifically restricts the discussion to denial by silence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وما لم ينكر الأصل) روايته إنكار سكوت (على ما أنكر ذلك لا يرى سقوط الحديث ،به وإنما قيدنا الإنكار بإنكار السكوت، لأنه إذا أنكر الإنكار عند من إنكار التكذيب سقط الخبر عن الحجية إجماعاً فلا اعتداد به حتى يعارض الصحيح منه ويطلب الترجيح (والنفي) يترجح على الإثبات فيما الغالب فيه الشهرة لو كان (ولم يشتهر) كحديث انتقاض الوضوء بمس الذكر على حديث الانتقاض به وحديث مس رجل أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة في الصلاة على حديث انتقاضه بمس النساء الظاهر إسقاط هذا الكلام، فإن الإثبات فيما الغالب فيه الشهرة مع عدم الاشتهار ،مردود ولا يعمل به لو انفرد عن المعارض عندنا، فلا يصلح معارضاً لحديث النفي، فلا يطلب الترجيح
And what is not denied in origin: its narration is denial by silence. As for what is denied by that, the hadith is not considered dropped. We only restrict denial to denial by silence, because if denial is of the type of accusation of lying (takdhib), the report drops from being a proof by consensus, so it is not considered until it is opposed by an authentic one and preference sought. And denial (nafy) is given preponderance over affirmation (ithbat) in matters where fame (shuhra) is the norm but [the affirming report] is not famous. For instance, the hadith about the nullification of wudu by touching the private parts over the hadith about nullification by touching it, and the hadith of touching the foot of Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha during prayer over the hadith of nullification by touching women. The apparent [intent] is to drop this statement, because affirmation in matters where fame is the norm, combined with lack of fame, is rejected and not acted upon alone if there is no opponent in our view. So it is not valid as an opponent to the denial hadith, hence no tarjih is sought.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage addresses tarjih between a report that denies a ruling (nafy) and one that affirms it (ithbat) when the matter is normally widely known but the affirming report lacks such fame. The principle is that denial is preferred. Examples include hadiths about wudu nullification by touching the private parts: the denying report (that it does not nullify) is preferred over the affirming one if the affirming report is not famous. Similarly, touching a woman's foot in prayer not nullifying versus nullification by touching women. The Hanafi position is that an affirming report that contradicts the general fame is rejected even if alone, so it cannot oppose a denying report that aligns with fame. The text also distinguishes between denial by silence and denial by accusation of lying; only the latter drops the hadith from consideration entirely.

Key Terms
النفي (al-nafy): Denial or negative report: a statement that something is not established or not a ruling.
الإثبات (al-ithbāt): Affirmation or positive report: a statement that something is established or a ruling exists.
الشهرة (al-shuhra): Fame or widespread transmission of a report or ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The affirming report if it is authentic.
B) The denying report if the affirming report is not famous.
C) Both are equal.
D) The affirming report regardless.

Key Takeaway
Denial (nafy) is preferred over affirmation (ithbat) when the matter would normally be well-known but the affirmative report lacks fame.

Tarjih in Sanad: Hanafi Priority of Narrator Reliability over Chain Height
Discussion of tarjih factors in sanad and Hanafi critique of prioritizing chain height

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria for tarjih in sanad and evaluate the strength of a chain based on narrator attributes rather than chain length.

Core Idea
A short chain with weak narrators is less reliable than a long chain with strong narrators: fiqh and memory matter more than chain height.

In hadith sciences, chain height is often prized for its proximity to the Prophet. However, the Hanafi school holds that the reliability of the narrator—his fiqh, memory, and piety—is the decisive factor. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on tarjih in sanad and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrator attributes for tarjih
From the source, list the three narrator attributes that strengthen a chain: fiqh (understanding), strong memory (dabt), and piety (wara'). These are the Hanafi criteria for preferring one chain over another.
Attributes are listed: فقه الراوي, قوة ضبطه, ورعه.
2
Understand the rationale for each attribute
A jurist narrator (faqih) preserves hadith correctly; a pious narrator avoids carelessness; a strong memorizer does not forget. This shows why each attribute reduces error in transmission.
The source explains: الفقيه يضبطه كما ينبغي والمتورع يبعد عنه التساهل وقوي الضبط لا ينسى
3
Analyze the Hanafi objection to chain height
Some scholars prefer high chains (few intermediaries) due to less error. Hanafis argue that few intermediaries may be weak, whereas many may be strong; thus, quality of narrators is decisive.
The source states: ربما تكون الوسائط القليلة كثيرة النسيان سيئة الفهم... والظن من رواية تلك الوسائط القليلة أضعف بكثير
4
Apply the Hanafi framework to the rafa' al-yadayn example
In the anecdote, al-Awza'i cited a short chain for raising hands. Abu Hanifa rejected it because it was 'not established', showing that a short chain alone does not suffice without checking narrator reliability and fiqh.
The chain: الزهري عن سالم عن أبيه. Hanafis did not accept it due to other criteria.
5
Evaluate a hypothetical chain using Hanafi criteria
Given two narrations—one with few weak narrators, another with many strong narrators—prefer the latter. Practice applying the three attributes to a new scenario.

(و) ترجيح السنن (في السند) يكون بفقه الراوي وقوة ضبطه وورعه) وهو الاعتياد بإتيان المستحبات والاجتناب عن المكروهات بل عن المباحات لحظ النفس أيضاً، فإن الفقيه يضبطه كما ينبغي والمتورع يبعد عنه التساهل وقوي الضبط لا ينسى كما تقدم من ترجيح ابن عباس على يزيد بن الأصم (و) يكون الترجيح بعلو (الإسناد وهو قلة الوسائط (قيل: قرب الإسناد قربة إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وذلك لقلة احتمال الغلط (خلافاً للحنفية ووجه قولهم أنه ربما تكون الوسائط القليلة كثيرة النسيان سيئة الفهم بمعنى الحديث والكثيرة قوية الحفظ قوية الذهن، فالظن من رواية تلك الوسائط القليلة أضعف بكثير من الحاصل عن وسائط كثيرة. فالاعتبار للفقاهة وقوة الضبط لا للقلة والكثرة، تأمل فيه . حكى ابن عيينة أن أبا حنيفة اجتمع مع الأوزاعي، فقال الأوزاعي : ما بالكم لا ترفعون عند الركوع، والرفع سنة؟ فقال أبو حنيفة : لأنه لم يثبت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فقال الأوزاعي : كيف وحدثني الزهري عن سالم عن أبيه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه
And the tarjih of traditions in the chain is by the fiqh of the narrator, strength of his memory, and his piety (wara'): that is, habitually performing supererogatory acts and avoiding disliked acts, even permissible ones for the sake of the ego. For the jurist (faqih) preserves it as it should be, the pious person stays far from carelessness, and the strong memorizer does not forget, as previously mentioned: preferring Ibn Abbas over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. And tarjih is also by the height of the chain, i.e., few intermediaries. It is said: proximity of chain is a means of nearness to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and is due to less probability of error. Contrary to the Hanafis. Their argument is that sometimes few intermediaries may be very forgetful, of poor understanding of the meaning of hadith, while many intermediaries may be strong in memorization and intelligence. So the conjecture from the narration of those few intermediaries is much weaker than that from many intermediaries. Therefore the consideration is for fiqh and strength of memory, not for fewness or manyness. Reflect on this. Ibn 'Uyayna narrated that Abu Hanifa met al-Awza'i. Al-Awza'i said: 'Why do you not raise your hands during bowing? Raising is sunna.' Abu Hanifa said: 'Because it has not been established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' Al-Awza'i said: 'How? I was told by al-Zuhri from Salim from his father that the Messenger of Allah...'
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers tarjih factors related to the chain (sanad). First, the narrator's fiqh (understanding of hadith), strong memory, and piety (wara') weigh positively; a jurist narrator preserves better, a pious narrator avoids carelessness, a strong memorizer does not forget. An example: Ibn Abbas was preferred over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. Second, height of chain (few intermediaries) is considered a virtue by some because it reduces error possibility and brings closeness to the Prophet. However, the Hanafi position disagrees: short chains may have weak narrators, while long chains may have strong ones; thus, what matters is the narrator's reliability, not chain length. The anecdote illustrates this: Abu Hanifa did not accept rafa' al-yadayn despite a short chain because the act was not established according to Hanafi criteria, emphasizing the importance of narrator fiqh and verification beyond chain length.

Key Terms
فقه الراوي (fiqh al-rāwī): The narrator's deep understanding of hadith and fiqh, enabling accurate transmission.
علو الإسناد (ʿuluww al-isnād): A high chain with few narrators between the transmitter and the Prophet.
الورع (al-waraʿ): Piety that leads to avoidance of even permissible things for caution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi objection to relying on high chains for tarjih?
A) High chains are always better.
B) Few intermediaries may be weak, and many may be strong.
C) High chains are not considered in Hanafi school.
D) The Prophet disliked high chains.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tarjih in sanad depends on narrator fiqh, memory, and piety, not chain length; a chain's strength is judged by narrator quality.
