Tarjih by Fiqh of the Narrator: Core Factors
Explaining primary factors for sanad preponderance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three primary factors (fiqh, dabt, wara) for sanad tarjih in Hanafi usul and apply them to evaluate conflicting chains, using the Abu Hanifa/al-Awza'i dispute as an example.

Core Idea
Fiqh of the narrator, not chain length, is the decisive factor in weighing conflicting hadith.

When two hadiths conflict, Hanafi usul prioritizes the chain of narrators based on their juristic understanding, memory, and piety. This lesson explains these factors and contrasts them with the common preference for high chains, using the famous debate between Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i.

Guided Path
1
Extract the primary factors
Read the first part of the passage and list the three qualities mentioned for tarjih: fiqh al-rawi, quwwat al-dabt, and wara'. Note the definition of wara' as avoiding even permissible acts for self-discipline.
These are the core Hanafi criteria.
2
Understand the refutation of uluww al-isnad
Read the section on 'uluww al-isnad. Identify the opposing view that a short chain reduces error probability. Then note the Hanafi counter-argument: few intermediaries may be weak in fiqh and memory, while a longer chain with strong narrators is more reliable.
The key insight: probability of error depends on narrator quality, not chain length.
3
Analyze the Abu Hanifa/al-Awza'i anecdote
Read the anecdote carefully. Identify the two chains: al-Awza'i's (al-Zuhri → Salim → Ibn Umar) and Abu Hanifa's (Hammad → Ibrahim → Alqamah and al-Aswad → Ibn Mas'ud). Observe how Abu Hanifa argues that his narrators are more knowledgeable in fiqh, outweighing the shorter chain.
This is the classic illustration of the Hanafi method.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Consider a scenario: Chain A has two narrators known for weak fiqh but strong memory; Chain B has four narrators all strong in fiqh and memory. Which does the Hanafi school prefer? Apply the principle from the text: fiqh is decisive.
The answer is Chain B.
5
Note the scope of the anecdote
Read the author's comment that the anecdote only proves that fiqh-based tarjih is stronger, but does not negate that uluww may be considered when fiqh is equal. Understand the nuance.
The Hanafi position is that fiqh is primary, but uluww can be secondary.

و ترجيح السنن في السند يكون بفقه الراوي وقوة ضبطه وورعه وهو الاعتياد بإتيان المستحبات والاجتناب عن المكروهات بل عن المباحات لحظ النفس أيضاً، فإن الفقيه يضبطه كما ينبغي والمتورع يبعد عنه التساهل وقوي حنيفة : حدثنا حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة والأسود عن عبد الله بن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لا يرفع إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة ثم لا يعود بشيء من ذلك ، فقال الأوزاعي : أقول حدثنا الزهري عن كثير، فرجح بفقه الرواة، كما رجح الأوزاعي بعلو الإسناد، وهو المذهب المنصور عندنا. وكذا في فتح القدير»، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن هذه الحكاية لا تدل إلا على أن الترجيح بفقه الرواة أوثق منه بعلو الإسناد، وأما أن علو الإسناد لا يقع به الترجيح ولو عند المساواة في الفقاهة وعدمها فليس بلازم منه و الترجيح في السند يكون باعتياد الرواية لأن للمعتادية اهتماماً بضبطه خلافاً لشمس الأئمة وهذا لأن الاعتياد لا دخل له ولا عبرة بالخط بلا تذكر عند أبي حنيفة فلا عبرة بحديث رآه مكتوباً عنده وعرف أنه خطه أو خط ثقة، لكن لا يتذكر ما فيه وقد مر
And the preponderance of the Sunan in the chain is by the fiqh of the narrator, the strength of his memory, and his piety. Piety is the habit of performing recommended acts and avoiding disliked acts, even permissible acts for the sake of self-restraint. For the jurist retains it as he should, the pious distance themselves from leniency, and the strong in memory do not forget, as previously mentioned in the preponderance of Ibn Abbas over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. And preponderance is by high chain (uluww al-isnad), which is few intermediaries. It is said: nearness of chain is a nearness to the Messenger of Allah, due to the low probability of error, contrary to the Hanafis. Their argument is that the few intermediaries might be forgetful and poor in understanding the meaning of the hadith, while the many intermediaries might be strong in memory and intellect. So the probability from the narration of those few intermediaries is much weaker than that obtained from many intermediaries. Thus consideration is given to juristic expertise and strength of memory, not to fewness or numerousness. Ponder on it. Ibn Uyaynah narrated that Abu Hanifa met al-Awza'i. Al-Awza'i said: 'Why do you not raise your hands at bowing, while raising is sunna?' Abu Hanifa said: 'Because it is not confirmed from the Messenger of Allah.' Al-Awza'i said: 'How so? Al-Zuhri narrated to me from Salim from his father that the Messenger of Allah used to raise his hands when opening the prayer and did the same when he intended to bow.' Abu Hanifa said: 'Hammad narrated to us from Ibrahim from Alqamah and al-Aswad from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet does not raise except at the opening of the prayer, then does not return to any of that.' Al-Awza'i said: 'I say: Al-Zuhri narrated to me from Salim from his father Ibn Umar, and you say: Hammad narrated to me from Ibrahim.' Abu Hanifa said: 'Hammad was more learned in fiqh than al-Zuhri, Ibrahim was more learned than Salim, and Alqamah is not inferior to Ibn Umar in fiqh, even though Ibn Umar has companionship and has the virtue of companionship—al-Aswad has much virtue.' So he gave preponderance by the fiqh of the narrators, just as al-Awza'i gave preponderance by high chain. This is the supported madhhab according to us. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. And it should not escape you that this anecdote only indicates that preponderance by fiqh of narrators is stronger than by high chain. As for the idea that high chain does not effect preponderance even when there is equality in fiqh or its absence, that is not necessarily derived from it. And preponderance in the chain is by habit of narrating (i'tiyad al-riwaya), because habitual narrators have concern for retention, contrary to Shams al-A'imma. And this is because habit has no bearing on truthfulness or memory; many habitual narrators are lenient or even lie, and many non-habitual ones are concerned with the hadith. So understand. And preponderance is by knowledge of Arabic, i.e., the narrators' knowledge of Arabic, according to the correct view of the schools, contrary to some. That is because the one who knows Arabic can easily retain and not err in inflection, unlike the ignorant. And by it being from his memory, not from his copy (nuskha), i.e., over one who narrates from his copy, because the memorizer's concern for the hadith is more intense than that of the one relying on the copy. Ponder it. And there is no consideration to handwriting without recollection according to Abu Hanifa, so there is no consideration to a hadith he sees written with him and knows it is his handwriting or that of a trustworthy person, but does not recall its content, and this has passed.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage discusses factors that give preponderance to one chain of transmission (sanad) over another when conflicting hadiths are otherwise equal. The first factor is the narrator's fiqh (juridic understanding), strong memory (ضبط), and piety (ورع). Piety is defined as consistently performing recommended acts and avoiding disliked ones, even some permissible acts for self-discipline. The narrators' fiqh and memory are key because a jurist retains meanings accurately, and the pious avoid carelessness. The author cites the example of Ibn Abbas being preferred over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. The second factor is 'uluww al-isnad (high chain with few intermediates). Some argue this is a virtue because it reduces error probability. However, the Hanafis disagree: they point out that few intermediates might be forgetful and poor in understanding, while a longer chain with more reliable narrators is stronger. So the criterion is fiqh and memory, not the number of links. The famous anecdote of Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i illustrates this: al-Awza'i preferred his chain (al-Zuhri → Salim → Ibn Umar) because it is shorter, while Abu Hanifa preferred his own chain (Hammad → Ibrahim → Alqamah and al-Aswad → Ibn Mas'ud) because the narrators were more knowledgeable in fiqh. This 'madhhab' is the supported one for Hanafis. The author then adds that habit of narrating (i'tiyad al-riwaya) is not a valid factor, contrary to Shams al-A'imma, because habit does not guarantee truthfulness or accuracy. Next, the narrator's knowledge of Arabic is a factor because it helps in correct retention and recitation. Finally, narration from memory is stronger than from a written copy, because the memorizer's attention is more intense. Abu Hanifa disregards a written hadith if the narrator does not remember it, even if he recognizes his own handwriting.

Key Terms
فقه الراوي (fiqh al-rawi): The narrator's understanding of the legal implications of the hadith
علو الإسناد (uluww al-isnad): A chain with few intermediaries between the narrator and the Prophet
ضبط (dabt): The narrator's accuracy and memory strength
ورع (wara'): Piety and scrupulousness, avoiding both prohibitions and doubtful matters

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa prefer his chain of narrators (Hammad → Ibrahim → Alqamah and al-Aswad → Ibn Mas'ud) over al-Awza'i's chain (al-Zuhri → Salim → Ibn Umar)?
A) Because his chain had more narrators and thus more witnesses
B) Because his narrators were more knowledgeable in fiqh than al-Awza'i's narrators
C) Because his chain was shorter
D) Because Ibn Mas'ud was a senior companion

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the fiqh of the narrator is the primary factor for preponderance in the chain, not shortness of the chain.

Secondary Factors in Sanad Tarjih: Habit, Arabic, and Memory
Explaining secondary factors for sanad preponderance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the role of habitual narration, knowledge of Arabic, and memory vs written copy in preponderance, and identify the exception regarding handwriting without recollection.

Core Idea
Habit does not guarantee reliability, but Arabic proficiency and memory strengthen a narrator's weight.

Beyond the core qualities of fiqh, memory, and piety, the text discusses additional factors that can tip the scales: the narrator's habitual practice, linguistic skill, and whether he narrates from memory or his notes. This lesson unpacks these nuanced points, including a dispute with Shams al-A'imma.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the factor of i'tiyad al-riwaya
Read the section on 'i'tiyad al-riwaya' (habit of narrating). Note that some scholars consider it a valid factor, but the text rejects it. Identify the reasons: habit does not guarantee truthfulness or memory; many habitual narrators are lenient or even lie.
This is a disagreement with Shams al-A'imma.
2
Understand the role of Arabic knowledge
Read the sentence about 'ilm al-Arabiyya. Note that the correct view is that knowledge of Arabic is a valid factor because it helps in correct retention and recitation, preventing errors in inflection (i'rab).
This is the correct view according to the text, contrary to some.
3
Distinguish memory narration from copy narration
Read the passage on narration from memory (hifz) vs from a written copy (nuskha). The memorizer's concern is more intense, so memory-based narration is stronger. Also note Abu Hanifa's rule that a hadith seen in writing but not recalled is not considered, even if the handwriting is recognized.
This shows the priority of memory over written records.
4
Apply the factors to a scenario
Consider two chains equal in fiqh and dabt. Chain A: narrator habitually narrates, knows Arabic well, but relies on his copy. Chain B: narrator not habitual, poor Arabic, but narrates from memory. Which is preponderant? Weigh each factor: habit is irrelevant, Arabic favors Chain A, memory favors Chain B. Since the text does not rank Arabic vs memory, you must note the tension.
The text does not provide a clear ranking between these; but memory is emphasized more.
5
Note the special case of handwriting without recollection
Read the final sentence: 'ولا عبرة بالخط بلا تذكر عند أبي حنيفة'. Understand that even if a narrator recognizes his own handwriting or that of a trustworthy person, if he does not recall the content, it is not acceptable. This emphasizes the importance of active memory.
This is a ruling from Abu Hanifa himself.

And the preponderance of the Sunan in the chain is by the fiqh of the narrator, the strength of his memory, and his piety. Piety is the habit of performing recommended acts and avoiding disliked acts, even permissible acts for the sake of self-restraint. For the jurist retains it as he should, the pious distance themselves from leniency, and the strong in memory do not forget, as previously mentioned in the preponderance of Ibn Abbas over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. And preponderance is by high chain (uluww al-isnad), which is few intermediaries. It is said: nearness of chain is a nearness to the Messenger of Allah, due to the low probability of error, contrary to the Hanafis. Their argument is that the few intermediaries might be forgetful and poor in understanding the meaning of the hadith, while the many intermediaries might be strong in memory and intellect. So the probability from the narration of those few intermediaries is much weaker than that obtained from many intermediaries. Thus consideration is given to juristic expertise and strength of memory, not to fewness or numerousness. Ponder on it. Ibn Uyaynah narrated that Abu Hanifa met al-Awza'i. Al-Awza'i said: 'Why do you not raise your hands at bowing, while raising is sunna?' Abu Hanifa said: 'Because it is not confirmed from the Messenger of Allah.' Al-Awza'i said: 'How so? Al-Zuhri narrated to me from Salim from his father that the Messenger of Allah used to raise his hands when opening the prayer and did the same when he intended to bow.' Abu Hanifa said: 'Hammad narrated to us from Ibrahim from Alqamah and al-Aswad from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet does not raise except at the opening of the prayer, then does not return to any of that.' Al-Awza'i said: 'I say: Al-Zuhri narrated to me from Salim from his father Ibn Umar, and you say: Hammad narrated to me from Ibrahim.' Abu Hanifa said: 'Hammad was more learned in fiqh than al-Zuhri, Ibrahim was more learned than Salim, and Alqamah is not inferior to Ibn Umar in fiqh, even though Ibn Umar has companionship and has the virtue of companionship—al-Aswad has much virtue.' So he gave preponderance by the fiqh of the narrators, just as al-Awza'i gave preponderance by high chain. This is the supported madhhab according to us. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. And it should not escape you that this anecdote only indicates that preponderance by fiqh of narrators is stronger than by high chain. As for the idea that high chain does not effect preponderance even when there is equality in fiqh or its absence, that is not necessarily derived from it. And preponderance in the chain is by habit of narrating (i'tiyad al-riwaya), because habitual narrators have concern for retention, contrary to Shams al-A'imma. And this is because habit has no bearing on truthfulness or memory; many habitual narrators are lenient or even lie, and many non-habitual ones are concerned with the hadith. So understand. And preponderance is by knowledge of Arabic, i.e., the narrators' knowledge of Arabic, according to the correct view of the schools, contrary to some. That is because the one who knows Arabic can easily retain and not err in inflection, unlike the ignorant. And by it being from his memory, not from his copy (nuskha), i.e., over one who narrates from his copy, because the memorizer's concern for the hadith is more intense than that of the one relying on the copy. Ponder it. And there is no consideration to handwriting without recollection according to Abu Hanifa, so there is no consideration to a hadith he sees written with him and knows it is his handwriting or that of a trustworthy person, but does not recall its content, and this has passed.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage discusses factors that give preponderance to one chain of transmission (sanad) over another when conflicting hadiths are otherwise equal. The first factor is the narrator's fiqh (juridic understanding), strong memory (ضبط), and piety (ورع). Piety is defined as consistently performing recommended acts and avoiding disliked ones, even some permissible acts for self-discipline. The narrators' fiqh and memory are key because a jurist retains meanings accurately, and the pious avoid carelessness. The author cites the example of Ibn Abbas being preferred over Yazid ibn al-Asamm. The second factor is 'uluww al-isnad (high chain with few intermediates). Some argue this is a virtue because it reduces error probability. However, the Hanafis disagree: they point out that few intermediates might be forgetful and poor in understanding, while a longer chain with more reliable narrators is stronger. So the criterion is fiqh and memory, not the number of links. The famous anecdote of Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i illustrates this: al-Awza'i preferred his chain (al-Zuhri → Salim → Ibn Umar) because it is shorter, while Abu Hanifa preferred his own chain (Hammad → Ibrahim → Alqamah and al-Aswad → Ibn Mas'ud) because the narrators were more knowledgeable in fiqh. This 'madhhab' is the supported one for Hanafis. The author then adds that habit of narrating (i'tiyad al-riwaya) is not a valid factor, contrary to Shams al-A'imma, because habit does not guarantee truthfulness or accuracy. Next, the narrator's knowledge of Arabic is a factor because it helps in correct retention and recitation. Finally, narration from memory is stronger than from a written copy, because the memorizer's attention is more intense. Abu Hanifa disregards a written hadith if the narrator does not remember it, even if he recognizes his own handwriting.

Key Terms
اعتياد الرواية (i'tiyad al-riwaya): The habit of frequently narrating hadith
علم العربية (ilm al-arabiyya): Knowledge of Arabic language, especially grammar and inflection
حفظ (hifz): Memorization; narrating from memory
نسخة (nuskha): A written copy of hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in the text, why is habitual narration (i'tiyad al-riwaya) not a valid factor for tarjih?
A) Because habitual narrators are always liars
B) Because habit does not guarantee truthfulness or memory; many habitual narrators are lenient or lie
C) Because habit only matters if the narrator is also pious
D) Because the text does not discuss habit

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, habit of narrating is not a valid factor, while knowledge of Arabic and narration from memory are considered positive factors.

8 min
Tarjih by Fiqh of the Narrator: The Raf' al-Yadayn Debate
Debate on raf' al-yadayn illustrating tarjih by fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prioritizes the narrator's fiqh over chain height when resolving contradictory hadith.

Core Idea
A narrator's deep understanding of fiqh is a stronger indicator of accuracy than a high chain.

In the famous debate on raising hands in prayer, Imam Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i presented conflicting hadith. Abu Hanifa argued that his narrators (Hamad, Ibrahim, Alqama, al-Aswad) were more knowledgeable in fiqh than al-Awza'i's (al-Zuhri, Salim, Ibn Umar), and therefore their narration should be preferred. This establishes a key Hanafi principle: tarjih by the fiqh of the narrator outweighs mere chain height.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting hadith
Note that Abu Hanifa cites the hadith of Ibn Masud: the Prophet only raised hands at the opening takbir. Al-Awza'i cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet raised hands at various points.
2
Analyze the chains
Compare the chains: Abu Hanifa's chain goes through Hamad, Ibrahim, Alqama, al-Aswad to Ibn Masud. Al-Awza'i's chain goes through al-Zuhri, Salim to Ibn Umar.
Ibn Umar is a Companion; Ibn Masud also a Companion.
3
Understand the tarjih criterion
Abu Hanifa does not claim his chain is higher; he claims his narrators are more knowledgeable in fiqh. This is the Hanafi criterion.
He specifically says Hamad was more knowledgeable than al-Zuhri, Ibrahim than Salim, and Alqama not less than Ibn Umar in fiqh.
4
Recognize the school's position
The author states this is the supported madhhab: tarjih by fiqh of narrators is preferred over tarjih by height of chain.
This principle is applied in many Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني/ السنة. قال أبو حنيفة: حدثنا حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة والأسود عن عبد الله بن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لا يرفع إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة ثم لا يعود بشيء من ذلك. فقال الأوزاعي: أقول حدثنا الزهري عن سالم عن أبيه ابن عمر، وتقول حدثني حماد عن إبراهيم: فقال أبو حنيفة: كان حماد أفقه من الزهري، وكان إبراهيم أفقه من سالم، وعلقمة ليس دون ابن عمر في الفقه وإن كان لابن عمر صحبة وله فضل صحبة للأسود فضل كثير، فرجح بفقه الرواة، كما رجح الأوزاعي بعلو الإسناد، وهو المذهب المنصور عندنا. (و) الترجيح في السند يكون (باعتياد الرواية) لأن للمعتادية اهتماماً بضبطه (خلافاً لشمس الأئمة) وهذا لأن الاعتياد لا دخل له في الصدق ولا في الضبط. (و) يترجح بعلمه بالعربية) أي بمعرفة الرواة العربية (في الصحيح) من المذاهب خلافاً للبعض، لأن العارف بالعربية يسهل عليه الضبط ولا يخطىء في الإعراب بخلاف الجاهل بها. (و) بكونها عن حفظه لا نسخته) أي على ما يكون رواية عن نسخته لأن اهتمام الحافظ بالحديث أكثر وأشد عن اهتمام المعتمد على النسخة. (و) يكون بكونه من أكابر الصحابة خلافاً للشيخين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى كما في الهدم لما دون الثلاث بعد وطء الزوج الثاني، كما يهدم الثلاث وحتى يملك الزوج الأول بالتزوج ثانياً بعد إبانة الثاني أو موته، كمال التطليقات الثلاث، كما كان يملك من قبل (فإنه ) مروي عن ابن عباس وابن عمر) وقد اختاراه (وعدم الهدم مروي (عن) أمير المؤمنين (عمر و أمير المؤمنين (علي) ولم يختاراه. (و) الترجيح في السند قد يكون (بالمباشرة) أي بمباشرة الراوي (و) قد يكون بالقرب عند السماع لأنه أسمع (وذلك إذا بعد الآخر بعداً بعيداً) بحيث يحتمل الغلط في السماع بأن يسمع البعض دون البعض الآخر وبه رجح الشافعية الإفراد بالحج من رواية ابن عمر أنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أهل بالحج لأنه كان تحت ناقته فيكون أقرب أسمع للإهلال (و) رجح (الحنفية القرآن فعن أنس أنه كان آخذاً بزمامها حين يقول: لبيك بحجة وعمرة. اعلم أنه اضطربت الروايات في حجة الوداع، ففي البعض أنه أفرد بالحج، وفي أخرى أنه قرن بالحجة العمرة بإحرام وفي أخرى أنه تمتع. قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي: وأكثر الروايات شاهدة بالقران وبعضهم جمع بأنه أهل أولاً بالعمرة، ثم ضم إليه الإهلال بالحج، قال حين التلبية بعد ذلك: لبيك بحجة وعمرة. فمن سمع القول الأول حكى التمتع، ومن سمع القول الثاني ولم يكن شاعراً بأنه أهل من قبل بالعمرة حكى الإفراد، ومن القول الأخير وهم الأكثر حكوا القرآن. ولهذا الاختلاف اختلفوا في أن الأفضل ما هو، فعندنا القرآن، وعند الشافعي الإفراد وعند مالك: التمتع، وقال أحمد: القرآن إن ساق الهدي وإلا فالإفراد. (و) قد يكون (بالتحمل بالغاً ومسلماً) فيكون ما تحمله بالغاً مسلماً أرجح مما تحمله صبياً أو كافراً لأن اهتمام المسلم البالغ بالسماع أشد من اهتمام غيره. (و) قد يكون بتأخر الإسلام وذلك إذا كان متقدم الإسلام لم يسمع بعد إسلامه بأن مات قبله. وصرح متأخر الإسلام بأنه سمع بنفسه، وهذا ظاهر جداً (كالوارد في المدينة المطهرة، فإنه مرجح على الوارد بمكة، فإن أكثره وارد بعد الهجرة والغلبة فيما ورد بمكة لما ورد قبل الهجرة، والذي ينزل بعد الهجرة يسمى مدنياً، والذي قبل الهجرة يسمى مكياً، لكن هذا الترجيح إنما يكون فيما إذا لم يعلم ورود ما في مكة بعد الهجرة. (و) قد يكون بتصريح السماع والوصل على العنعنة لاحتمال الإرسال والانقطاع فيها وفيه نظر، لأن قابل المرسل لا يسلم ذلك بعد عدالة المعنعن وإمامته وكونه غير مدلس تدليس التسوية، قال الحاكم: الأحاديث المعنعنة التي ليس فيها تدليس متصلة بالإجماع. (و) قد يكون (بالذكورة) فيترجح مروي الذكر على مروي الأنثى لكن في غير أحكام النساء) أي أحكام يكون الغالب فيها معرفة النساء، وبه رجح خبر الركوع الواحد في الصلاة الكسوف على خبر تعدده لأن راوي التعدد أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة وراوي الركوع الواحد سمرة بن جندب، كما روى الترمذي وقال: حسن صحيح، لأن هذه الحال أكشف للرجال، لكن حديث تعدد الركوع رواه ابن عباس أيضاً على ما في الصحيحين، فلا يتم هذا النحو من الترجيح.
Second principle: the Sunnah. Abu Hanifa said: Hamad narrated to us from Ibrahim from Alqama and al-Aswad from Abdullah ibn Masud that the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family and companions, did not raise his hands except at the opening of the prayer and then did not return to any of that. al-Awza'i said: I say al-Zuhri narrated to us from Salim from his father Ibn Umar, and you say Hamad narrated to me from Ibrahim. Abu Hanifa said: Hamad was more knowledgeable in fiqh than al-Zuhri, and Ibrahim was more knowledgeable in fiqh than Salim, and Alqama is not inferior to Ibn Umar in fiqh, though Ibn Umar has companionship and virtue, and al-Aswad has much virtue. So he gave preference by the fiqh of the narrators, just as al-Awza'i gave preference by the high chain, and this is the supported madhhab with us. (And) preference in the chain occurs (by habit of narration) because those accustomed have care in preserving it (contrary to Shams al-A'imma). (And) preference is given by knowledge of Arabic (in the correct view) contrary to some. (And) by being from memory not from his copy. (And) by being from the senior Companions, contrary to the two shaykhs Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. (And) preference in the chain may occur (by direct hearing). (And) by proximity at hearing because it is more audible. (And) by being transmitted as an adult and Muslim. (And) by later Islam. (And) by explicit mention of hearing and connection over 'an'anah. (And) by masculinity.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Muslim al-Thubut discusses the various criteria for prefering one hadith narration over another when there is apparent conflict, focusing on the chain of transmission (sanad). The author begins by narrating a famous debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Awza'i regarding the raising of hands in prayer. Abu Hanifa preferred the narration of Hamad, Ibrahim, Alqama, and Ibn Masud over that of al-Zuhri, Salim, and Ibn Umar because the narrators in his chain were more knowledgeable in fiqh, even though al-Awza'i's chain was higher. This shows that tarjih by the fiqh of narrators is stronger than tarjih by high chain according to the Hanafi madhhab. Then the author lists other criteria for tarjih in the sanad: (1) habit of narration – but this is disputed because habit does not guarantee truthfulness; (2) knowledge of Arabic – because it aids in accurate preservation; (3) narration from memory rather than from a written copy – because a memorizer is more attentive; (4) being among the senior Companions – but this is rejected by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for the purpose of tarjih; (5) direct hearing and proximity to the speaker – illustrated by the dispute over whether the Prophet performed hajj ifrad, qiran, or tamattu', with the Shafi'is preferring Ibn Umar's narration (he was close to the Prophet's camel) and the Hanafis preferring Anas's narration (he held the camel's reins); (6) being an adult Muslim at the time of hearing; (7) later acceptance of Islam (so that the narrator heard after becoming Muslim); (8) explicit mention of hearing (sama') versus 'an'anah – though 'an'anah from a non-mudallis is considered connected by consensus; (9) masculinity of the narrator – but this applies only in matters not specific to women, exemplified by the debate on the number of bowings in the eclipse prayer. The author notes that this last criterion is not fully sound because Ibn Abbas also narrated multiple rak'ahs.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preferring one narration over another when they appear contradictory, based on certain strengths in the chain or text.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer; the specific dispute is about whether to raise them at times other than the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Hanifa cite to prefer his hadith over al-Awza'i's?
A) His chain was shorter
B) His narrators were more senior Companions
C) His narrators were more knowledgeable in fiqh
D) His hadith was more widely narrated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the fiqh comprehension of narrators is a stronger tarjih factor than mere chain height.

Internal Qualities of the Narrator for Tarjih
Listing four internal narrator qualities for tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria of habit of narration, knowledge of Arabic, memory vs copy, and seniority of Companions to prefer one hadith over another.

Core Idea
Stronger narration comes from a narrator who is well-practiced, linguistically skilled, reliant on memory, and, notably, seniority does not automatically give preference.

After establishing the primacy of fiqh, the author lists other internal qualities of narrators that can tip the balance in tarjih. Some of these are contested within the Hanafi school, offering a nuanced view of how to weigh different strengths.

Guided Path
1
Examine each criterion
Review the four internal qualities: (1) habit of narration (i'tiyad al-riwaya), (2) knowledge of Arabic, (3) narration from memory vs. copy, (4) being a senior Companion.
Each has a specific application and sometimes a counterview.
2
Identify the Hanafi position on each
For each criterion, note whether the Hanafi school accepts it or rejects it. For example, habit of narration is rejected by Shams al-A'imma; senior Companionship is rejected by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The author often mentions the opposition (khilaf) and then the correct view.
3
Apply to an example
Consider a hypothetical scenario where two narrators are otherwise equal but one is a senior Companion. According to the Hanafi view, this does not automatically give preference.
The example about 'al-hadm' illustrates that senior Companions can disagree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني/ السنة. قال أبو حنيفة: حدثنا حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة والأسود عن عبد الله بن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لا يرفع إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة ثم لا يعود بشيء من ذلك. فقال الأوزاعي: أقول حدثنا الزهري عن سالم عن أبيه ابن عمر، وتقول حدثني حماد عن إبراهيم: فقال أبو حنيفة: كان حماد أفقه من الزهري، وكان إبراهيم أفقه من سالم، وعلقمة ليس دون ابن عمر في الفقه وإن كان لابن عمر صحبة وله فضل صحبة للأسود فضل كثير، فرجح بفقه الرواة، كما رجح الأوزاعي بعلو الإسناد، وهو المذهب المنصور عندنا. (و) الترجيح في السند يكون (باعتياد الرواية) لأن للمعتادية اهتماماً بضبطه (خلافاً لشمس الأئمة) وهذا لأن الاعتياد لا دخل له في الصدق ولا في الضبط. (و) يترجح بعلمه بالعربية) أي بمعرفة الرواة العربية (في الصحيح) من المذاهب خلافاً للبعض، لأن العارف بالعربية يسهل عليه الضبط ولا يخطىء في الإعراب بخلاف الجاهل بها. (و) بكونها عن حفظه لا نسخته) أي على ما يكون رواية عن نسخته لأن اهتمام الحافظ بالحديث أكثر وأشد عن اهتمام المعتمد على النسخة. (و) يكون بكونه من أكابر الصحابة خلافاً للشيخين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى كما في الهدم لما دون الثلاث بعد وطء الزوج الثاني، كما يهدم الثلاث وحتى يملك الزوج الأول بالتزوج ثانياً بعد إبانة الثاني أو موته، كمال التطليقات الثلاث، كما كان يملك من قبل (فإنه ) مروي عن ابن عباس وابن عمر) وقد اختاراه (وعدم الهدم مروي (عن) أمير المؤمنين (عمر و أمير المؤمنين (علي) ولم يختاراه. (و) الترجيح في السند قد يكون (بالمباشرة) أي بمباشرة الراوي (و) قد يكون بالقرب عند السماع لأنه أسمع (وذلك إذا بعد الآخر بعداً بعيداً) بحيث يحتمل الغلط في السماع بأن يسمع البعض دون البعض الآخر وبه رجح الشافعية الإفراد بالحج من رواية ابن عمر أنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أهل بالحج لأنه كان تحت ناقته فيكون أقرب أسمع للإهلال (و) رجح (الحنفية القرآن فعن أنس أنه كان آخذاً بزمامها حين يقول: لبيك بحجة وعمرة. اعلم أنه اضطربت الروايات في حجة الوداع، ففي البعض أنه أفرد بالحج، وفي أخرى أنه قرن بالحجة العمرة بإحرام وفي أخرى أنه تمتع. قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي: وأكثر الروايات شاهدة بالقران وبعضهم جمع بأنه أهل أولاً بالعمرة، ثم ضم إليه الإهلال بالحج، قال حين التلبية بعد ذلك: لبيك بحجة وعمرة. فمن سمع القول الأول حكى التمتع، ومن سمع القول الثاني ولم يكن شاعراً بأنه أهل من قبل بالعمرة حكى الإفراد، ومن القول الأخير وهم الأكثر حكوا القرآن. ولهذا الاختلاف اختلفوا في أن الأفضل ما هو، فعندنا القرآن، وعند الشافعي الإفراد وعند مالك: التمتع، وقال أحمد: القرآن إن ساق الهدي وإلا فالإفراد. (و) قد يكون (بالتحمل بالغاً ومسلماً) فيكون ما تحمله بالغاً مسلماً أرجح مما تحمله صبياً أو كافراً لأن اهتمام المسلم البالغ بالسماع أشد من اهتمام غيره. (و) قد يكون بتأخر الإسلام وذلك إذا كان متقدم الإسلام لم يسمع بعد إسلامه بأن مات قبله. وصرح متأخر الإسلام بأنه سمع بنفسه، وهذا ظاهر جداً (كالوارد في المدينة المطهرة، فإنه مرجح على الوارد بمكة، فإن أكثره وارد بعد الهجرة والغلبة فيما ورد بمكة لما ورد قبل الهجرة، والذي ينزل بعد الهجرة يسمى مدنياً، والذي قبل الهجرة يسمى مكياً، لكن هذا الترجيح إنما يكون فيما إذا لم يعلم ورود ما في مكة بعد الهجرة. (و) قد يكون بتصريح السماع والوصل على العنعنة لاحتمال الإرسال والانقطاع فيها وفيه نظر، لأن قابل المرسل لا يسلم ذلك بعد عدالة المعنعن وإمامته وكونه غير مدلس تدليس التسوية، قال الحاكم: الأحاديث المعنعنة التي ليس فيها تدليس متصلة بالإجماع. (و) قد يكون (بالذكورة) فيترجح مروي الذكر على مروي الأنثى لكن في غير أحكام النساء) أي أحكام يكون الغالب فيها معرفة النساء، وبه رجح خبر الركوع الواحد في الصلاة الكسوف على خبر تعدده لأن راوي التعدد أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة وراوي الركوع الواحد سمرة بن جندب، كما روى الترمذي وقال: حسن صحيح، لأن هذه الحال أكشف للرجال، لكن حديث تعدد الركوع رواه ابن عباس أيضاً على ما في الصحيحين، فلا يتم هذا النحو من الترجيح.
Second principle: the Sunnah. Abu Hanifa said: Hamad narrated to us from Ibrahim from Alqama and al-Aswad from Abdullah ibn Masud that the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family and companions, did not raise his hands except at the opening of the prayer and then did not return to any of that. al-Awza'i said: I say al-Zuhri narrated to us from Salim from his father Ibn Umar, and you say Hamad narrated to me from Ibrahim. Abu Hanifa said: Hamad was more knowledgeable in fiqh than al-Zuhri, and Ibrahim was more knowledgeable in fiqh than Salim, and Alqama is not inferior to Ibn Umar in fiqh, though Ibn Umar has companionship and virtue, and al-Aswad has much virtue. So he gave preference by the fiqh of the narrators, just as al-Awza'i gave preference by the high chain, and this is the supported madhhab with us. (And) preference in the chain occurs (by habit of narration) because those accustomed have care in preserving it (contrary to Shams al-A'imma). (And) preference is given by knowledge of Arabic (in the correct view) contrary to some. (And) by being from memory not from his copy. (And) by being from the senior Companions, contrary to the two shaykhs Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. (And) preference in the chain may occur (by direct hearing). (And) by proximity at hearing because it is more audible. (And) by being transmitted as an adult and Muslim. (And) by later Islam. (And) by explicit mention of hearing and connection over 'an'anah. (And) by masculinity.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Muslim al-Thubut discusses the various criteria for prefering one hadith narration over another when there is apparent conflict, focusing on the chain of transmission (sanad). The author begins by narrating a famous debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Awza'i regarding the raising of hands in prayer. Abu Hanifa preferred the narration of Hamad, Ibrahim, Alqama, and Ibn Masud over that of al-Zuhri, Salim, and Ibn Umar because the narrators in his chain were more knowledgeable in fiqh, even though al-Awza'i's chain was higher. This shows that tarjih by the fiqh of narrators is stronger than tarjih by high chain according to the Hanafi madhhab. Then the author lists other criteria for tarjih in the sanad: (1) habit of narration – but this is disputed because habit does not guarantee truthfulness; (2) knowledge of Arabic – because it aids in accurate preservation; (3) narration from memory rather than from a written copy – because a memorizer is more attentive; (4) being among the senior Companions – but this is rejected by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for the purpose of tarjih; (5) direct hearing and proximity to the speaker – illustrated by the dispute over whether the Prophet performed hajj ifrad, qiran, or tamattu', with the Shafi'is preferring Ibn Umar's narration (he was close to the Prophet's camel) and the Hanafis preferring Anas's narration (he held the camel's reins); (6) being an adult Muslim at the time of hearing; (7) later acceptance of Islam (so that the narrator heard after becoming Muslim); (8) explicit mention of hearing (sama') versus 'an'anah – though 'an'anah from a non-mudallis is considered connected by consensus; (9) masculinity of the narrator – but this applies only in matters not specific to women, exemplified by the debate on the number of bowings in the eclipse prayer. The author notes that this last criterion is not fully sound because Ibn Abbas also narrated multiple rak'ahs.

Key Terms
اعتياد الرواية (i'tiyad al-riwaya): Being accustomed to narrating hadith regularly; some considered this a preference factor.
أكابر الصحابة (akabir al-sahaba): Senior Companions, i.e., those with early Islam and high status; their narrations were considered stronger by some.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which internal quality for tarjih is rejected by Shams al-A'imma?
A) Knowledge of Arabic
B) Narration from memory
C) Habit of narration
D) Senior Companionship

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, internal narrator qualities like Arabic knowledge and memory matter, but habit and senior Companionship do not.

External and Contextual Factors for Tarjih
Listing external factors for tarjih with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criteria of direct hearing, proximity, adulthood/Islam, later Islam, explicit sama', and masculinity to prefer one hadith over another.

Core Idea
A narrator's physical closeness to the Prophet and explicit methods of transmission strengthen their narration, but masculinity is a limited criterion.

Beyond internal qualities, certain contextual factors—like how the narrator heard the hadith, their age at hearing, and even gender—can influence tarjih. This lesson unpacks these external factors with real examples from hajj and eclipse prayer disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify each external factor
List the external factors: direct hearing (mubashara), proximity when hearing, adulthood/Islam at time of hearing, later Islam, explicit mention of hearing (sama') vs. 'an'anah, and masculinity.
Each factor has an application and often a counter-example.
2
Analyze the hajj dispute
The Shafi'is used proximity to prefer Ibn Umar's narration (ifrad), while Hanafis used direct involvement to prefer Anas's narration (qiran). Understand the difference.
This illustrates the interplay of factors.
3
Evaluate the masculinity criterion
Masculinity is a factor only in matters not specific to women. The example of eclipse prayer shows its limitations.
This criterion is not universally applied.

الأصل الثاني/ السنة. قال أبو حنيفة: حدثنا حماد عن إبراهيم عن علقمة والأسود عن عبد الله بن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لا يرفع إلا عند افتتاح الصلاة ثم لا يعود بشيء من ذلك. فقال الأوزاعي: أقول حدثنا الزهري عن سالم عن أبيه ابن عمر، وتقول حدثني حماد عن إبراهيم: فقال أبو حنيفة: كان حماد أفقه من الزهري، وكان إبراهيم أفقه من سالم، وعلقمة ليس دون ابن عمر في الفقه وإن كان لابن عمر صحبة وله فضل صحبة للأسود فضل كثير، فرجح بفقه الرواة، كما رجح الأوزاعي بعلو الإسناد، وهو المذهب المنصور عندنا. (و) الترجيح في السند يكون (باعتياد الرواية) لأن للمعتادية اهتماماً بضبطه (خلافاً لشمس الأئمة) وهذا لأن الاعتياد لا دخل له في الصدق ولا في الضبط. Second principle: the Sunnah. (And) by masculinity.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Muslim al-Thubut discusses the various criteria for prefering one hadith narration over another when there is apparent conflict, focusing on the chain of transmission (sanad). The author begins by narrating a famous debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Awza'i regarding the raising of hands in prayer. Abu Hanifa preferred the narration of Hamad, Ibrahim, Alqama, and Ibn Masud over that of al-Zuhri, Salim, and Ibn Umar because the narrators in his chain were more knowledgeable in fiqh, even though al-Awza'i's chain was higher. This shows that tarjih by the fiqh of narrators is stronger than tarjih by high chain according to the Hanafi madhhab. Then the author lists other criteria for tarjih in the sanad: (1) habit of narration – but this is disputed because habit does not guarantee truthfulness; (2) knowledge of Arabic – because it aids in accurate preservation; (3) narration from memory rather than from a written copy – because a memorizer is more attentive; (4) being among the senior Companions – but this is rejected by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for the purpose of tarjih; (5) direct hearing and proximity to the speaker – illustrated by the dispute over whether the Prophet performed hajj ifrad, qiran, or tamattu', with the Shafi'is preferring Ibn Umar's narration (he was close to the Prophet's camel) and the Hanafis preferring Anas's narration (he held the camel's reins); (6) being an adult Muslim at the time of hearing; (7) later acceptance of Islam (so that the narrator heard after becoming Muslim); (8) explicit mention of hearing (sama') versus 'an'anah – though 'an'anah from a non-mudallis is considered connected by consensus; (9) masculinity of the narrator – but this applies only in matters not specific to women, exemplified by the debate on the number of bowings in the eclipse prayer. The author notes that this last criterion is not fully sound because Ibn Abbas also narrated multiple rak'ahs.

Key Terms
المباشرة (al-mubashara): Direct hearing from the Prophet or being physically close to him during the utterance.
العنعنة (al-'an'anah): A chain using 'an (from) without explicit mention of hearing; considered connected by consensus if the narrator is not a mudallis.
الذكورة (al-dhukura): Masculinity of the narrator; used as a preference factor in matters not specific to women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the main reason Hanafis preferred Anas's narration over Ibn Umar's regarding the Prophet's hajj?
A) Anas was a male
B) Anas's chain was shorter
C) Anas had direct physical contact with the camel and heard the Prophet clearly
D) Anas was a senior Companion

Key Takeaway
External factors like direct hearing, adulthood, and explicit sama' strengthen a narration, but each must be applied with its limitations.

Tarjih by Proximity and the Hajj Dispute
Explaining tarjih by proximity and analyzing conflicting Hajj narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih by narrator proximity to resolve conflicting Hadith and state the Hanafi position on the best form of Hajj.

Core Idea
Proximity strengthens a narration but reconciliation can still yield the preferred ruling.

Two narrators report different versions of the same event—who is more reliable? The Hanafi school teaches that physical proximity to the speaker at the time of hearing strengthens a narration, yet conflicting reports can often be harmonized. This lesson unpacks a famous dispute about the Prophet's ﷺ Farewell Hajj, showing how tarjih by proximity was applied and ultimately reconciled to derive the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the tarjih principle
Identify the principle of tarjih by proximity: the narrator who was physically closer to the speaker at the time of hearing is given preponderance because error in hearing is less likely.
This principle applies when other factors are equal.
2
Identify the conflicting narrations
List the three types of narrations about the Farewell Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj only), Qiran (combined Hajj and 'Umrah with one Ihram), and Tamattu' ('Umrah then Hajj with separate Ihrams).
The conflict is about what the Prophet ﷺ actually did.
3
Analyze each school's tarjih argument
Shafi'is used Ibn 'Umar's narration (he was under the camel, thus close) to support Ifrad. Hanafis used Anas's narration (he held the halter, also close) and argued that most narrations support Qiran.
Both schools claim proximity, but Hanafis also rely on plurality of narrations.
4
Apply the reconciliation method
Follow the reconciliation proposed by Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi: the Prophet first entered Ihram for 'Umrah, then added Hajj. Different narrators heard different stages, creating apparent conflict.
Reconciliation removes the contradiction without rejecting any narration.
5
Determine the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi position (Qiran) is based on the majority of narrations and the reconciliation. It becomes the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for Hanafis.
Know the thamarah al-khilaf: which intention a pilgrim should make.

Source Text

بالقرب عند السماع لأنه أسمع (وذلك إذا بعد الآخر بعداً بعيداً) بحيث يحتمل الغلط في السماع بأن يسمع البعض دون البعض الآخر وبه رجح الشافعية الإفراد بالحج من رواية ابن عمر أنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أهل بالحج لأنه كان تحت ناقته فيكون أقرب أسمع للإهلال (و) رجح (الحنفية القرآن فعن أنس أنه كان آخذاً بزمامها حين يقول : لبيك بحجة وعمرة اعلم أنه اضطربت الروايات في حجة الوداع، ففي البعض أنه أفرد بالحج، وفي أخرى أنه قرن بالحجة العمرة بإحرام وفي أخرى أنه تمتع قال الشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي : وأكثر الروايات شاهد بالقران وبعضهم جمع بأنه أهل أولاً بالعمرة، ثم ضم إليه الإهلال بالحج، قال حين التلبية بعد ذلك : لبيك بحجة وعمرة. فمن سمع القول الأول حكى التمتع، ومن سمع القول الثاني ولم يكن شاعراً بأنه أهل من قبل بالعمرة حكى الإفراد، ومن القول الأخير وهم الأكثر حكوا القرآن، ولعل روايات القرآن مشهورة، بل تبلغ حد التواتر المعنوي والله أعلم؛ ولهذا الاختلاف اختلفوا في أن الأفضل ما هو، فعندنا القرآن، وعند الشافعي الإفراد وعند مالك : التمتع ، وقال أحمد : القرآن إن ساق الهدي وإلا فالإفراد فافهم. والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال
By proximity at the time of hearing because it is more audible (and that is when the other narrator is far away) such that the possibility of error in hearing exists, that he hears some but not all. With this, the Shafi'is gave preponderance to Ifrad in Hajj from the narration of Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions ﷺ performed Ifrad of Hajj because he was under his she-camel, so he was closer to hear the talbiyah. And the Hanafis gave preponderance to Qiran from Anas that he was holding the camel's halter while he said: 'Labbayk bi-Hajjah wa 'Umrah'. Know that the narrations about the Farewell Hajj are conflicting: some say he performed Ifrad, some say Qiran (combining Hajj and 'Umrah with one Ihram), and some say Tamattu'. Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi said: Most narrations support Qiran, and some reconciled by saying he first entered Ihram for 'Umrah, then added Hajj, saying later 'Labbayk bi-Hajjah wa 'Umrah'. Whoever heard the first report related Tamattu', whoever heard the second without knowing he had previously entered Ihram for 'Umrah related Ifrad, and most of those who heard the final report related Qiran. The Qiran narrations are well-known, almost reaching the level of tawatur ma'nawi. Due to this disagreement, scholars differed on what is best: with us (Hanafis) it is Qiran, with al-Shafi'i Ifrad, with Malik Tamattu', and Ahmad said Qiran if he brings the sacrificial animal, otherwise Ifrad. So understand. And Allah knows the reality.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage discusses tarjih (preponderance) by proximity of the narrator to the speaker, using the example of conflicting narrations about the Farewell Hajj. The Shafi'is argued that Ibn 'Umar's narration of Ifrad is stronger because he was physically close to the Prophet (under his camel). The Hanafis countered with Anas's narration of Qiran, where Anas was holding the camel's halter. The author then presents the reconciliation by Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq al-Dihlawi, explaining that the apparent conflict arises from different stages of the same event: the Prophet first entered Ihram for 'Umrah, then added Hajj. Most narrations support Qiran, which is the Hanafi view. The passage concludes by listing the positions of the major madhhabs: Hanafi: Qiran, Shafi'i: Ifrad, Maliki: Tamattu', Hanbali: Qiran if he brings the sacrificial animal, else Ifrad.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Giving preponderance to one conflicting evidence over another based on a valid criterion
القرآن (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and 'Umrah with a single Ihram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Shafi'is consider Ibn 'Umar's narration of Ifrad stronger?
A) Because Ibn 'Umar was a senior companion
B) Because he was physically close to the Prophet under his camel, making hearing more reliable
C) Because the narration is in Sahih al-Bukhari
D) Because he narrated the exact words of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Tarjih by proximity is a valid usul method, but reconciliation of narrations often reveals the stronger position; in the Hajj dispute, Qiran is the Hanafi view.

Tarjih by Narrator Qualities and Timing
Listing tarjih factors: narrator status, timing, and explicit hearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the criteria for tarjih based on narrator status and timing, and apply them to evaluate conflicting narrations.

Core Idea
Adult Muslim narrators, explicit hearing, and post-Hijrah context strengthen a hadith's preponderance.

When two hadith narrations conflict, Hanafi usul provides criteria to weigh them. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut outlines several factors related to the narrator's state and the time of narration, including age, faith, explicitness of hearing, and the Meccan vs Medinan context. Understanding these rules sharpens your ability to resolve apparent contradictions in the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first tarjih factor: narrator being adult and Muslim.
The passage states that a narration received by an adult Muslim is more reliable than one from a child or non-Muslim due to greater care in hearing.
This applies to the moment of hearing, not the narrator's entire life.
2
Identify the second factor: timing of Islam—later convert who explicitly heard vs early convert who died before hearing.
If an early Muslim died before hearing a hadith, his narration is less reliable than a later convert who explicitly states he heard it himself.
The key is explicit statement of hearing.
3
Identify the third factor: Madani vs Makki narrations.
Most of what came after Hijrah is considered Madani and is given preference over Makki narrations, but only when it is not known that the Makki narration occurred after Hijrah.
This is a temporal priority, not a judgement on the cities themselves.
4
Analyze the fourth factor: explicit mention of hearing (samā') vs 'an'anah.
Explicit hearing is given preference because 'an'anah carries a possibility of irsal (discontinuity). However, 'an'anah from a trustworthy non-mudallis is accepted by consensus as connected for the purpose of further argumentation.
The consensus (Ijma) cited by al-Hakim is key: mu'an'an ahadith without tadlis are considered connected.
5
Analyze the fifth factor: certainty of being marfu' vs disputed marfu' status.
A hadith that is definitively marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) is preferred over one whose marfu' status is disputed. However, in matters beyond human opinion, a mawquf (stopped at Companion) is treated as marfu' because the companion could not have said it other than from the Prophet.
This exception applies to matters like the unseen or future events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) قد يكون (بالتحمل بالغاً ومسلماً) فيكون ما تحمله بالغاً مسلماً أرجح مما تحمله صبياً أو كافراً لأن اهتمام المسلم البالغ بالسماع أشد من اهتمام غيره (و) قد يكون بتأخر الإسلام وذلك إذا كان متقدم الإسلام لم يسمع بعد إسلامه بأن مات قبله. وصرح متأخر الإسلام بأنه سمع بنفسه، وهذا ظاهر جداً (كالوارد في المدينة المطهرة، فإنه مرجح على الوارد بمكة، فإن أكثره وارد بعد الهجرة والغلبة فيما ورد بمكة لما ورد قبل الهجرة، والذي ينزل بعد الهجرة يسمى مدنياً، والذي قبل الهجرة يسمى مكياً، لكن هذا الترجيح إنما يكون فيما إذا لم يعلم ورود ما في مكة بعد الهجرة (و) قد يكون بتصريح السماع والوصل على العنعنة لاحتمال الإرسال والانقطاع فيها وفيه نظر، لأن قابل المرسل لا يسلم ذلك بعد عدالة المعنعن وإمامته وكونه غير مدلس تدليس التسوية، قال الحاكم : الأحاديث المعنعنة التي ليس فيها تدليس متصلة بالإجماع، كذا في «الحاشية» مطابقاً لما قال الشيخ ابن الهمام، والظاهر أن قبول المرسل لا دخل له في الإيراد، فإن اتصال العنعنة من غير المدلس إجماعاً يكفي في الإيراد، وأما إذا بقي احتمال الإرسال وإن كان هو لا يرسل إلا ثقة فالمصرح بالسماع أرجح البتة لأن المسند مقدم على المرسل، فكذا قطعي الإسناد على ما يحتمل الإرسال فافهم. وبالاتفاق على رفعه فيرجح مقطوع الرفع على ما اختلف في رفعه إلا ما ليس للرأي فيه مجال فإن الوقف هناك كالرفع لتعين جهة السماع هناك
(And) it may be (by the narrator being an adult and Muslim): so what an adult Muslim narrates is more preponderant than what a child or non-Muslim narrates, because the adult Muslim's care in hearing is stronger than others. (And) it may be by being later in Islam: that is, if one who accepted Islam early did not hear after his Islam because he died before him, but one who accepted Islam later explicitly states that he heard himself. This is very clear. (Like the narration occurring in Medina the purified, it is preponderant over that occurring in Mecca, because most of it occurred after the Hijrah, and most of what occurred in Mecca is before the Hijrah. What was revealed after the Hijrah is called Madani, and before Hijrah Makki. But this preponderance applies only when it is not known that the Meccan narration occurred after the Hijrah.) (And) it may be by explicit mention of hearing and connection (ittisal) over 'an'anah (the 'an' form), because of the possibility of irsal and discontinuity in 'an'anah. But there is consideration: the one who accepts mursal does not concede that after the 'adalah and imamah of the mu'an'an and his not being a mudallis of tadlis al-taswiyah. Al-Hakim said: The mu'an'an ahadith that do not contain tadlis are connected by consensus. As in al-Hashiyah, matching what Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said. It appears that accepting mursal has no bearing on the presentation, because the connection of 'an'anah from a non-mudallis is sufficient by consensus for presentation. But if the possibility of irsal remains, even though he does not narrate except from trustworthy sources, the explicit mention of hearing is absolutely more preponderant, because the musnad is preferred over the mursal, and likewise definitive isnad over what is possible to be irsal. So understand. And by agreement on its being marfu', the marfu' that is certain in its raising is preponderant over that which is disputed, except for what has no room for opinion, then the mawquf there is like marfu' because the source of hearing is certain there.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage enumerates further criteria for tarjih (preponderance) in conflicting hadith narrations. First, a narrator who was an adult Muslim at the time of hearing is preferred over a child or non-Muslim, because their attention and memory are stronger. Second, a narrator who explicitly states hearing (samā') is preferred over one who uses the ambiguous 'an expression, although 'an'anah from a trustworthy non-mudallis is accepted by consensus. Third, Madani narrations (those that took place after the Hijrah) are generally given precedence over Makki ones (before Hijrah), unless the Makki narration is known to be from after the Hijrah. Fourth, a hadith that is definitively marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) is preferred over one whose marfu' status is disputed, except in matters beyond human opinion, where a mawquf (stopped at Companion) can be treated as marfu' due to the impossibility of personal reasoning.

Key Terms
العنعنة (al-'an'anah): A narrator saying 'an (from) without specifying whether he heard directly
المدني والمكي (al-madani wa al-makki): Narrations occurring after the Hijrah (Madani) and before (Makki); Madani generally preferred in tarjih

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a Madani narration preferred over a Makki narration?
A) Always
B) When it is not known that the Makki narration occurred after the Hijrah
C) Only if the narrator is an adult Muslim
D) When the Makki narration is mawquf

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in Hanafi usul weighs narrator reliability, explicitness of hearing, and temporal context of narration.

Tarjih by Gender and by Book: Hanafi Usul
Explaining tarjih by masculinity and critique of Sahihain superiority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of tarjih by narrator's gender and by inclusion in the Sahihain, and evaluate the critique of over-reliance on Sahihain.

Core Idea
Masculinity gives tarjih except in women’s matters; being in Sahihain does not guarantee superiority over other narrations.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut discusses two important tarjih factors in Hanafi usul: the narrator's gender and the prestige of the hadith collection. While masculinity generally strengthens a narration, exceptions exist where women's knowledge is paramount. More provocatively, the author critiques the blanket superiority of Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, arguing that critical scrutiny of individual chains remains necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tarjih factors
Read the passage and list the two factors: tarjih by masculinity and tarjih by being in a famous book (Sahihain). Note that both have conditions and exceptions.
2
Understand tarjih by masculinity
State the rule: a male narrator's narration is preponderant over a female's, except in matters where women's knowledge is predominant (e.g., rulings specific to women). Analyze the eclipse prayer example: one ruku' (man's narration) preferred over multiple ruku's (woman's narration) because men observe eclipses more. However, note that the multiple ruku' hadith is also narrated by Ibn 'Abbas, weakening the tarjih.
3
Distinguish two applications of tarjih by book
The passage distinguishes between: (i) a narration attributed to a known book (like Sahihain) is preponderant over one not attributed to any book, and (ii) the false claim that narrations in Sahihain are absolutely superior to narrations by other imams. This second claim is rejected.
4
Analyze the critique of Sahihain superiority
The author argues that many narrators in Muslim are criticized, and even Bukhari has criticized narrators. Therefore, the Ummah does not accept everything in them. The Hanafi position is that tarjih must be based on individual chain scrutiny, not the book's reputation alone.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is in how a mufti decides between conflicting hadiths. The Hanafi does not automatically prefer a Sahihain hadith but examines chains and other tarjih factors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) قد يكون (بالذكورة) فيترجح مروي الذكر على مروي الأنثى لكن في غير أحكام النساء) أي أحكام يكون الغالب فيها معرفة النساء، و به رجح خبر الركوع الواحد في الصلاة الكسوف على خبر تعدده لأن راوي التعدد أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة وراوي الركوع الواحد سمرة بن جندب، كما روى الترمذي وقال: حسن صحيح، لأن هذه الحال أكشف للرجال، لكن حديث تعدد الركوع رواه ابن عباس أيضاً على ما في الصحيحين»، فلا يتم هذا النحو من الترجيح (و) يكون (بالنسبة إلى كتاب معروف بالصحة كـ «الصحيحين (الآن فإن المنسوب إليهما يترجح على ما لم ينسب إلى كتاب لا أن مرويات الصحيحين راجحة على مرويات أئمة آخرين، فإن هذا لا يساعد عليه العقل والنقل، ولا عمل من يعتد بعملهم، وأفحش من هذا ما قال ابن الصلاح وأتباعه أن مرويات الأئمة الآخرين برواتهما مرجوحة عن مروياتهما كما قال (وكون ما في الصحيحين» راجحاً على ما يروى برجالهما أو شرطهما بعد إمامة المخرج تحكم) محض (كيف لا يكون تحكماً ولم يسلم كثير من شيوخ مسلم عن غوائل الجرح) كما لم يسلم شيوخ غيره إلا أن شيوخ مسلم أكثرهم مبرؤون عن الجرح (وفي) صحيح البخاري جماعة تكلم فيهم فكيف يكون المروي عن هذه الرجال المختلف فيهم مقدماً على مروي غيره عن متفق الصحة وهل هذا إلا بهت وتلقي الأمة لجميع ما في كتابيهما ممنوع) وقد قررنا من قبل فتذكر
(And) it may be (by masculinity): the narration of a man is preponderant over that of a woman, except in matters concerning women (i.e., rulings where women's knowledge is predominant). With this, the hadith of one bowing (ruku') in the solar eclipse prayer was given preponderance over the hadith of multiple bows, because the narrator of multiple bows is Umm al-Mu'minin 'A'ishah al-Siddiqah, and the narrator of one bow is Samurah ibn Jundub, as narrated by al-Tirmidhi who said it is hasan sahih. Because this situation (solar eclipse) is more observable by men. However, the hadith of multiple bows was also narrated by Ibn 'Abbas as in the Sahihain, so this type of tarjih is not conclusive. (And) it may be (by reference to a famous book of authenticity, like the two Sahihs): now, what is attributed to them is preponderant over what is not attributed to any book, not that the narrations in the two Sahihs are preponderant over the narrations of other imams, for this is not supported by reason or transmission, nor by the practice of those whose practice is considered. Even more excessive is what Ibn al-Salah and his followers said, that the narrations of other imams via the narrators of the two Sahihs or their conditions are weaker than their narrations. And saying that what is in the two Sahihs is preponderant over what is narrated via their narrators or their conditions after the imamate of the compiler is sheer imposition. How is it not imposition when many of Muslim's shuyukh are not free from the harms of jarh, just as the shuyukh of others are not free – except that Muslim's shuyukh are mostly free from jarh. And in Sahih al-Bukhari, there is a group who have been criticized, so how can a narration from these differing men be preferred over another's narration from those of agreed-upon reliability? Is this not slander? And the Ummah's acceptance of everything in the two books is rejected. We have previously established this, so remember.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses two tarjih factors and critiques an over-reliance on the authenticity of Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim. First, tarjih by masculinity: a male narrator is preferred, except in matters where women's knowledge is predominant (e.g., issues specific to women). The example given is the solar eclipse prayer: the hadith of one ruku' (from Samurah) is preferred over the hadith of multiple ruku's (from 'Aishah) because men would be more aware of the prayer's performance. However, this tarjih is weakened because Ibn 'Abbas also narrated multiple ruku's in the Sahihain. Second, tarjih by being in a famous book like the Sahihain: merely being in these books does not automatically make a hadith superior to those narrated by other imams through their own chains. The author strongly criticizes Ibn al-Salah's view that any hadith in the Sahihain is superior to those narrated via the same narrators or conditions outside these books. He argues that many narrators in Muslim's chain have been criticized, and even Bukhari's chain includes criticized narrators. Therefore, the Ummah does not universally accept everything in the two books without scrutiny. This is a sobering reminder for students who might assume absolute superiority of Sahihain over all other collections.

Key Terms
الصحيحان (al-sahihan): Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim
الجرح والتعديل (al-jarh wa al-ta'dil): Criticism and accreditation of narrators

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi view on the tarjih of a hadith that appears in Sahih al-Bukhari or Muslim?
A) It is always superior to any other hadith
B) It is superior only if the other hadith is not in any book
C) It is not automatically superior; individual chain scrutiny is necessary
D) It is superior only if it is also in the Musnad of Ahmad

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in Hanafi usul requires individual chain scrutiny; neither narrator gender nor inclusion in the Sahihain provides automatic superiority.

Critique of Absolute Tarjih and the Maymunah Case
Refutes absolute tarjih of Sahihayn and illustrates conflicting tarjih with Maymunah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim of absolute superiority of the Sahihayn and apply tarjih criteria (dabt, fiqh, direct involvement) to resolve conflicting hadith reports.

Core Idea
The Sahihayn are not absolutely superior; tarjih depends on multiple factors including precision, fiqh, and direct knowledge.

In usul al-fiqh, tarjih (preference) between conflicting evidences is a critical skill. This passage challenges a common misconception that the Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) are always preponderant over other collections. It then illustrates the complexity of tarjih through the case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah, where two Companions gave conflicting reports, each with their own strengths. By studying this passage, you will learn to weigh conflicting factors and avoid blanket hierarchies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Locate the claim by Ibn al-Salah and his followers that narrations in the Sahihayn are absolutely preponderant over narrations from other imams. Note the author's labeling of this as 'arbitrariness' (tahakkum).
The passage uses 'Aqfahu min hadha' to emphasize the severity.
2
Analyze the refutation
The author argues that many narrators in Muslim and Bukhari are not free from criticism (jarh). Therefore, claiming absolute superiority is not supported by reason (aql) or transmission (naql).
The text mentions 'shuyukh Muslim' and 'jama'ah takallama fihim' in Bukhari.
3
Examine the Maymunah case
Two hadiths conflict: Ibn Abbas says the Prophet married Maymunah while in ihram; Abu Rafi says while halal. Each narrator has a point of preponderance: Ibn Abbas excels in dabt and fiqh; Abu Rafi was directly involved as the messenger.
Note the specific tarjih factors: dabt, fiqh, mubasharah.
4
Evaluate the conflict of tarjih
The author presents a dispute: Ibn Abbas's dabt/fiqh vs. Abu Rafi's direct involvement. He then mentions additional arguments: Ibn Abbas's report implies eyewitness of ihram, Abu Rafi's report is supported by Maymunah herself. These create a second level of conflict.
The author does not settle the matter absolutely but explores resolutions.
5
Review proposed resolutions
The author attempts to combine by metaphorical interpretation: Abu Rafi's 'married' could mean intercourse; Ibn Abbas's 'married' could mean betrothal. He notes weaknesses and prefers the metaphor of intercourse as stronger.
This shows that even when tarjih is inconclusive, jama (combination) may be attempted.

ويكون (بالنسبة إلى كتاب معروف بالصحة كـ «الصحيحين» الآن فإن المنسوب إليهما يترجح على ما لم ينسب إلى كتاب لا أن مرويات الصحيحين راجحة على مرويات أئمة آخرين، فإن هذا لا يساعد عليه العقل والنقل، ولا عمل من يعتد بعملهم، وأفحش من هذا ما قال ابن الصلاح وأتباعه أن مرويات الأئمة الآخرين برواتهما مرجوحة عن مروياتهما كما قال (وكون ما في الصحيحين» راجحاً على ما يروى برجالهما أو شرطهما بعد إمامة المخرج تحكم) محض (كيف لا يكون تحكماً ولم يسلم كثير من شيوخ مسلم عن غوائل الجرح) كما لم يسلم شيوخ غيره إلا أن شيوخ مسلم أكثرهم مبرؤون عن الجرح (وفي) صحيح البخاري جماعة تكلم فيهم فكيف يكون المروي عن هذه الرجال المختلف فيهم مقدماً على مروي غيره عن متفق الصحة وهل هذا إلا بهت وتلقي الأمة لجميع ما في كتابيهما ممنوع) وقد قررنا من قبل فتذكر وقد تتعارض في التراجيح) فيوجد في أحد المتعارضين ترجيح وفي آخر آخر کابن عباس عارض أبا رافع في نكاح) أم المؤمنين (ميمونة) فابن عباس روى أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام نكحها وهو محرم، وأبو رافع أنه نكحها وهما حلالان وابن عباس راجح على أبي رافع (ضبطاً وفقها) وأبو رافع راجح عليه (مباشرة حيث قال : كنت الرسول بينهما، فتعارضا في الرجحان أيضاً، ولا يبعد أن يقال : الترجيح بالفقاهة والضبط راجح عليه بالمباشرة ورجح ابن عباس بأن الأخبار بالإحرام لا يكون إلا عن معاينة الهيئة الإحرامية فيكون العلم به أقوى (و) رجح (أبو رافع بموافقة صاحبة الواقعة قالت : تزوجني ونحن (حلالان وصاحب الواقعة أعرف بحاله (فتعارضا) في هذا الترجيح أيضاً ( فيتخلص) بالجمع وذلك بتجوز التزوج عن الدخول في خبر أبي رافع من قبيل إطلاق السبب على المسبب (أقول : لا يخفى جواز تجوز النكاح في خبر ابن عباس (عن الخطبة فتعارضا (ثالثاً) في وجه الجمع . ولا يذهب عليك أن قوله وبنى بها وهو حلال يأبى عن إرادة الخطبة من النكاح فهو مفسر، ورواية أبي رافع نص فرواية ابن عباس راجحة من هذه الجهة (فيتخلص) عن هذا التعارض بأن مجاز الدخول أقوى علاقة فيتسارع إليه الذهن دون مجاز الخطبة تأمل فيه
And it is (with respect to a book known for authenticity like the Sahihayn (now)) that what is attributed to them is preponderant over what is not attributed to a book, not that the narrations of the Sahihayn are preponderant over the narrations of other imams, for the intellect and transmission do not support this, nor the practice of those whose practice is relied upon. More outrageous than this is what Ibn al-Salah and his followers said: that the narrations of other imams through their narrators are inferior to their narrations, as he said (And the fact that what is in the Sahihayn is preponderant over what is narrated through their men or their conditions after the imamate of the compiler is pure arbitrariness). How could it not be arbitrariness when many of Muslim's shaykhs are not safe from the evils of jarh (disparagement), just as the shaykhs of others are not safe, except that Muslim's shaykhs are mostly free from jarh. And in Sahih al-Bukhari there are a group who are criticized, so how can what is narrated from these men who are disputed be preferred over the narration of another who is agreed upon for authenticity? Is this not slander? And the ummah's acceptance of everything in the two books is denied. We have established this before, so remember. And mutations occur in tarjih (preponderance). So in one of the two conflicting reports there is a point of preponderance, and in the other another. Like Ibn Abbas opposed Abu Rafi regarding the marriage of the Mother of the Believers Maymunah. Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) married her while he was in ihram, and Abu Rafi that he married her while both were halal. Ibn Abbas is preponderant over Abu Rafi in precision (dabt) and jurisprudence (fiqh), and Abu Rafi is preponderant over him in direct involvement, since he said: I was the messenger between them. So they conflict in preponderance as well. And it is not far to say that the tarjih by jurisprudence and precision is preponderant over that by direct involvement. And Ibn Abbas's side is strengthened by the fact that reporting about ihram cannot be except from seeing the state of ihram, so the knowledge of it is stronger. And Abu Rafi's side is strengthened by agreement with the lady of the incident who said: He married me while we were halal, and the lady of the incident knows best her condition. So they conflict in this tarjih as well. The resolution is by combination, through interpreting 'married' in Abu Rafi's report as a metaphor for intercourse, as a case of applying the cause to the effect. I say: It is not hidden that the metaphorical use of marriage in Ibn Abbas's report is for betrothal. So they conflict thirdly in the manner of combination. And it does not escape you that his statement 'and he consummated with her while he was halal' prevents the intended meaning of betrothal from marriage, so it is an explicative (mufassar), and Abu Rafi's report is explicit (nass), so Ibn Abbas's report is preponderant from this aspect. The resolution of this conflict is that the metaphor of intercourse is stronger in connection, so the mind hastens to it, unlike the metaphor of betrothal. Reflect on this.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage discusses two main points. First, it refutes the claim that the Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) are unconditionally preferred over other authentic hadith collections. The author argues that this is not supported by reason or transmission, and criticizes Ibn al-Salah's view as arbitrary. He points out that many narrators in Sahih Muslim are not immune from criticism, and likewise in Sahih Bukhari, so absolute superiority cannot be claimed. Second, it provides an example of conflicting tarjih from the case of the marriage of Maymunah. Ibn Abbas reported the Prophet married her in ihram, Abu Rafi reported it was while halal. Each narrator has a point of preponderance: Ibn Abbas is better in dabt and fiqh, Abu Rafi was directly involved. The author discusses various attempts at tarjih and resolution through metaphorical interpretation. The passage concludes that the metaphor of intercourse (for marriage) is stronger than the metaphor of betrothal. This illustrates the complexity of tarjih when multiple conflicting factors exist.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjih): Preference given to one conflicting evidence over another due to a point of strength.
ضبط (dabt): Precision and accuracy in narration; a quality that makes a narrator more reliable.
فقاهة (fiqh): Juridic understanding and knowledge; another quality of a narrator relevant to tarjih.
مباشرة (mubasharah): Direct involvement or eyewitness; a tarjih factor that gives the narrator's report additional weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute over the marriage of Maymunah, which aspect made Ibn Abbas preponderant over Abu Rafi?
A) He was a direct witness
B) He was superior in precision and fiqh
C) He was older
D) He narrated from the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Sahihayn are not absolutely superior; tarjih requires evaluating specific narrators and their qualities, not just the collection's fame.

Does Multiplicity of Narrators Strengthen Weak Hadiths? The Hanafi Position
Debate on multiplicity strengthening weak hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the principle of taqawwi bi-kathrat al-ruwat and distinguish the nature of certainty in ijma versus tawatur.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of weak narrators does not strengthen a hadith; only tawatur yields certainty by accumulation.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: can multiple weak narrations combine to produce a strong hadith? Some scholars analogize this to ijma, where multiple ijtihads yield certainty. The Hanafi school disagrees, drawing a critical distinction between the nature of certainty in ijma (devotional, instantaneous) and in tawatur (gradual accumulation). We will explore the arguments and understand why the Hanafi position remains cautious about relying on multiplicity in hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Contested Issue
Identify the core question: Does having many narrators, each individually weak, strengthen a weak hadith to a degree that it becomes acceptable as proof?
This is the principle of al-taqawwi bi-kathrat al-ruwat.
2
Identify the Opposing Argument (Qiyas with Ijma)
The opponent argues that just as multiple ijtihads accumulate to produce certainty through ijma, multiple weak narrations should similarly accumulate to strengthen a hadith. Understand the analogy they draw.
The analogy: multiplicity of ijtihads → certainty via ijma; multiplicity of narrators → strength via accumulation.
3
Follow the Hanafi Response and Distinction
The Hanafi author refutes the analogy by distinguishing the nature of certainty. Certainty from ijma is ta'abbudi (devotional) and occurs instantly, not through gradual accumulation. In contrast, certainty from tawatur does result from gradual accumulation of opinion, but this does not apply to weak hadiths that have not reached tawatur.
The key point: ijma's certainty is immediate, not constructed from gradual strengthening.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence
Recognize that in Hanafi usul, a weak hadith remains weak even if it has multiple chains; multiplicity does not elevate it to hasan or sahih. This affects which hadiths are accepted as proof in legal reasoning.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a weak hadith with many chains is still considered weak and not used as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أكثر وقد رجح أمير المؤمنين عمر وغيره من الصحابة خبر أم المؤمنين وحدها، فلم يعتبروا التقوّي بكثرة الرواة، ولعل هذه القوة ضعيفة مراتبها متفاوتة ففي اعتبارها نوع من العسر والله يريد اليسر (أقول منقوض هذا بكثرة الاجتهاد، فإن عدم الترجيح بها اتفاق بيننا وبينكم (مع أنه ينتهي إلى اليقين بالاجماع كما أنه تنتهي كثرة الرواة بالتواتر إلى القطع (فتدبر) وجوابه أن القطع الحاصل بالاجماع تعبدي يحصل دفعة لا بأن يتدرج الظن الحاصل باجتهاد إلى أن يتقوّى بانضمام آخر حتى ينتهي بالإجماع إلى اليقين بخلاف الرواة، فإن الظن فيه يتقوى بالانضمام وينتهي بالتواتر إلى اليقين فافهم.
More often, the Commander of the Faithful Umar and other Companions preferred the report of the Mother of the Believers (Aisha) alone, and they did not consider strengthening by the multiplicity of narrators. Perhaps this strength is weak, its ranks varying, so considering it involves some difficulty, while God desires ease. (I say: This is refuted by the multiplicity of ijtihad, for the lack of preference by multiplicity is agreed upon between us and you, even though it leads to certainty through ijma just as the multiplicity of narrators through tawatur leads to certainty. So reflect.) The answer is that the certainty obtained by ijma is devotional, attained at once, not that the opinion obtained by ijtihad gradually strengthens by the addition of another until it reaches certainty through ijma, unlike the narrators, for the opinion therein strengthens by addition and reaches certainty through tawatur. So understand.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute about the evidential value of multiplicity in hadith. The opponent argues that just as multiple ijtihads can accumulate to produce certainty through ijma, so multiple weak hadiths can combine to produce strength. The author refutes this by distinguishing the nature of certainty: ijma gives certainty devotionally and instantaneously, not by gradual accumulation of opinion. In contrast, the multiplicity of narrators in tawatur does produce certainty by accumulation. Therefore, the analogy fails. The passage also notes that Umar and other Companions did not consider multiplicity as a factor when preferring a single report, indicating that the principle of strengthening by multiplicity is weak and not relied upon.

Key Terms
التقوّي بكثرة الرواة (al-taqawwī bi-kathrat al-ruwāt): Strengthening a hadith by having multiple narrators, each weak, but collectively may add strength.
متواتر (mutawātir): A hadith narrated by so many at each level that it gives certainty.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah after the Prophet's death on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi author reject the analogy between multiplicity of narrators and ijma?
A) Because ijma is based on consensus, not narrators
B) Because the certainty from ijma is devotional and instantaneous, not gradually accumulated
C) Because ijma is stronger than tawatur
D) Because multiplicity of narrators is impossible

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, multiplicity of weak narrators does not strengthen a weak hadith; only tawatur provides certainty by accumulation.
