Second Proof for Ijma: Hadith and Its Tawatur Ma'nawi
Establishing the authority of ijma via hadith and its tawatur ma'nawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that the hadiths on community infallibility are mutawatir ma'nawi and evaluate Imam al-Razi's objections.

Core Idea
Mutawatir ma'nawi hadiths prove ijma is qat'i: the umma is infallible from error.

The authority of ijma rests on textual proof. The second major proof is a set of hadiths that all convey the same meaning: the Muslim community will never unite on error. In this passage, the author argues that these hadiths are mutawatir ma'nawi, yielding certain knowledge. However, Imam al-Razi objects, denying the tawatur. We will follow the Hanafi response and understand why ijma is considered a definitive source in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim
The Hanafi claim is that the hadiths about community infallibility are mutawatir ma'nawi, meaning they collectively provide certain knowledge that the community is protected from error, thereby proving the authority of ijma.
The claim is that ijma is a qat'i source of law.
2
Examine the evidence cited
The author lists several variant hadith wordings, such as 'لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلالة', 'ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن', and others. These all convey the common meaning of infallibility.
The number of narrators for each wording reaches tawatur numerically.
3
Analyze Imam al-Razi's objections
Al-Razi objects on two grounds: (1) Twenty or even a thousand narrators could collude to lie, so tawatur is not achieved; (2) Even if tawatur is conceded, the common element is not 'ijma is authoritative' but something else, so the argument fails.
Al-Razi's doubts are representative of the mutakallimun approach.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes both objections: collusion of so many narrators is impossible; the common meaning is clearly infallibility; tawatur is analogous to historical events like Badr; opposition does not negate tawatur; and the questions about specific texts do not affect the certain common element.
The author warns that this is a slippery point – do not let doubts slip in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل ثانياً : بقوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم : «لا تجتمع أمتي على الضلالة) فإنه يفيد عصمة عن الخطأ فإنه متواتر (المعنى فإنه قد ورد بألفاظ مختلفة يفيد كلها العصمة، وبلغت رواة تلك الألفاظ حد التواتر وتلك الألفاظ نحو: ما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن» ونحو من فارق الجماعة شبراً فقد خلع ربقة الإسلام ونحو : عليكم بالجماعة» ونحو: «الزموا الجماعة ونحو من فارق الجماعة مات ميتة الجاهلية ونحو: «عليكم بالسواد الأعظم ونحو: «لا تجتمع أمتي على الخطأ» وغير ذلك من الألفاظ التي يطول الكلام بذكرها واستحسنه ابن الحاجب) فإنه دليل لا خفاء فيه بوجه ولا مساغ للارتياب فيه واستبعد الإمام الرازي) صاحب المحصول كما هو دأبه من التشكيكات في الأمور الظاهرة (التواتر المعنوي سيما على حجيته) وقال لا نسلم بلوغ مجموع هذه الآحاد حد التواتر المعنوي فإن الرواة العشرين أو الألف لا تبلغ حد التواتر ولا تكفي للتواتر المعنوي، فإنه ليس بمستبعد في العرف إقدام عشرين على الكذب في واقعة معينة بعبارات مختلفة، ولو سلم فتواتره بالمعنى غير مسلم فإن القدر المشترك هو أن الإجماع حجة أو ما يلزم هو منه، فقد ادعيتم أن حجية الإجماع متواترة من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ويلزم أن يكون كغزوة بدر، وهو باطل فإنه لو كان كذلك لم يقع الخلاف فيه، وإنكم بعد تصحيح المتن توردون على دلالته على حجية الإجماع الأسئلة والأجوبة، ولو كان متواتراً لأفاد العلم ولغت تلك الأسئلة والأجوبة وإن ادعيتم أن هذه الأخبار تدل على عصمة الأمة وهي بعينها حجية الإجماع وقرر هذه بعبارات مطنبة كما هو دأبه وهذا الاستبعاد في بعد بعيد كبرت كلمة خرجت من فيه. فإن القدر المشترك المفهوم من هذه الأخبار قطعاً عصمة الأمة هو عن الخطأ، ولا شك فيه واجتماع عشرين من العدول الخيار بل أزيد على الكذب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم مما لا يتوهم وأما قوله : لو كان لكان كغزوة بدر قلنا نعم إنه كغزوة بدر كيف وقد عرفت سابقاً أنه تواتر في كل عصر من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم إلى هذا الآن تخطئة المخالف للإجماع قطعاً، وهل هذا إلا تواتر الحجية، وأيضاً يجوز أن يكون المتوترات مختلفة بحسب قوم دون قوم فهذا متواتر عند كل من طالع كثرة الوقائع والأخبار، وما قال إنه لو كان متواتراً لما وقع الخلاف فيه، قلنا: التواتر لا يوجب أن يكون الكل عالمين به ألا ترى أن أكثر العوام لا يعلمون غزوة بدر أصلاً بل المتواتر إنما يكون متواتراً عند من وصل إليه أخبار تلك الجماعة، وذلك بمطالعة الوقائع والأخبار والمخالفون لم يطالعوا وأيضاً : الحق أن مخالفتهم كمخالفة السوفسطائية في القضايا الضرورية الأولية، فكما أن مخالفتهم لا تضر كونها أولية فكذا مخالفة المخالفين لا تضر التواتر، وأما ايراد الأسئلة والأجوبة فعلى بعض المتون لا على القدر المشترك المستفاد من الأخبار فافهم ولا تزل فإنه مزلة
He [the author] adduced secondly: the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'My community will not unite upon error' – for it indicates infallibility from error, and it is mutawatir in meaning, as it has been narrated in various wordings all indicating infallibility, and the narrators of those wordings have reached the level of tawatur. Among those wordings: 'What the Muslims see as good is good with Allah', 'Whoever separates from the community by a handspan has cast off the rope of Islam', 'Hold fast to the community', 'Keep to the community', 'Whoever separates from the community dies a death of ignorance', 'Hold fast to the great majority', 'My community will not unite upon error', and other wordings too numerous to mention. Ibn al-Hajib accepted it. It is a proof with no hidden aspect and no room for doubt. Imam al-Razi, author of al-Mahsul, doubted the tawatur ma'nawi, especially regarding its authority, as is his habit of casting doubts on evident matters. He said: We do not accept that the sum of these ahad reports has reached the level of tawatur ma'nawi, for twenty narrators or even a thousand do not reach the level of tawatur and are not sufficient for tawatur ma'nawi, because it is not improbable in custom for twenty to conspire to lie about a specific incident with different expressions. Even if it is conceded, its tawatur in meaning is not accepted, for the common element is that ijma is authoritative or something derived from it. You claim that the authority of ijma is mutawatir from the Messenger of Allah, and it would then be like the battle of Badr, which is false, because if that were so, there would be no disagreement about it. And you, after correcting the text, raise questions and answers about its indication of the authority of ijma. If it were mutawatir, it would yield knowledge and those questions and answers would be futile. If you claim that these reports indicate the infallibility of the community, which is exactly the authority of ijma, and you elaborate this in lengthy phrases as is your habit, this improbability is far-fetched. 'Great is the word that comes out of their mouths!' The common element understood from these reports with certainty is the infallibility of the community from error, and there is no doubt about it. The gathering of twenty just and excellent narrators, or more, to lie about the Messenger of Allah is unimaginable. As for his saying: 'If it were so, it would be like the battle of Badr', we say: Yes, it is like the battle of Badr. How? You have learned earlier that it is mutawatir in every age from the time of the Messenger of Allah until now to declare the opponent of ijma as wrong with certainty. Is this not tawatur of authority? Also, it is possible that mutawatir reports differ with respect to some people and not others. This is mutawatir for whoever has studied the abundance of events and reports. His statement that if it were mutawatir, there would be no disagreement, we say: Tawatur does not require that everyone knows it; do you not see that most common people do not even know the battle of Badr? Rather, tawatur is only tawatur for those to whom the reports of that group have reached through studying events and reports, and the opponents have not studied. Also, the truth is that their opposition is like the opposition of sophists to primary necessary propositions; just as their opposition does not harm their primariness, so too the opposition of opponents does not harm tawatur. As for raising questions and answers, that concerns some specific texts, not the common element derived from the reports. Understand and do not slip, for it is a slippery place.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for the authority of ijma: the hadith 'My community will not unite upon error' and similar narrations. The author argues that these hadiths are mutawatir ma'nawi (tawatur in meaning) because they all share the common meaning of the community's infallibility. Ibn al-Hajib endorsed this argument. However, Imam al-Razi objected, denying that the sum of these ahad reports reaches tawatur; he argued that twenty narrators could collude to lie, and even if accepted, the common element is not precisely 'authority of ijma' but something derived from it. The author responds vigorously: the common element is clearly the infallibility of the umma from error, and it is unimaginable that so many narrators would lie. He compares the situation to the battle of Badr, which is known by tawatur. The fact that some oppose ijma does not negate tawatur, just as the opposition of sophists does not negate primary knowledge. The tawatur is for those who have studied the reports; opponents simply lack that study. The questions and answers about specific texts do not affect the certain common element. The author warns the reader not to slip into doubt about this clear proof.

Key Terms
التواتر المعنوي (al-tawatur al-ma'nawi): Tawatur in meaning: multiple ahad hadiths with differing wordings all conveying the same meaning, yielding certainty about that meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the common meaning (قدر مشترك) derived from the various hadiths supporting ijma according to the Hanafi argument?
A) That ijma is a source of law alongside Quran
B) That the community is infallible from error
C) That following the majority is obligatory
D) That the Prophet forbade separation

Key Takeaway
The hadiths on community infallibility are mutawatir ma'nawi, establishing ijma as a certain, qat'i source of law in Hanafi usul.
